*Section 5 of Paper 3 (Unified Quantum Force Completion). Upgrade tier: model-definition (Paper 2 §6.3) → auditable object. Carrier-neutral: no specific graviton / gauge / Higgs / fermion certificate is closed in this section. Carriers are written separately in §§8–11.*

---

## 5.0 Purpose and tier statement

Paper 2 §6.3 records a single quantum-gravity package — a background-split BV-BRST master action, a 13D de Donder gauge, an ADM canonical algebra, and a BRST-cohomological physical state space — but labels every entry "model-definition only; not required for the four-force interface trunk." That label is appropriate to Paper 2's interface scope; it is *not* sufficient for Paper 3, whose central question is whether the four interface projections can be *quantized* compatibly and *audited* against a single, internally consistent quantization ledger.

This section therefore promotes the §6.3 package from "model-definition" to "auditable object" by writing it in three textbook formulations *in parallel*, certifying their pairwise equivalence on the overlap where both are well-defined (UQF-2 of the gate stack), and listing the Kaluza-Klein mode expansion that the §6.4 line referenced but did not unfold.

The tier discipline below is binding for the rest of Paper 3:

- **CERTIFICATE.** The canonical Hamiltonian formulation, the classical BV-BRST formalism, the gauge-fixed Faddeev-Popov path integral, the equivalence of the three on free / linearised / weakly-coupled overlap, and the harmonic mode expansion on $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ are textbook quantum field theory in 4D, generalised here to 13D. The textbook character of the construction is what makes the tier *certificate*: the methods are well-established (Weinberg *Quantum Theory of Fields* Vol. II §§15-17; Peskin-Schroeder Chs. 9, 16; Henneaux-Teitelboim *Quantization of Gauge Systems*; Schwartz Chs. 14, 25).
- **AUDIT-with-roadmap.** The 13D-specific subtleties — positive Hilbert space of the *interacting* compactified theory (carried into §6), full anomaly closure including boundary contributions (carried into §7), nonperturbative renormalizability via asymptotic safety (carried into §§14-15) — sit here only as flagged dependencies that this section *names but does not close*. The named research roadmap is inherited from UQC-1 (asymptotic safety) and from the existing project literature on Dai-Freed / Freed-Hopkins boundary anomalies.

Nothing in this section closes UQF-3 (positivity), UQF-4 (BRST nilpotency + anomaly closure), UQF-5..UQF-8 (carrier certificates), or any other downstream gate. This section supplies the *common ground* on which §§6-11 perform those closures.

The §6.3 model-definition package, the §6.4 KK quantization note, the §6.5 nonperturbative RG target rule, the §6.6 list of what gravity defines, the §6.7 list of gravity-sector open controls, and the §6.9.7 optional BRST physical-space formula are all *imported* by reference rather than re-derived. Where the present section uses more compact notation than §6.3 (e.g., generic gauge index $a$ instead of a separately spelled diffeomorphism / gauge / EW index), the substitution is declared in §5.1 and is binding for the rest of Paper 3.

---

## 5.1 Field content and index conventions

Let $M_{13} = M_{3,1} \times K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ be the active 13D compactification (Paper 2 §3.1, Paper 1 active branch). Capital Latin indices $M, N \in \{0,\dots,12\}$ run over $M_{13}$; lowercase Greek indices $\mu, \nu \in \{0,1,2,3\}$ run over $M_{3,1}$; capital Latin indices $A, B \in \{4,\dots,12\}$ run over the internal nine-manifold $X = K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$. Coordinates split as $X^M = (x^\mu, y^A)$.

The collected field content of Paper 3 is

$$
\Phi^{\rm tot} \;=\; \big\{\,G_{MN}\,,\,\, A_M^a\,,\,\, \Psi\,,\,\bar\Psi\,,\,\, H\,,\,\, c^\alpha\,,\,\bar c^\alpha\,,\, b^\alpha\,\big\}
$$

with the BV antifields $\Phi^{\rm tot,*}$ for each entry. Index assignments:

- **$G_{MN}(X)$** — symmetric 13D metric. After background-splitting $G_{MN} = \bar G_{MN} + \kappa_{13} h_{MN}$ (Paper 2 §6.3, "Background split") the fluctuation $h_{MN}$ is the dynamical metric field. Block decomposition: $h_{\mu\nu}$ (graviton block), $h_{\mu A}$ (mixed block — descends to gauge bosons per Paper 2 §6.9.2), $h_{AB}$ (internal block — descends to moduli).
- **$A_M^a(X)$** — 13D gauge connection. Internal gauge index $a$ runs over the Lie algebra of the *high-dimensional* gauge group whose 4D zero-mode descendant is $SU(3)_c \times SU(2)_L \times U(1)_Y$ per Paper 2 §§7-9. The connection decomposes as $A_M = (A_\mu, A_A)$; the internal components $A_A$ play the role of scalar / Wilson-line zero modes.
- **$\Psi(X), \bar\Psi(X)$** — 13D Dirac spinor multiplet whose 4D zero-mode reduction supplies the chiral SM matter content of Paper 2 §§7.4, 8.4. In 13D one Dirac spinor has $2^{6} = 64$ complex components; the active $S^1/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary parity selects one chirality per surviving zero mode (Paper 2 §8.11.3 + the no-mirror lift). Conventions: left-handed Weyl projection $P_L = \tfrac12(1 - \Gamma^{14})$ where $\Gamma^{14}$ is the 13D chirality matrix.
- **$H(X)$** — scalar / Wilson-line carrier whose 4D zero mode is the SM Higgs doublet $(\mathbf 1, \mathbf 2)_{1/2}$ per Paper 2 §8.5a. Whether $H$ is a primitive field or is identified with an internal component of $A_M$ along $S^1/\mathbb Z_2$ (Wilson-line route) is a *carrier choice* in §10 of Paper 3; this section is neutral and writes $H$ as a separate symbol.
- **Ghosts $c^\alpha$, antighosts $\bar c^\alpha$, Nakanishi-Lautrup auxiliaries $b^\alpha$** — Grassmann-odd (for $c, \bar c$) and Grassmann-even (for $b$) ghost fields, indexed by a *combined* gauge-redundancy index $\alpha$ which runs over the union of diffeomorphism generators (one per spacetime direction, 13 components) and gauge generators (one per Lie-algebra generator $a$). Where the distinction matters, $c^M$ denotes a diffeomorphism ghost and $c^a$ a gauge ghost; outside §5.4 and §6 the combined symbol $c^\alpha$ is used.
- **BV antifields $\Phi^{*}$** — one Grassmann-conjugate partner for each entry of $\Phi^{\rm tot}$: $G^{*MN}$ (Grassmann-odd), $A^{*Ma}$ (Grassmann-odd), $\Psi^*, \bar\Psi^*$ (Grassmann-even), $H^*$ (Grassmann-odd), $c^*_\alpha$ (Grassmann-even), $\bar c^*_\alpha$ (Grassmann-even), $b^*_\alpha$ (Grassmann-odd). Ghost numbers: $\mathrm{gh}(c) = +1$, $\mathrm{gh}(\bar c) = -1$, $\mathrm{gh}(b) = 0$, $\mathrm{gh}(\Phi^*) = -\mathrm{gh}(\Phi) - 1$. These ghost-number assignments are textbook (Henneaux-Teitelboim Ch. 17; Weinberg Vol. II §15.9).

The combined symbol $\Phi^A$ (with $A$ now a *DeWitt-condensed* superindex that bundles spacetime point, internal index, and field-species label) is used in the BV master action of §5.3.

---

## 5.2 Canonical formulation

This subsection writes the canonical Hamiltonian formulation of Paper 3's full field content. The construction generalises Paper 2 §6.3 "Canonical algebra" (which gave the metric block only) to the full multiplet.

### 5.2.1 ADM split

Choose a $12+1$ ADM foliation $M_{13} = \mathbb R \times \Sigma_{12}$ with timelike unit normal $n^M$ to the spatial slice $\Sigma_{12}$. Spatial indices $I, J \in \{1,\dots,12\}$. The 13D metric decomposes as

$$
G_{MN}\,dX^M dX^N \;=\; -N^2\,dt^2 + \gamma_{IJ}\,(dX^I + N^I dt)(dX^J + N^J dt),
$$

with lapse $N$, shift $N^I$, and spatial metric $\gamma_{IJ}$. The lapse and shift are *Lagrange multipliers* for the Hamiltonian and momentum constraints respectively; they are not propagating degrees of freedom.

### 5.2.2 Phase space

The dynamical phase space $\Gamma$ for Paper 3 is

$$
\Gamma \;=\; \big\{\,(\gamma_{IJ}, \Pi^{IJ})\,,\;\, (A_I^a, E^{Ia})\,,\;\, (\Psi, \Psi^\dagger)\,,\;\, (H, \Pi_H)\,\big\}
$$

restricted to the constraint surface defined in §5.2.4 below, and modulo the gauge orbits generated by the first-class constraints.

### 5.2.3 Canonical momenta

The canonical momenta conjugate to the configuration variables are:

- **Metric.** $\Pi^{IJ} = \dfrac{\partial \mathcal L_{\rm grav}}{\partial \dot\gamma_{IJ}}$. For the 13D Einstein-Hilbert Lagrangian, $\Pi^{IJ} = \tfrac{\sqrt\gamma}{16\pi G_{13}}(K^{IJ} - K\gamma^{IJ})$ where $K_{IJ}$ is the extrinsic curvature of $\Sigma_{12}$ and $K = \gamma^{IJ}K_{IJ}$ its trace; $G_{13}$ is the 13D Newton constant. This is the standard ADM canonical momentum lifted from 4D to 13D (Wald *General Relativity* Appendix E; Henneaux-Teitelboim §4.2).
- **Gauge.** $E^{Ia} = \dfrac{\partial \mathcal L_{\rm gauge}}{\partial \dot A_I^a} = \sqrt\gamma\, F^{0Ia}/g^2$ (Yang-Mills electric field, with $g$ the relevant high-dimensional gauge coupling). $A_0^a$ is a Lagrange multiplier for the Gauss constraint and has no conjugate momentum.
- **Matter (Dirac).** $\Pi_\Psi = i\Psi^\dagger$, $\Pi_{\bar\Psi} = 0$. The vanishing antichiral momentum is the textbook source of the *primary second-class constraint* of Dirac fermions (Henneaux-Teitelboim §3.3; Weinberg Vol. I §7.5).
- **Higgs / scalar.** $\Pi_H = \dfrac{\partial \mathcal L_H}{\partial \dot H}$.

The equal-time canonical brackets are

$$
\begin{aligned}
\big[\hat\gamma_{IJ}(t,X),\hat\Pi^{KL}(t,X')\big]
&= i\hbar\,\delta_{(I}^K\delta_{J)}^L\,\delta^{(12)}(X-X'),\\[4pt]
\big[\hat A_I^a(t,X),\hat E^{Jb}(t,X')\big]
&= i\hbar\,\delta_I^J\,\delta^{ab}\,\delta^{(12)}(X-X'),\\[4pt]
\big\{\hat\Psi(t,X),\hat\Psi^\dagger(t,X')\big\}
&= \hbar\,\delta^{(12)}(X-X'),\\[4pt]
\big[\hat H(t,X),\hat\Pi_H(t,X')\big]
&= i\hbar\,\delta^{(12)}(X-X').
\end{aligned}
$$

The metric line generalises Paper 2 §6.3 "Canonical algebra" (which gave the same line with index range restricted to $\Sigma_{12}$). The remaining three lines are textbook canonical (anti-)commutators lifted from 4D to 13D without modification.

### 5.2.4 Constraint algebra

The phase space $\Gamma$ has both first-class and second-class constraints. The first-class set generates gauge redundancies; the second-class set is solved (or imposed via Dirac brackets) before quantization.

**First-class constraints** (one per gauge generator $\alpha$):

- **Hamiltonian constraint** $\mathcal H(X) \approx 0$, generating time reparametrisations.
- **Momentum (diffeomorphism) constraints** $\mathcal H_I(X) \approx 0$, $I = 1,\dots,12$, generating spatial diffeomorphisms.
- **Gauss-law constraints** $\mathcal G^a(X) \approx 0$, one per Lie-algebra generator $a$ of the high-dimensional gauge group, generating $A_M^a$-gauge transformations.

The closing brackets of the first-class set are the standard *hypersurface deformation algebra* augmented by the internal Gauss algebra:

$$
\begin{aligned}
\{\mathcal H(X), \mathcal H(X')\}
&= \gamma^{IJ}(X)\mathcal H_J(X)\partial_I\delta(X-X') - (X \leftrightarrow X'),\\[2pt]
\{\mathcal H(X), \mathcal H_I(X')\}
&= \mathcal H(X')\partial_I\delta(X-X'),\\[2pt]
\{\mathcal H_I(X), \mathcal H_J(X')\}
&= \mathcal H_I(X')\partial_J\delta(X-X') + \mathcal H_J(X)\partial_I\delta(X-X'),\\[2pt]
\{\mathcal G^a(X), \mathcal G^b(X')\}
&= f^{ab}{}_c\,\mathcal G^c(X)\,\delta(X-X'),\\[2pt]
\{\mathcal H_I(X), \mathcal G^a(X')\}
&= \mathcal G^a(X')\partial_I\delta(X-X').
\end{aligned}
$$

The first three lines are the Dirac-DeWitt hypersurface deformation algebra (Wald Appendix E.2); the fourth is the internal Yang-Mills algebra; the fifth records that spatial diffeomorphisms transport gauge generators correctly. The closure of this bracket algebra is what makes the constraints first-class.

**Second-class constraints** sit in the matter sector: the Dirac primary constraint $\Pi_{\bar\Psi} = 0$ pairs with the chirality projection to give a second-class pair, solved by the standard Dirac-bracket prescription (Henneaux-Teitelboim §3.3.2). The result is that the matter sector's effective phase space is $(\Psi, i\Psi^\dagger)$ with the Poisson bracket replaced by the Dirac bracket in mixed first-/second-class brackets; this reproduces the textbook canonical anticommutator above.

### 5.2.5 Symplectic form

The canonical symplectic form on $\Gamma$ is

$$
\Omega \;=\; \int_{\Sigma_{12}} d^{12}X\,\Big[\,
\delta \Pi^{IJ} \wedge \delta \gamma_{IJ}
+ \delta E^{Ia} \wedge \delta A_I^a
+ i\delta \Psi^\dagger \wedge \delta \Psi
+ \delta \Pi_H \wedge \delta H
\,\Big],
$$

and is closed, $d\Omega = 0$, on the constraint surface. The first-class constraints are precisely the generators of the symplectic null directions; the physical phase space is the symplectic quotient by those directions.

---

## 5.3 BV-BRST formulation

This subsection writes the classical Batalin-Vilkovisky master action and the BRST operator. The construction generalises Paper 2 §6.3 "BV-BRST master action" (metric only) to the full Paper 3 multiplet.

### 5.3.1 Classical master action

For the combined multiplet $\Phi^A = \{h_{MN}, A_M^a, \Psi, \bar\Psi, H, c^\alpha, \bar c^\alpha, b^\alpha\}$ and antifields $\Phi^*_A$, the classical BV master action is

$$
S_{\rm BV}[\Phi, \Phi^*; \bar G]
\;=\;
S_{\rm cl}[\bar G + \kappa_{13} h, A, \Psi, \bar\Psi, H]
\;+\;
\int d^{13}X\,\,\Phi^*_A\,(s\Phi^A),
$$

where $s$ is the classical BRST differential. Explicit action of $s$ on each field:

$$
\begin{aligned}
s h_{MN} &= \nabla_{(M} c_{N)} \;+\; \kappa_{13}\,(c^P \partial_P h_{MN} + h_{PN}\partial_M c^P + h_{MP}\partial_N c^P),\\[2pt]
s A_M^a &= \partial_M c^a + f^{abc}A_M^b c^c \;+\; c^M \partial_M A_M^a,\\[2pt]
s \Psi &= -i c^a T^a \Psi \;+\; c^M \partial_M \Psi,\\[2pt]
s H &= -i c^a t^a H \;+\; c^M \partial_M H,\\[2pt]
s c^a &= -\tfrac12 f^{abc} c^b c^c \;+\; c^M\partial_M c^a,\\[2pt]
s c^M &= c^P \partial_P c^M,\\[2pt]
s \bar c^\alpha &= b^\alpha,\\[2pt]
s b^\alpha &= 0.
\end{aligned}
$$

Here $T^a$ are the matter representations of the gauge generators, $t^a$ those of the Higgs, and $c^M$ are the diffeomorphism ghosts (which act on every field through Lie derivatives along $c^M\partial_M$). Nilpotency $s^2 = 0$ holds at the classical level on each line (verified by direct computation; e.g., the gauge line is the standard $(0,1)$-Maurer-Cartan structure of Yang-Mills BRST, and the diffeomorphism line is the Lie algebra of vector fields under bracket).

The master equation is

$$
\boxed{\,(S_{\rm BV}, S_{\rm BV}) \;=\; 0\,}
$$

with the BV antibracket

$$
(A, B) \;=\; \frac{\delta^R A}{\delta \Phi^A}\frac{\delta^L B}{\delta \Phi^*_A} - \frac{\delta^R A}{\delta \Phi^*_A}\frac{\delta^L B}{\delta \Phi^A}.
$$

The classical master equation holds for the action above by inspection (Henneaux-Teitelboim §17; Weinberg Vol. II §15.9). The *quantum* master equation $\tfrac12(W,W) = i\hbar \Delta W$ is the audit object of §7 of Paper 3 and is not asserted here.

### 5.3.2 Gauge-fixing fermion

A BRST gauge fixing is implemented by a fermionic functional $\Psi_{\rm gf}[\Phi]$ of ghost number $-1$; the gauge-fixed action is obtained by setting $\Phi^*_A = \delta \Psi_{\rm gf}/\delta \Phi^A$ in $S_{\rm BV}$. For Paper 3 the gauge-fixing fermion is

$$
\Psi_{\rm gf}
\;=\;
\int d^{13}X\,\Big[\,
\bar c^M\Big(F_M[\bar G, h] - \tfrac{\xi_g}{2}b_M\Big)
\;+\;
\bar c^a\Big(F^a[A] - \tfrac{\xi_a}{2}b^a\Big)
\,\Big],
$$

with the 13D de Donder gauge fixing function for gravity,

$$
F_M[\bar G, h] \;=\; \bar\nabla^N h_{MN} - \tfrac12 \bar\nabla_M h, \qquad h = \bar G^{MN}h_{MN},
$$

(Paper 2 §6.3 "Gauge fixing", line by line) and a generic linear gauge for the Yang-Mills sector, e.g.\ Lorenz gauge

$$
F^a[A] \;=\; \nabla^M A_M^a.
$$

The parameters $\xi_g, \xi_a$ are gauge-fixing parameters of the corresponding sector. The resulting gauge-fixed action contains the standard Faddeev-Popov ghost terms and the auxiliary $b$-field terms that integrate out to produce the gauge-fixing delta-functions.

### 5.3.3 BRST charge

The Noether charge associated with the BRST symmetry of the gauge-fixed action is, at the canonical level,

$$
Q_{\rm BRST}
\;=\;
\int_{\Sigma_{12}} d^{12}X\,\Big[\,c^\alpha \mathcal G_\alpha + \tfrac12 f^{\alpha}{}_{\beta\gamma}\,c^\beta c^\gamma\, \mathcal P_\alpha\,\Big],
$$

where $\mathcal G_\alpha$ is the unified first-class constraint (Hamiltonian, momentum, or Gauss, depending on the index $\alpha$), $\mathcal P_\alpha$ is the conjugate ghost momentum, and $f^\alpha{}_{\beta\gamma}$ is the structure constant of the unified constraint algebra of §5.2.4. Classical nilpotency $\{Q_{\rm BRST}, Q_{\rm BRST}\} = 0$ follows from the Jacobi identity for the constraint algebra; this is the standard Henneaux-Teitelboim construction (§§17.2-17.4). The fully quantum nilpotency $Q_{\rm BRST}^2 = 0$ is the audit object of §6 of Paper 3.

---

## 5.4 Path-integral formulation

This subsection writes the gauge-fixed path-integral measure. It records the BV master action with the antifields fixed by the gauge-fermion, then states the measure's BRST invariance and the Slavnov–Taylor identities that make it the path-integral counterpart of the canonical and BV–BRST constructions of §§5.1–5.3.

### 5.4.1 Gauge-fixed measure

Schematically,

$$
Z \;=\; \int \mathcal D\Phi^{\rm tot}\,\exp\!\Big(\tfrac{i}{\hbar} S_{\rm BV}\big[\Phi, \Phi^* = \delta\Psi_{\rm gf}/\delta \Phi\big]\Big),
$$

where $\mathcal D\Phi^{\rm tot}$ is the formal product measure over all field species. After integrating out the auxiliary $b$-field (Gaussian integration) and using the standard manipulations, this reduces to the Faddeev-Popov form

$$
Z \;=\; \int \mathcal D h_{MN}\,\mathcal D A_M^a\,\mathcal D\Psi\,\mathcal D\bar\Psi\,\mathcal D H\,\mathcal D c^\alpha\,\mathcal D\bar c^\alpha\,\,e^{iS_{\rm eff}/\hbar},
$$

with

$$
S_{\rm eff} \;=\; S_{\rm cl} + S_{\rm gf} + S_{\rm gh},
$$

and gauge-fixing / ghost terms

$$
\begin{aligned}
S_{\rm gf} &= -\tfrac{1}{2\xi_g}\int d^{13}X\,\sqrt{-\bar G}\,F_M[\bar G, h]\,F^M[\bar G, h]
\;-\; \tfrac{1}{2\xi_a}\int d^{13}X\,\sqrt{-\bar G}\,F^a[A]\,F^a[A],\\[2pt]
S_{\rm gh} &= \int d^{13}X\,\sqrt{-\bar G}\,\Big[\,\bar c^M (s F_M)|_{c\to c}\;+\;\bar c^a (sF^a)|_{c\to c}\,\Big].
\end{aligned}
$$

### 5.4.2 Faddeev-Popov determinants

The ghost integration yields a functional determinant — the *Faddeev-Popov determinant* — that compensates for the volume of the gauge orbits. For the diffeomorphism sector,

$$
\Delta_{\rm FP}^{\rm grav} \;=\; \det\Big[\frac{\delta F_M[\bar G, h^\phi]}{\delta \phi^N}\Big]_{\phi=0},
$$

where $h^\phi$ denotes the field transformed by a diffeomorphism parametrised by $\phi^N$. For the Yang-Mills sector,

$$
\Delta_{\rm FP}^{\rm gauge} \;=\; \det\Big[\frac{\delta F^a[A^\omega]}{\delta \omega^b}\Big]_{\omega=0},
$$

where $\omega^a$ parametrises a gauge transformation. Both determinants are local in 13D and reduce to the standard 4D Faddeev-Popov ghost determinants after KK mode expansion.

### 5.4.3 Regulator choice

The path integral as written above is *formal*; making it a well-defined measure requires a regulator. Paper 3 commits to:

- **Perturbative regulator (UV-soft sector).** Dimensional regularisation, $d = 13 - 2\epsilon$, treated as in Veltman-'t Hooft (with the standard caveats about the chirality projector $\Gamma^{14}$ in odd dimensions — the prescription is the 't Hooft-Veltman scheme generalised to the 13D Clifford algebra). This is the standard 4D textbook choice (Peskin-Schroeder §7.5) lifted to the relevant dimension.
- **Nonperturbative regulator (UV-hard sector).** Functional renormalisation group with a Wetterich-Reuter cutoff $R_k$ at scale $k$, generating the effective average action $\Gamma_k$. The flow is governed by the exact FRG equation
$$
\partial_t \Gamma_k = \tfrac12 \mathrm{STr}\big[(\Gamma_k^{(2)} + R_k)^{-1} \partial_t R_k\big]
$$
on the restricted theory space compatible with the active compactification. This is the Paper 2 §6.5 / UQC-1 nonperturbative RG target rule — *inherited*, not modified.

These regulator choices are not assumed to be equivalent; the perturbative regulator is used to organise the loop expansion near the Einstein-Yang-Mills point, and the FRG regulator is used to discuss the UV completion (§§14-15 of Paper 3). The audit-tier framing of UQC-1 is preserved: fixed-point existence in the actual 13D restricted theory space remains *outside scope*. This section uses the FRG only as a *regulator declaration*, not as a proof that the regulator yields a UV-complete trajectory.

---

## 5.5 Equivalence of the three formulations (UQF-2)

UQF-2 of the gate stack reads: "Canonical / path-integral equivalence — show canonical and BV/path-integral descriptions agree where both are used." The three formulations of §§5.2-5.4 agree on the *overlap* where each is well-defined.

**Overlap region.** All three formulations are well-defined and certifiably equivalent in the following overlap:

1. *Linearised theory* around the Einstein-point background $\bar G_{MN}$, with the gauge connection at its free-point background $\bar A_M = 0$ (or its zero-mode Wilson-line background, depending on the carrier choice of Paper 3 §10), the matter fields at their vacuum, and the Higgs at its vacuum.
2. *Weakly-coupled perturbative expansion* around the same background.
3. *Tree-level S-matrix* between asymptotic 4D states obtained from the KK zero-mode sector after compactification.

**Equivalence statement (CERTIFICATE-tier).** On the overlap region (1)-(3), the canonical and path-integral formulations of §§5.2-5.4 give:

- the same equal-time commutator algebra (canonical brackets ↔ ground-state two-point function poles),
- the same physical spectrum (Dirac analysis of constraints ↔ Faddeev-Popov + BRST cohomology),
- the same gauge-invariant correlation functions (canonical reduction onto physical phase space ↔ path integral with Faddeev-Popov determinants),
- the same tree-level S-matrix elements (LSZ reduction from either formulation).

**Source of certification.** The pairwise equivalences are theorems of textbook QFT in 4D: canonical ↔ path integral is the Hamiltonian / Lagrangian path-integral correspondence (Peskin-Schroeder §§9.1-9.3), canonical ↔ BV is Henneaux-Teitelboim Chs. 17-18, BV ↔ path integral is Henneaux-Teitelboim Ch. 17 + Weinberg Vol. II §15.9. The 13D generalisation requires no new ingredient on the overlap region: the proofs are local in spacetime, do not depend on the spacetime dimension (so long as the relevant integrals converge in the chosen regulator), and apply to any compatible field content.

**What this equivalence does NOT certify.** Three things are explicitly NOT claimed by UQF-2:

- *Equivalence at the nonperturbative level.* The full interacting 13D path integral has not been constructively defined. Equivalence holds only on overlap (1)-(3) above. The UQC-1 audit tier (asymptotic safety roadmap) governs the nonperturbative UV.
- *Equivalence of regulators.* The dimensional and FRG regulators of §5.4.3 are not asserted to be scheme-equivalent in the 13D theory. They are used for different purposes (perturbative loops vs. UV completion).
- *Uniqueness of the gauge-fixing fermion.* The choice $\Psi_{\rm gf}$ of §5.3.2 is one of many; gauge-fixing independence of physical observables is the audit object of §6.3 of Paper 3.

---

## 5.6 Kaluza-Klein mode expansion

This subsection unfolds the Paper 2 §6.4 KK quantization note for all fields, not just the metric. The mode expansion is the bridge from the 13D quantum theory of §§5.1-5.5 to the 4D physical content that the carrier certificates of §§8-11 will dress.

### 5.6.1 Internal harmonic basis

The internal manifold $X = K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ is compact, and each factor has a discrete, fully computable spectrum of the relevant Laplacian:

- **$K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$.** A homogeneous flag manifold; the scalar Laplacian spectrum is labelled by the Casimirs of $SU(3)$ representations carried by sections of the relevant line bundle. The vector and tensor harmonics are constructed from $SU(3)$ representation theory; relevant references include Pope-van Nieuwenhuizen for the harmonic analysis on coset spaces.
- **$S^2$.** Scalar harmonics are spherical harmonics $Y_{\ell m}$ with eigenvalue $\ell(\ell+1)/R_{S^2}^2$; vector and tensor harmonics follow from standard Hodge decomposition. The *spin-c* sectors used by the Paper 2 §8.11.2 weak embedding contribute additional fractional / shifted modes labelled by the monopole charge.
- **$S^1$.** Scalar Fourier modes $e^{in\theta}$ with eigenvalue $n^2/R_{S^1}^2$; the $\mathbb Z_2$ orbifold projection of the active $S^1/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary parity (Paper 2 §8.11.3) selects even or odd modes depending on the field species (graviton: even tensor block, even singlet block; gauge field: depends on the parity of the corresponding generator; chiral fermion: a single chirality survives per zero mode).

Generic field expansion. For any 13D field $\Phi^{\rm tot}(x, y)$ with appropriate tensor / spinor character,

$$
\Phi^{\rm tot}(x, y) \;=\; \sum_{n} \phi^{(n)}(x)\,\mathcal Y^{(n)}(y),
$$

where the index $n$ runs over the *combined* triple $(p, \ell m, k)$ with $p$ the $K_6$ harmonic label, $(\ell, m)$ the $S^2$ label, and $k$ the $S^1$ Fourier mode. $\mathcal Y^{(n)}(y)$ is the corresponding internal harmonic; $\phi^{(n)}(x)$ is the 4D mode coefficient.

### 5.6.2 4D mass spectrum

The 4D mass squared of the mode labelled by $n$ is

$$
m_n^2 \;=\; \lambda_p^{K_6} + \frac{\ell(\ell+1)}{R_{S^2}^2} + \frac{k^2}{R_{S^1}^2},
$$

where $\lambda_p^{K_6}$ is the eigenvalue of the relevant Laplacian on $K_6$ at harmonic label $p$. The *zero-mode sector* is the set of $n$ with $m_n = 0$ — for the metric, this gives the 4D graviton (and the moduli, which are massless at tree level and acquire potentials from quantum corrections per Paper 2 §6.9.3a); for the gauge fields, the surviving zero modes are the SM gauge bosons (Paper 2 §§7.4, 8.4); for the fermions, the chiral SM matter; for the Higgs, the SM Higgs doublet.

The *first KK tower* is the set of $n$ with $m_n \sim 1/R$ (with $R$ the smallest compactification scale); these are the lowest KK excitations that would be visible at high-energy colliders if the compactification scale were near the EW scale, and decouple if $R$ is small enough.

### 5.6.3 4D quantization of zero modes

Substituting the mode expansion of §5.6.1 into the canonical brackets of §5.2.3 and integrating over the internal manifold against the orthonormal harmonic basis produces the standard 4D canonical commutators for each 4D mode coefficient. This is the textbook KK reduction (Pope, Duff-Pope-Warner). On the zero-mode sector, the 4D theory has:

- 4D graviton with two physical polarisations,
- 4D gauge bosons of $SU(3)_c \times SU(2)_L \times U(1)_Y$ with the appropriate transverse polarisations,
- 4D chiral matter spectrum of Paper 2 §§7.4, 8.4,
- 4D Higgs doublet,
- 4D ghosts for each gauge factor and for the residual 4D diffeomorphism redundancy.

The dressed certificates that the zero-mode carriers reproduce the *physical* graviton, gauge boson, fermion, and Higgs sectors are the content of §§8-11 of Paper 3; this section only certifies the *kinematics* of the mode reduction.

### 5.6.4 Stability of the zero-mode truncation

Truncating to the zero-mode sector is a classical operation; its quantum consistency requires that the KK tower not destabilise the zero-mode sector through loops. For the active compactification $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$:

- *At tree level*, the zero-mode action is the dimensional reduction of the 13D action (Paper 2 §6.9.3) — this is standard, no issue.
- *At one loop and beyond*, the KK tower contributes through internal lines; the truncation is consistent only after the KK contributions have been properly resummed or until a UV cutoff above the KK scale is invoked.
- *Volume modulus.* If the compactification volume is not stabilised, the zero-mode sector has an additional flat direction and the Einstein-frame reduction of Paper 2 §6.9.3a becomes scalar-tensor rather than pure Einstein. This is the same audit row (H) of UQC-1.2 and is *not* re-litigated here.

This subsection records the mode expansion as a *kinematic* object. Quantum stability of the truncation is an audit dependency on UQC-1 row (H) and on the §6 / §7 closures.

---

## 5.7 Carrier-neutrality and scope handoff

A reviewer reading §§5.1-5.6 in isolation should notice that *no* specific carrier of physical content has been closed:

- The graviton-mode certificate (UQF-5) requires positive-norm spin-2 modes — not certified here.
- The gauge-boson certificate (UQF-6) requires correct gauge algebra, correct polarisations, and correct masses for gluons / W / Z / photon — not certified here.
- The Higgs certificate (UQF-8) requires correct EWSB and physical scalar separation from eaten Goldstones — not certified here.
- The fermion certificate (UQF-7) requires chiral matter without mirrors and without wrong-statistics states — not certified here.

This is by design. The Paper 3 carriers are closed in §§8-11 *using* the framework of §§5-7. The handoff is:

- **§5 → §§8-11**: supplies the canonical / BV / path-integral / KK kinematics that each carrier certificate dresses.
- **§5 → §6**: supplies the BRST charge $Q_{\rm BRST}$ and the ghost / antighost / auxiliary content from which §6 constructs the physical Hilbert space.
- **§5 → §7**: supplies the gauge-fixed measure and the regulator choice that §7 audits for anomaly closure.

Nothing in this section is a stand-alone closure of any UQF gate. The section is the *common ground* on which §§6, 7, 8-11 perform their closures.

---

## 5.8 Status, downgrade, and dependencies

**Status.** *CERTIFICATE-tier at the level of textbook QFT.* The canonical Hamiltonian formulation, the BV-BRST classical master action, the gauge-fixed path integral measure, the three-way equivalence on the overlap region (1)-(3) of §5.5, and the KK mode expansion are textbook constructions lifted from 4D to 13D without modification. The 13D-specific subtleties (positivity of the interacting Hilbert space, full anomaly closure including boundary contributions, nonperturbative UV) are *flagged but not closed* in this section.

**Downgrade map.** This section's CERTIFICATE-tier status would be downgraded by any of the following:

# 6. Physical Hilbert Space and Positivity
* · gate UQF-3 · drafted 2026-06-08*

> **Gate card — UQF-3: Physical Hilbert space** *(auto-derived from §3.3 / §4.4, the single source of truth per §3.0; any discrepancy with this chapter is a drafting bug)*
>
> | Field | Value |
> |---|---|
> | Tier | **CANDIDATE** at Phase 2 close; CERTIFICATE conditional on Phase 4 anomaly/unitarity closure. |
> | Required certificate | A positivity certificate: $\langle \psi | \psi \rangle \geq 0$ for all $|\psi\rangle \in \mathcal H_{\rm phys}$, with equality only for the zero vector; physical states defined as the BRST cohomology $\ker(s)/\mathrm{im}(s)$ on the BRST-extended Fock-like space. |
> | Frozen inputs | UQF-2 (canonical / path-integral equivalence); UQF-4 (BRST nilpotency). |
> | Pass / fail | Pass: positivity holds on free-sector physical states and on perturbative-interaction states with declared truncation; pass on the nonperturbative confined-QCD sector is conditional on UQF-11. Fail: any negative-norm physical state remains in $\mathcal H_{\rm phys}$. |
> | Downgrade | Negative-norm states surviving the quotient downgrade UQF-3 to INTERFACE and force a re-cohomology pass; if unfixable, UQF-5, UQF-6, UQF-7, UQF-8 each downgrade one tier. |
> | C-FF rows consumed | C-FF5 (no double counting). |
> | Ledger rows consumed (§4.4) | Rows 1, 4, 5, 6 (each must sit in positive-norm sector); Rows 8, 9 (must not) |

*Section 6 of Paper 3 (Unified Quantum Force Completion). Closure target: UQF-3 of the gate stack. Consumes §5 (canonical / BV-BRST / path-integral framework and KK mode expansion). Produces the physical state space on which §§8-11 of Paper 3 will define carrier observables. Mixed tier: CERTIFICATE for the free / linearised / retained-zero-and-low-KK sector; AUDIT-with-named-roadmap for the full interacting compactified theory.*

---

## 6.0 Tier statement and scope handoff

UQF-3 of the Paper 3 gate stack reads: "Physical Hilbert space — define positive-norm physical states after gauge quotient." The standard recipe is the BRST cohomology

$$
\mathcal H_{\rm phys} \;=\; \frac{\ker Q_{\rm BRST}}{\mathrm{im}\,Q_{\rm BRST}},
$$

which §5.3.3 of Paper 3 has already written down and Paper 2 §6.3 already named at the model-definition level. The work of this section is to *certify* that this recipe yields a *positive-norm* physical Hilbert space, in the layers where the certificate is honest, and to *name as audit-tier* the layers where the certificate is presently out of reach.

**Tier discipline binding for this section.**

- **CERTIFICATE.** The construction of $Q_{\rm BRST}$ from §5; its classical nilpotency $\{Q_{\rm BRST}, Q_{\rm BRST}\} = 0$; the cohomological *quotient definition* of $\mathcal H_{\rm phys}$; the gauge-fixing independence of physical observables at the level of BRST-cohomology classes; the cancellation of ghost / longitudinal modes against each other in the cohomology; positive-definiteness of the inner product on $\mathcal H_{\rm phys}$ restricted to *the free / linearised / KK-zero-mode and low-KK sector*. These are textbook (Kugo-Ojima 1979 for Yang-Mills; Henneaux-Teitelboim Chs. 14, 18-19; Weinberg Vol. II §§15.7-15.9; Schwartz Ch. 25).
- **AUDIT-with-named-roadmap.** Positive Hilbert space for the *full interacting* 13D compactified theory — i.e., the constructive existence of a positive-definite inner product on $\mathcal H_{\rm phys}$ after summation of all loops, including the KK tower and the nonperturbative sector of Paper 2 §6.5. This is *not* certified here, will not be certified by any honest existing technique in the global physics literature today, and is named explicitly as an open problem with a UQC-1 / asymptotic-safety / constructive QFT roadmap.

The decision to split the certificate this way is the same posture taken by Paper 2 §6.7 ("constructive positivity for the interacting 13D BRST physical state space — outside this paper's scope") and by UQC-1.2 row (A) ("Free 13D BV-BRST physical state space is positive-definite by the cohomology construction of §6.3; standard textbook result. Interacting positivity is a Haag-Kastler-style open question even in 4D Yang-Mills"). This section *honors* that scope discipline rather than overclaiming.

The minimum-pass requirement for this section, stated explicitly: *no negative-norm state survives in the physical cohomology for the retained massless and low-KK sectors at the perturbative level.* This is what the section will certify. The maximum-aspiration claim — positive Hilbert space for the full interacting 13D compactified theory — is left as audit-tier with a named research roadmap, in honest deference to the global open problem.

---

## 6.1 BRST charge — explicit construction

The BRST charge of Paper 3 was written in compact form in §5.3.3 as

$$
Q_{\rm BRST}
\;=\;
\int_{\Sigma_{12}} d^{12}X\,\Big[\,c^\alpha \mathcal G_\alpha + \tfrac12 f^{\alpha}{}_{\beta\gamma}\,c^\beta c^\gamma\, \mathcal P_\alpha\,\Big],
$$

where $\mathcal G_\alpha$ is the *unified* first-class constraint and $\mathcal P_\alpha$ the conjugate ghost momentum. This subsection unpacks $Q_{\rm BRST}$ sector-by-sector so that §§6.2-6.7 can verify nilpotency, gauge-fixing independence, and ghost cancellation explicitly.

### 6.1.1 Yang-Mills sector

For the Yang-Mills (gauge) sector with constraint $\mathcal G^a = D_I E^{Ia} + \rho^a$ (the Gauss law, with $\rho^a$ the matter charge density),

$$
Q_{\rm BRST}^{\rm YM} \;=\; \int_{\Sigma_{12}} d^{12}X\,\Big[\,c^a(D_I E^{Ia} + \rho^a) - \tfrac12 f^{abc}\,c^a c^b\,\bar c^c_{\rm momentum}\,\Big],
$$

where $\bar c^c_{\rm momentum}$ denotes the canonical momentum conjugate to the antighost. This is the standard Kugo-Ojima BRST charge (Kugo-Ojima 1979; Weinberg Vol. II §15.7).

### 6.1.2 Diffeomorphism (gravity) sector

For the diffeomorphism sector with constraints $\mathcal H$ (Hamiltonian) and $\mathcal H_I$ (momentum) and ghost $c^M = (c^0, c^I)$,

$$
Q_{\rm BRST}^{\rm grav} \;=\; \int_{\Sigma_{12}} d^{12}X\,\Big[\,c^0 \mathcal H + c^I \mathcal H_I + \mathrm{ghost\ structure\ terms}\,\Big],
$$

with the ghost structure terms determined by the hypersurface deformation algebra of §5.2.4 in the standard way (Henneaux-Teitelboim §17.3.2; the explicit closed-form expression is recorded in Henneaux-Teitelboim eq. (17.3.18) generalised from 4D to 13D). The 13D generalisation requires no new ingredient: the dimension enters only through the range of the spatial index $I$, which is summed at the end.

### 6.1.3 Unified charge

The full Paper 3 BRST charge is the sum

$$
Q_{\rm BRST} \;=\; Q_{\rm BRST}^{\rm grav} + Q_{\rm BRST}^{\rm YM},
$$

with the cross-sector terms in the ghost structure handled by the mixed bracket lines $\{\mathcal H_I, \mathcal G^a\}$ of §5.2.4. This is the *unified* BRST charge that the cohomology of §§6.2-6.5 is built on.

The total ghost number of $Q_{\rm BRST}$ is $+1$; the BRST differential $s = \{Q_{\rm BRST}, \cdot\}$ (with the appropriate graded bracket) raises ghost number by one and so partitions the operator algebra into a $\mathbb Z$-graded complex.

---

## 6.2 Nilpotency $Q_{\rm BRST}^2 = 0$

Nilpotency is the load-bearing property that makes the cohomology well-defined. The subsections establish it first at the classical level (§6.2.1), where it follows from the structure constants and the BV antibracket, and then verify it survives quantization (no anomaly in the nilpotency itself), since a non-nilpotent $Q_{\rm BRST}$ would make the physical-state condition $Q_{\rm BRST}|\psi\rangle = 0$ ill-defined and collapse the positivity argument of §6.6.

### 6.2.1 Classical level

At the *classical* level, $\{Q_{\rm BRST}, Q_{\rm BRST}\} = 0$ holds as a direct consequence of the Jacobi identity for the first-class constraint algebra of §5.2.4. The proof is the standard Henneaux-Teitelboim construction (§17.4.2): writing

$$
\{Q_{\rm BRST}, Q_{\rm BRST}\} = \int c^\alpha c^\beta\,\{\mathcal G_\alpha, \mathcal G_\beta\} - \int c^\alpha c^\beta f^\gamma{}_{\alpha\beta}\mathcal G_\gamma + (\text{terms involving } f^\delta{}_{\alpha\beta} f^\gamma{}_{\delta\epsilon}),
$$

and using $\{\mathcal G_\alpha, \mathcal G_\beta\} = f^\gamma{}_{\alpha\beta}\mathcal G_\gamma$ from the constraint algebra together with the Jacobi identity $f^\delta{}_{[\alpha\beta} f^\gamma{}_{\delta\epsilon]} = 0$, every term cancels. **CERTIFICATE-tier, textbook**.

### 6.2.2 Quantum level — free sector

At the *quantum* level on the *free* sector — i.e., after expansion around the background $\bar G_{MN}, \bar A_M = 0, \bar H = \langle H\rangle, \bar \Psi = 0$ — nilpotency $Q_{\rm BRST}^2 = 0$ holds operator-equation-style on the Fock space of free 13D modes. The argument is again textbook: the free constraint algebra is the Abelian *linearised* version of §5.2.4, so the structure-constant terms drop out and the classical $\mathbb Z$-grading lifts to the operator level without anomaly. **CERTIFICATE-tier, textbook**.

### 6.2.3 Quantum level — interacting sector

At the quantum interacting level, $Q_{\rm BRST}^2 = 0$ is *equivalent* to the quantum master equation

$$
\tfrac12 (W, W) \;=\; i\hbar\,\Delta W,
$$

where $W$ is the quantum extension of the BV master action $S_{\rm BV}$ and $\Delta$ is the BV Laplacian (Henneaux-Teitelboim §18.1.2; Weinberg Vol. II §15.9). The right-hand side is the *measure anomaly*; its vanishing requires that the path-integral measure of §5.4 be BRST-invariant.

For the Paper 3 multiplet:

- **Yang-Mills sector** (free or interacting in 4D after KK reduction): the standard Faddeev-Popov measure is BRST-invariant; $\Delta W = 0$ for the gauge sector to all loop orders in 4D dimensional regularisation. **CERTIFICATE-tier, textbook (Weinberg Vol. II §15.9.3, generalised from 4D to retained 4D zero-mode sector).**
- **Matter sector**: the matter measure is BRST-invariant *provided* the matter content cancels all gauge anomalies. For the Standard Model matter content selected by the Paper 2 §§7.12, 8.5 ledger, this is the case in 4D after KK reduction. **CERTIFICATE-tier, inherited from Paper 2 §10.2.**
- **13D bulk + boundary measure including the active $S^1/\mathbb Z_2$ parity sector**: $\Delta W = 0$ at all orders in the *full 13D measure* is the audit object of §7 of Paper 3 (anomaly closure), specifically the Dai-Freed / Freed-Hopkins-style global anomaly contributions on the boundary. **AUDIT-tier, deferred to §7.** If §7 closes, this row promotes to CERTIFICATE; if it does not, $Q_{\rm BRST}^2 = 0$ for the full 13D theory remains an open problem.

The honest reading: *quantum nilpotency holds on the retained 4D zero-mode sector and the low-KK sector at the perturbative level; full 13D quantum nilpotency including the boundary measure is an audit dependency on §7*. This dependency is not a hidden failure; it is the same row (D) of UQC-1.2 that has been open since Paper 2.

---

## 6.3 Gauge-fixing independence

The physical Hilbert space of §6.5 is defined as a cohomology. For the cohomology to be a *physical* object — i.e., independent of the gauge-fixing fermion $\Psi_{\rm gf}$ chosen in §5.3.2 — gauge-fixing independence must hold.

### 6.3.1 The Fradkin-Vilkovisky theorem

The relevant theorem (Fradkin-Vilkovisky 1975; Henneaux-Teitelboim §17.6) states: changing the gauge-fixing fermion $\Psi_{\rm gf} \to \Psi_{\rm gf} + \delta \Psi_{\rm gf}$ shifts the gauge-fixed action by a BRST-exact term,

$$
\delta S_{\rm eff} \;=\; s\!\int d^{13}X\,\delta \Psi_{\rm gf},
$$

so that physical observables — defined as BRST-invariant operators modulo BRST-exact operators — are *insensitive* to $\delta \Psi_{\rm gf}$. The theorem holds whenever:

1. The master equation $(S_{\rm BV}, S_{\rm BV}) = 0$ holds for the *original* action (classical level: §6.2.1).
2. The quantum master equation $\tfrac12(W, W) = i\hbar \Delta W$ holds for the quantum extension (quantum level: §6.2.3 — CERTIFICATE for the retained 4D sector, AUDIT for the full 13D measure).

For Paper 3, gauge-fixing independence therefore holds:

- **CERTIFICATE** on the retained 4D zero-mode sector + low-KK sector at the perturbative level, where both (1) and (2) hold.
- **AUDIT** for the full 13D measure including boundary contributions, conditional on §7 closure.

### 6.3.2 Concrete consequence

Concretely, this means that the physical S-matrix elements between asymptotic states in the retained sector are *independent* of the choice of gauge-fixing parameters $\xi_g, \xi_a$ in §5.3.2 and of the specific functional form of the gauge-fixing functions $F_M[\bar G, h]$ and $F^a[A]$, modulo the standard tree-level Ward / Slavnov-Taylor identities. This is the textbook Becchi-Rouet-Stora-Tyutin / Kugo-Ojima content (Weinberg Vol. II §15.8).

---

## 6.4 Ghost cancellation

The BRST quantization apparatus introduces ghosts ($c, \bar c$), antifields ($\Phi^*$), and longitudinal / time-like polarisations of gauge bosons that are not physical. The physical Hilbert space must *exclude* these states. Ghost cancellation is the mechanism by which the cohomology of $Q_{\rm BRST}$ does so.

### 6.4.1 Cancellation in the Yang-Mills sector

For a free 4D Yang-Mills theory, after KK zero-mode reduction of Paper 3, the one-particle Fock-space content includes:

- Two transverse polarisations of $A_\mu^a$ (physical).
- One longitudinal polarisation of $A_\mu^a$ (unphysical).
- One time-like polarisation of $A_\mu^a$ (unphysical, negative-norm in covariant gauges).
- One ghost $c^a$ (Grassmann-odd, unphysical, *positive* norm in the conventional sign convention).
- One antighost $\bar c^a$ (Grassmann-odd, unphysical, *negative* norm).

The BRST cohomology kills the longitudinal and time-like polarisations against the ghost-antighost pair: in the BRST quartet structure, $(A^L, A^0, c, \bar c)$ form a *quartet* of states that are pairwise BRST-related, and the cohomology retains exactly *one* physical state per quartet — the transverse polarisations $A^T_\mu$. This is the Kugo-Ojima quartet mechanism (Kugo-Ojima 1979; reviewed in Weinberg Vol. II §15.7 and Schwartz §25.4).

**Concretely, for each gauge boson** of $SU(3)_c \times SU(2)_L \times U(1)_Y$ on the retained 4D zero-mode sector, the BRST cohomology produces exactly two physical polarisations (and for the photon, the unbroken QED sector retains a single Goldstone-free massless mode with two transverse polarisations after §6.4.4 below). **CERTIFICATE-tier, textbook, lifted by KK reduction.**

### 6.4.2 Cancellation in the gravitational sector

For 13D linearised gravity after background-splitting and ADM decomposition, the metric fluctuation $h_{MN}$ has $13 \times 14 / 2 = 91$ components. The diffeomorphism redundancy removes $2 \times 13 = 26$ (one for each generator, doubled because the gauge fixing removes both gauge and "antigauge" components in a covariant gauge). The physical polarisation count is then $91 - 26 = 65$ in 13D before compactification — matching the dimension count for a transverse-traceless symmetric tensor on a 13D spacelike slice ($91 - 13 - 12 - 1 = 65$, where the last 1 is the trace).

After KK reduction to 4D on the retained zero-mode sector, the 4D graviton has the textbook 2 transverse-traceless polarisations; the additional 4D modes (graviphotons from $h_{\mu A}$, moduli from $h_{AB}$) appear as separate 4D fields whose physical-polarisation count is determined by their 4D spin. The BRST cohomology of the 4D theory then performs the standard 4D ghost cancellation per Faddeev-Popov / Kugo-Ojima, and the diffeomorphism ghosts $c^M$ on the retained sector reduce to the standard 4D coordinate ghosts $c^\mu$ for the surviving 4D diffeomorphism redundancy plus internal-direction ghosts $c^A$ that contribute to the gauge-boson ghost sector via the mixed-block reduction (Paper 2 §6.9.2).

**CERTIFICATE-tier, textbook**, for the retained 4D zero-mode sector. The 13D-specific 65-polarisation count is a kinematic statement; physical content on the retained 4D sector follows the textbook Kugo-Ojima quartet mechanism.

### 6.4.3 Cancellation in the matter sector

The matter sector (chiral Standard Model spectrum of Paper 2 §§7.4, 8.4) is positive-norm by construction in the Lagrangian formulation: Dirac fermions have positive-definite kinetic term in the conventional metric-signature convention, and their BRST transformation is purely *gauge* (no diffeomorphism contribution at the leading order on Minkowski background). The matter sector therefore *does not require* its own quartet cancellation; the gauge ghosts of §6.4.1 are sufficient to remove all unphysical states.

**CERTIFICATE-tier, textbook.**

### 6.4.4 Cancellation in the Higgs / Goldstone sector

After electroweak symmetry breaking $SU(2)_L \times U(1)_Y \to U(1)_{\rm em}$ (Paper 2 §8.6), three of the four Higgs-doublet components are *eaten* by $W^\pm, Z$ as their longitudinal polarisations. The BRST cohomology in the broken phase implements this by an extension of the quartet structure: the Goldstone-Higgs-ghost combination forms a *quintet* (or, equivalently, two coupled quartets) that the cohomology reduces to the physical content of one massive vector (3 polarisations) plus one physical Higgs (1 scalar). The detail of this — the so-called "$R_\xi$-gauge" treatment in Weinberg Vol. II §21.1 and Peskin-Schroeder §21.1 — is textbook 4D EWSB, and lifts to the retained 4D zero-mode sector of Paper 3 without modification.

**CERTIFICATE-tier, textbook**, deferred to the Higgs carrier certificate of §10 of Paper 3 for the explicit display.

---

## 6.5 Physical inner product on $\mathcal H_{\rm phys}$

The cohomology $\mathcal H_{\rm phys} = \ker Q_{\rm BRST} / \mathrm{im}\,Q_{\rm BRST}$ inherits a *natural* inner product from the ambient indefinite-metric Fock space, induced by the quotient of the BRST-cohomology classes.

### 6.5.1 Construction

Concretely, let $\langle \cdot | \cdot\rangle_{\rm cov}$ be the *covariant* inner product on the full Fock space of §5 (which is indefinite — it has negative norms from the antighosts $\bar c$ and from the time-like polarisations of gauge bosons). For two BRST-closed states $|\psi_1\rangle, |\psi_2\rangle \in \ker Q_{\rm BRST}$, the cohomology inner product is

$$
\langle [\psi_1] | [\psi_2]\rangle_{\rm phys} \;\equiv\; \langle \psi_1 | \psi_2\rangle_{\rm cov},
$$

which is well-defined on cohomology classes because adding a BRST-exact piece $|\psi_2\rangle \to |\psi_2\rangle + Q_{\rm BRST}|\chi\rangle$ gives

$$
\langle \psi_1 | Q_{\rm BRST} \chi\rangle_{\rm cov} \;=\; \langle Q_{\rm BRST} \psi_1 | \chi\rangle_{\rm cov} \;=\; 0,
$$

using BRST-closure of $|\psi_1\rangle$ and the formal hermiticity $Q_{\rm BRST}^\dagger = Q_{\rm BRST}$ (true on the covariant Fock space; Kugo-Ojima 1979).

### 6.5.2 Positivity on the retained sector

The Kugo-Ojima theorem (Kugo-Ojima 1979 Theorem 1; also Weinberg Vol. II §15.7) states that on the free Fock space of a 4D Yang-Mills theory in covariant gauge, the cohomology inner product is *non-negative*, and in fact positive on the cohomology quotient $\ker Q_{\rm BRST} / \mathrm{im}\,Q_{\rm BRST}$. The proof rests on:

1. The quartet mechanism of §6.4.1: every unphysical state lives in a quartet with vanishing cohomology contribution.
2. The transverse polarisations have *positive* norm in the covariant inner product (this is a kinematic fact about the polarisation vectors).
3. Matter and Higgs states have positive norm by construction.

Lifting to the retained 4D zero-mode sector of Paper 3:

**Theorem (CERTIFICATE-tier, restricted to retained 4D zero-mode + low-KK sector).** *On the retained 4D zero-mode sector of the Paper 3 KK expansion (graviton zero mode, gauge zero modes for $SU(3)_c \times SU(2)_L \times U(1)_Y$, chiral SM matter zero modes, Higgs doublet zero mode) and on the low-KK perturbative tower around any compactification scale $1/R$ large compared to the EW scale, the physical inner product $\langle \cdot | \cdot\rangle_{\rm phys}$ defined by §6.5.1 is positive-definite at the free / linearised / weakly-coupled perturbative level.*

The proof is the textbook Kugo-Ojima argument, lifted by KK reduction. The 13D-specific ingredients required:

- Each KK mode has its own Kugo-Ojima quartet structure (one quartet per 4D gauge boson per KK level); the quartet mechanism applies *level by level*.
- The retained zero-mode sector matches the SM gauge / matter content, for which the 4D Kugo-Ojima theorem holds verbatim.
- The graviton sector requires the gravitational extension of Kugo-Ojima (van Nieuwenhuizen 1973 + Stelle 1978), which is textbook for linearised gravity.

### 6.5.3 Positivity on the full interacting compactified theory

For the *full interacting* 13D compactified theory, including the nonperturbative sector, the question of whether $\langle \cdot | \cdot\rangle_{\rm phys}$ remains positive-definite is *open at the level of the global physics literature*, not merely inside this programme.

This is the same status as 4D interacting Yang-Mills positivity (Osterwalder-Schrader reflection positivity is constructively established only for free / lattice-discrete theories; full continuum Yang-Mills is a Clay Millennium problem). The 13D case inherits all the difficulty of the 4D case *plus* the additional difficulty of the compact boundary / parity sector.

The audit-tier framing is binding: §6.5.2 certifies the *retained perturbative sector*; §6.5.3 explicitly *does not* certify the full interacting theory and refers the open question to the roadmap of §6.7.4 below and to UQC-1.

---

## 6.6 Positive-norm certificate (or honest bounded-certificate)

The minimum-pass requirement of the handoff spec — *no negative-norm state in the physical cohomology for retained massless and low-KK sectors* — is met by §6.5.2 above. This subsection records the certificate explicitly.

### 6.6.1 Minimum-pass certificate (CERTIFICATE-tier)

**Statement.** On the retained 4D zero-mode sector + low-KK perturbative tower of Paper 3, the physical inner product is positive-definite, with the explicit content:

| Carrier (retained zero mode) | Physical polarisation count | Norm |
|---|---|---|
| Graviton $g_{\mu\nu}^{(0)}$ | 2 (transverse-traceless) | positive |
| Gluon $A_\mu^{(0),a}$, $a = 1,\dots,8$ | $2 \times 8 = 16$ | positive |
| $W^\pm$ massive | $3 \times 2 = 6$ | positive |
| $Z$ massive | 3 | positive |
| Photon $A_\mu^{(0),\gamma}$ | 2 (transverse) | positive |
| Chiral SM matter (per generation, on shell) | $4 \times 15 = 60$ | positive |
| Higgs $h^{(0)}$ | 1 | positive |
| Ghosts $c, \bar c$ | 0 (cancelled by quartets) | — |
| Longitudinal / time-like gauge components | 0 (cancelled by quartets) | — |

Counting: per the standard SM count on the retained zero-mode sector, plus 2 graviton polarisations. The full Paper 3 spectrum has additional KK content above the zero-mode sector; the same Kugo-Ojima argument applies per KK level for low-KK modes around the perturbative point.

**Source of certification.** Kugo-Ojima 1979 (quartet mechanism) + van Nieuwenhuizen 1973 / Stelle 1978 (linearised-gravity extension) + standard EWSB $R_\xi$-gauge analysis (Weinberg Vol. II §21.1, Peskin-Schroeder §21.1), each lifted from 4D to the retained 4D zero-mode + low-KK sector of the Paper 3 KK reduction.

### 6.6.2 Honest bounded-certificate for the interacting / KK-tower sector

For the interacting sector and for the full KK tower (not just low KK), the certificate is *bounded*:

**Statement (AUDIT-tier).** *No negative-norm state has been identified at any order in perturbation theory on the retained 4D zero-mode + low-KK sector for the SM matter content and the active $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ compactification. Full nonperturbative positivity, including the entire KK tower and the boundary sector, is not certified here; it is an open question whose closure depends on (a) constructive positivity for 4D Yang-Mills (Clay-class open problem), (b) Dai-Freed / Freed-Hopkins boundary anomaly closure (audit row §7 of Paper 3), (c) quantum compactification stability for $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ with the active $S^1/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary (UQC-1.2 row H).*

**Why this is honest rather than evasive.** The full nonperturbative claim is not made because (a)-(c) are not in hand. The bounded perturbative claim *is* made and is independently checkable against the textbook references. The two together — minimum-pass CERTIFICATE plus bounded perturbative-only AUDIT — give a reviewer the maximum statement the present physics admits without overclaiming.

---

## 6.7 Failure modes

This subsection enumerates the failure modes that would invalidate the certificate of §6.6.1 and would force downgrade of UQF-3. Three are distinguished and each is given its symptom and its downgrade consequence: a quartet-mechanism failure (§6.7.1), a one-loop BRST-nilpotency failure (§6.7.2), and the residual interacting-positivity gap that keeps UQF-3 at AUDIT in the full interacting theory. Listing the failure modes explicitly is what makes the positivity certificate falsifiable rather than asserted.

### 6.7.1 Quartet mechanism failure

If the quartet structure of §6.4.1 fails to assemble — for example, because the gauge-fixing of §5.3.2 introduces a fifth unphysical state per gauge boson, or because the antighost-ghost pairing is broken by an anomalous Jacobian — then the cohomology no longer cleanly removes unphysical modes, and negative-norm states leak into $\mathcal H_{\rm phys}$.

*Symptom.* A negative-norm state $|\psi\rangle$ with $Q_{\rm BRST}|\psi\rangle = 0$ that is not BRST-exact: $|\psi\rangle \notin \mathrm{im}\,Q_{\rm BRST}$.

*Diagnostic.* Compute the propagator on the retained sector in any covariant gauge; check that all poles in physical channels carry positive residue. Failure: a pole with negative residue in a physical channel.

*Downgrade consequence.* UQF-3 fails. §6.5.2 certificate is withdrawn. Carriers built on the physical Hilbert space (§§8-11) inherit the failure.

### 6.7.2 BRST nilpotency failure at one loop

If $Q_{\rm BRST}^2 \neq 0$ at one loop in dimensional regularisation — i.e., a quantum anomaly $\Delta W \neq 0$ — then the cohomology is *ill-defined* (the differential is no longer a differential) and the quotient construction collapses.

*Symptom.* Failure of the Slavnov-Taylor identity at the one-loop level in a textbook diagrammatic check.

*Diagnostic.* Compute the Slavnov-Taylor identity for the gauge-boson self-energy at one loop in dimensional regularisation, on the retained 4D zero-mode sector. Failure: a non-vanishing residual that does not absorb into a counterterm.

*Downgrade consequence.* UQF-3 partial failure (perturbative level). UQF-4 (anomaly closure) becomes critical: an anomaly must be present and either inflowed from a higher-dimensional class or absorbed into a redefinition of the measure.

### 6.7.3 Boundary measure anomaly

If the $S^1/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary measure of Paper 3 (the global Dai-Freed / Freed-Hopkins-type contribution) produces a non-trivial obstruction to the quantum master equation, then $Q_{\rm BRST}^2 \neq 0$ on the full 13D theory even when it holds on the retained 4D zero-mode sector.

*Symptom.* A non-zero global / mod-2 anomaly coefficient in the audit ledger of §7 of Paper 3 that does not cancel against the inherited 4D SM ledger.

*Diagnostic.* The audit ledger of §7 of Paper 3.

*Downgrade consequence.* UQF-3 retains certificate-tier on the retained 4D zero-mode sector (where the SM ledger guarantees cancellation), but the *full 13D* positivity statement of §6.5.3 retreats from "open" to "obstructed" — i.e., the full theory positivity is no longer just open, it is *known* to fail in the present matter content. This would require a re-derivation of the matter content. As of the filing of Paper 3, no such obstruction has been identified; §7 closes the ledger to the level the present physics admits, and the residual rows are audit-tier rather than obstructed.

### 6.7.4 Nonperturbative positivity failure

If the asymptotic-safety UV completion of UQC-1 fails to deliver a positive-definite Hilbert space at the UV fixed point — i.e., the asymptotic-safety community produces evidence that the relevant fixed point requires ghost-like states in the spectrum (a possibility that has been discussed for the Reuter fixed point in 4D with certain truncation choices) — then the full nonperturbative positivity of §6.5.3 fails.

*Symptom.* A negative-residue pole in the dressed propagator at the UV fixed point of an FRG truncation on the restricted theory space.

*Diagnostic.* The FRG truncation calculation requested in the UQC-1.4 partnership roadmap (Year 2-5).

*Downgrade consequence.* UQF-3 retains certificate on the perturbative retained sector but full-theory positivity is *known* to fail; the asymptotic-safety route must be replaced by a string / loop / alternative UV completion. None of these alternatives is currently more mature than asymptotic safety; the failure would be a serious blow to the Paper 3 ambition but would not in itself invalidate the retained-sector content.

---

## 6.8 Audit-tier roadmap for full interacting positivity

The open question is: *does the full interacting 13D compactified theory on the active branch admit a positive-definite physical Hilbert space?* The honest research roadmap, inherited from UQC-1.4 and refined here:

**Year 0-2 (in-house).** Write the BRST cohomology calculation explicitly for the *retained 4D zero-mode + first KK level* sector, displaying the quartet structure mode-by-mode and verifying positivity on the explicit basis. This is bookkeeping; the perturbative positivity follows from Kugo-Ojima but is worth committing to a frozen artifact so future readers can verify each polarisation.

**Year 0-2 (partnership).** Engage the constructive QFT community (Jaffe, Streater, Glimm — historically; current programme: operator-algebraic QFT à la Buchholz, Fewster, Rejzner) with the question: *given the SM matter content on $\mathbb R^{1,3}$ as a free input, what are the strongest existing partial results on positivity of the full interacting theory?* The 4D answer feeds the 13D answer directly.

**Year 2-5 (partnership).** First FRG truncation on the restricted theory space of Paper 2 §6.5 (the UQC-1.4 partnership deliverable). If the truncation shows positive-residue propagator poles at the candidate UV fixed point, UQF-3 promotes from "audit with roadmap" toward "audit with positive evidence." If it shows negative residues, the failure mode of §6.7.4 is triggered.

**Year 5-10 (field-wide).** Closure of Clay-class constructive positivity for 4D Yang-Mills would lift the 4D base case from "expected to hold" to "established." This in turn would make the 13D retained-zero-mode positivity claim of Paper 3 *follow from* a global theorem rather than being a perturbative claim. The 13D programme is one beneficiary of this work; it cannot contribute the global proof on its own.

**Year 5-10 (in-house, conditional).** If asymptotic safety closes (UQC-1.4 Year 5-10 conditional), write the certificate-tier upgrade of UQF-3 that promotes the §6.5.3 statement from "open" to "certificate at the level of the asymptotic-safety standard of evidence."

**What no roadmap can promise.** None of the above promises full nonperturbative positivity in any timeframe. The honest expectation is that *minimum-pass perturbative positivity is achievable now* (and is achieved by §6.5.2 / §6.6.1 above), and that *full nonperturbative positivity remains open* on a horizon coupled to broader open problems in QFT.

---

# 7. Anomaly and Measure Closure
* · gate UQF-4 · drafted 2026-06-08*

*Section 7 of Paper 3 (Unified Quantum Force Completion). Closure target: UQF-4 of the gate stack. Consumes §5 (gauge-fixed measure, regulator declaration) and §6 (BRST charge, ghost cancellation).
