Downgrade if Appendix K does not earn its certificate: UQF-7G drops to *Diagnostic*; UQF-7A–F retain CERTIFICATE tier (they are independent of the neutrino-mass mechanism choice). |

**The single load-bearing 13D-specific subtlety for UQFC-11** is the **chirality survival under compactification — UQF-7B "no mirror fermions"**. The other rows reduce to standard QFT once the matter content is fixed; UQF-7B is the row where the 13D-specific compactification structure ($S^1_Y/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary parity) does the work that distinguishes the SM left-handed-only chiral matter content from a vector-like alternative.

---

## 11.11 Falsifiers

The fermion row is falsified by any of the following:

1. A surviving right-handed $SU(2)_L$ doublet at the 4D zero-mode level (e.g., $Q_R: (\mathbf 3, \mathbf 2)_{1/6}$) — would falsify UQF-7B (no mirror fermions). Observable signature: vector-like quark or lepton multiplets at low energy, or non-$V-A$ structure in the charged-current sector.
2. The 4D Weyl operators failing to obey Fermi-Dirac statistics — would falsify UQF-7C (wrong-statistics exclusion). Observable signature: spin-statistics violation in two-particle exchange experiments (no such violation observed to extraordinary precision).
3. Non-vanishing of any per-generation anomaly coefficient — would falsify UQF-7D. Observable signature: quantum-violation of the supposed gauge symmetry; unphysical degrees of freedom; failure of the SM at the loop level. The five-multiplet was selected precisely because every per-generation coefficient vanishes; any change would have to be accompanied by a compensating change in the matter content.
4. A family count other than three at the $K_6$ spin-c index level — would falsify UQF-7E. Observable signature: a fourth-generation chiral quark/lepton observed (extensive direct searches exclude a heavy fourth-generation chiral fermion).
5. A Yukawa coupling structure inconsistent with the gauge-invariance constraints of §11.6 (e.g., a term that requires the wrong $Y$ assignment on a fermion) — would falsify UQF-7F.
6. A neutrino-mass observation that requires *all three* options (i), (ii), (iii) to be excluded — would force a downgrade of UQF-7G and require Paper 1 Appendix K to specify a new mechanism.
7. Observation of macroscopic baryon-number violation at a rate inconsistent with Paper 1's proton-safety constraints — would falsify the joint UQFC-11 + Paper 1 matter-sector closure.

---

## 11.12 Boundary statement

UQFC-11 *certifies* the chiral matter sector at UQF-7A through UQF-7F tier:

- chiral 4D Weyl quantization for the SM five-multiplet $\{Q_L, u^c_L, d^c_L, L_L, e^c_L\}$ per generation, with gauge-covariant Dirac kinetic terms;
- no mirror fermions surviving the $S^1_Y/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary parity, so parity violation is structural;
- wrong-statistics exclusion — the 4D Weyl descendants obey Fermi-Dirac statistics, inherited from the 13D parent spinor;
- per-generation anomaly closure inherited from Paper 2 §8.5 and Paper 1's main anomaly tables, preserved under quantization;
- three families from the $K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$ spin-c index (Paper 2 §7.4 + Paper 1's spin-c calculation, by interface);
- Yukawa coupling structure to the Higgs Wilson line at the structural / gauge-invariance level (numerical flavor structure deferred).

UQFC-11 records the AUDIT-tier statement for UQF-7G:

- the neutrino-mass mechanism is one of three logical options — Dirac, Majorana from $\nu_L$ alone, or see-saw with right-handed Majorana $\nu_R$;
- the choice is determined by Paper 1 Appendix K, which is invoked by interface only.

UQFC-11 does *not* claim:

- numerical Yukawa values, fermion masses, CKM / PMNS angles, or the resolution of the flavor hierarchy puzzle (routed to Paper 1 + §16);
- the active neutrino masses, mixing angles, or CP-violating phases (routed to Paper 1 Appendix K + §16);
- the see-saw scale $M_R$ or the right-handed neutrino mass spectrum (routed to Paper 1 Appendix K);
- the proton-decay rate or other baryon-number-violation observables (routed to Paper 1 proton-safety sector);
- dark-matter fermion candidates (routed to Paper 4);
- baryogenesis (BG-10 is Paper 4 material, preserves Open / Diagnostic status).

# UQFC-12 — Nonperturbative QCD Certificate (UQF-11)
*UQF-11 (sub-gates UQF-11A confinement, UQF-11B mass gap, UQF-11C hadron-spectrum route, UQF-11D chiral symmetry breaking) · gate UQF-11 · drafted 2026-06-08*

> **Gate card — UQF-11: Nonperturbative QCD** *(auto-derived from §3.3 / §4.4, the single source of truth per §3.0; any discrepancy with this chapter is a drafting bug)*
>
> | Field | Value |
> |---|---|
> | Tier | **AUDIT + ROADMAP** (per UQC-3 inheritance; framework supplies UV completion only with IR inheritance from partner-community work). |
> | Required certificate | A *route* statement, not a closure. (a) Confinement: Wilson-loop area law compatibility with the inherited $SU(3)_c$ algebra; named lattice-QCD comparison program. (b) Mass gap: candidate mass-gap value $\Delta > 0$ inherited from lattice-QCD partner work; not derived in this paper. (c) Hadronic spectrum: inherited from partner-community lattice work. (d) Chiral condensate: candidate origin in the inherited chiral structure; not closed here. The Yang-Mills mass-gap Clay Millennium problem is explicitly **not** claimed to be solved. |
> | Frozen inputs | Paper 2 §7 strong interface; UV completion (UQF-9 for high-energy controllability); gauge-boson certificate (UQF-6 for gluons). |
> | Pass / fail | Pass: each of the four sub-rows has a named lattice / partner-community work program with a stated falsifier. Fail: any sub-row that asserts closure without partner work or without a falsifier. |
> | Downgrade | Any sub-row asserting unfounded closure drops UQF-11 to AUDIT and forces a §12 retraction. |
> | C-FF rows consumed | C-FF9 (regulator), C-FF11 (sanity target). |
> | Ledger rows consumed (§4.4) | Row 4 (gluon sub-row primary); Row 5 (quark fermions) |

**Tier of this section:** **AUDIT-TIER + ROADMAP — NOT A CERTIFICATE**

---

## 12.0 Reviewer first-read for §12

This is one of the two honest-audit sections of Paper 3 (the other is §13,
Strong CP). It is the place at which the paper *does not* hide what it
cannot do.

UQF-11 asks whether the strong-sector interface inherited from Paper 2
(`quantum_forces.md`, §7) admits a full nonperturbative quantum
completion: confinement, a positive mass gap, the hadron spectrum, and
chiral-symmetry breaking, all derived from the same 13D parent geometry
that supplies the active branch $\mathfrak B_{\rm active}$ of Paper 1 and
the $K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$ strong-sector geometry of Paper 2.

The honest answer, after audit, is that UQF-11 lands at **AUDIT-TIER**
across all four sub-gates (UQF-11A, UQF-11B, UQF-11C, UQF-11D). UQF-11A
(confinement) and UQF-11B (mass gap) are, between them, one of the seven
Clay Mathematics Institute Millennium Prize problems (Jaffe–Witten 2000);
no programme — algebraic, lattice-rigorous, holographic,
stochastic-quantization, exact-renormalization-group, or geometric — has
produced a Clay-grade certificate as of 2026. UQF-11C (hadron-spectrum
route) and UQF-11D (chiral symmetry breaking) are downstream of those two
in the certificate hierarchy; their AUDIT-tier outputs follow.

This section therefore does the same thing UQC-3 did in the earlier 13D
Unified Quantum Completion (UQC) series: it states what is required for a
Clay-grade or UQF-11-tier certificate, states what the 13D framework can
honestly contribute as a *compatibility statement*, names the genuinely
open questions, and lays out a 5–15-year research roadmap with named
external collaborators. It does **not** assert "QCD is solved because
$SU(3)_c$ appears." It does **not** assert "the area law follows from
the spin-c bundle on $K_6$." It does **not** upgrade UQF-11's status from
AUDIT-TIER to CERTIFICATE-TIER by implication, by composition, or by
phrasing.

The Paper-3 framing replaces the UQC-3 vocabulary "open problem at the
level of the community physics" with the certificate-stack vocabulary
"audit-tier within Paper 3's UQF-11 gate; full certificate is the
strong-pass target for a future revision." The honesty is identical.
The change is that every claim in this section now routes back to a
UQF-row ID with a frozen pass/fail criterion and a frozen downgrade
rule, in the same discipline the rest of Paper 3 uses.

The reader who wants only the bottom line can skip to §12.7
(Summary-of-audit table) and §12.10 (Status line). The reader who wants
the full audit per sub-gate proceeds linearly.

---

## 12.1 What UQF-11 demands, sub-gate by sub-gate

The UQF-11 gate decomposes into four sub-gates per the handoff
(§9 of `HANDOFF_unified_quantum_force_completion_2026-06-08.md`). We
record the formal demand and the certificate-tier pass/fail criterion
for each.

### 12.1.A UQF-11A — Confinement

**Formal demand.** For pure $SU(3)$ Yang–Mills theory on $\mathbb{R}^4$,
in the confining phase, the rectangular Wilson loop $W(C)$ of contour
$C$ enclosing area $A(C)$ obeys an area law at large $A$:

$$
\langle W(C)\rangle \;\sim\; \exp\!\bigl[-\sigma\, A(C)\bigr],
\qquad \sigma > 0.
$$

**Certificate-tier pass/fail criterion.** A frozen, peer-checkable
mathematical proof that (i) the $SU(3)$ Yang–Mills quantum theory exists
as a Wightman / Osterwalder–Schrader QFT on $\mathbb{R}^4$ in the
constructive sense, and (ii) within that constructed theory,
$\lim_{R,T\to\infty}\bigl[-\tfrac{1}{RT}\log\langle W(R,T)\rangle\bigr]
= \sigma > 0$.

**Candidate analytic routes** (none complete):

- **Center-vortex mechanism** (Greensite school): center-projected
  $Z_3$ vortices reproduce the lattice string tension within statistical
  error after maximal center gauge fixing.
- **Dual superconductor / 't Hooft–Mandelstam**: a magnetic monopole
  condensate squeezes chromoelectric flux into Nielsen–Olesen tubes.
- **Generalized-symmetry / mixed-anomaly** approaches (Gaiotto, Kapustin,
  Komargodski, Seiberg, Cordova): one-form $Z_3$ center symmetry and its
  mixed anomalies sharpen what a confining vacuum must do.
- **Lattice-continuum constructive** (Bałaban-style RG, Magnen–Rivasseau–
  Sénéor): rigorous control exists for abelian gauge theory and
  super-renormalizable scalar models; not for 4D non-abelian.
- **Holographic** (Klebanov–Strassler, Witten thermal $AdS$): produces
  gap-like / area-law behaviour at large $N$, planar, in specific
  confining backgrounds. Not a proof at $N=3$ on $\mathbb{R}^4$.

**Audit verdict at UQF-11A.** No route has produced a Clay-grade
certificate; the framework does not modify that situation.

### 12.1.B UQF-11B — Mass gap

**Formal demand.** The spectrum of the $SU(3)$ Yang–Mills Hamiltonian on
$\mathbb{R}^4$ is contained in $\{0\}\cup[\Delta,\infty)$ for some
$\Delta>0$, with a unique vacuum.

**Certificate-tier pass/fail criterion.** The Clay statement
(Jaffe–Witten 2000) requires (a) a constructive existence proof for the
quantum theory, (b) a proof that the Hamiltonian spectrum has a strictly
positive lowest eigenvalue above the vacuum, (c) a uniqueness proof for
the vacuum. The "minimum practical" version of this gate, recommended in
the handoff §9, is a *frozen nonperturbative certificate* that, under a
declared regulator and a controlled continuum extrapolation, exhibits a
positive lowest glueball or hadronic gap that survives all named
systematics. The full mathematical certificate is the Clay target and is
strictly stronger.

**Audit verdict at UQF-11B.** AUDIT-TIER: minimum-practical version
inherited from lattice QCD (lightest pure-glue $0^{++}$ glueball at
$m_{0^{++}}\approx 1.7$ GeV; Athenodorou & Teper 2020); the full
constructive certificate is the Millennium Prize problem.

### 12.1.C UQF-11C — Hadron-spectrum route

**Formal demand.** A specified route from the quark/gluon fields of the
4D effective theory to the observed hadron spectrum: gauge invariant
color-singlet operator basis, nonperturbative correlator definitions,
mass extraction from correlator asymptotics, and a comparison to the
PDG hadron mass list.

**Certificate-tier pass/fail criterion.** A *route specification*
(not a full computation) at CERTIFICATE-tier requires: (i) the
color-singlet operator basis written down, (ii) the correlator
definitions written down with frozen regulator, (iii) the asymptotic
mass-extraction procedure named, (iv) the cross-check against lattice
QCD that turns the same UV inputs into the same hadron masses. The full
*computation* is standard lattice nonperturbative QCD and is what BMW,
RBC/UKQCD, MILC, HotQCD, FLAG, and the Hadron Spectrum Collaboration
deliver at sub-percent precision in many channels.

**Audit verdict at UQF-11C.** AUDIT-TIER: the route specification is in
hand and is standard nonperturbative QCD; the framework supplies the UV
boundary conditions ($\alpha_3(M_Z)$ from $\mathrm{Vol}(K_6)$; quark
masses from chamber overlap integrals); the IR hadronization is
inherited and is not a framework-distinct derivation.

### 12.1.D UQF-11D — Chiral symmetry breaking

**Formal demand.** A nonzero chiral condensate
$\langle\bar q q\rangle\neq 0$ or an equivalent chiral-breaking
certificate (e.g., Banks–Casher density at the spectrum origin).

**Certificate-tier pass/fail criterion.** A rigorous proof that
spontaneous chiral-symmetry breaking occurs in the constructed
4D $SU(3)$ Yang–Mills + light-quark theory with order parameter
$\Sigma>0$. The Coleman–Witten (1980) result is suggestive in the planar
large-$N$ limit if confinement holds; no rigorous $N=3$ proof exists.

**Audit verdict at UQF-11D.** AUDIT-TIER: $\Sigma^{1/3}\approx
250$–$280$ MeV is measured on dynamical lattices and consistent with
Gell-Mann–Oakes–Renner; no Clay-grade certificate of chiral breaking
exists for $N=3$.

---

## 12.2 Wilsonian universality disclosure (UQF-11A,B,C,D)

A single Wilsonian observation governs why the framework's UV completion
does not, by itself, deliver an IR nonperturbative certificate.

Below $m_{\rm KK}=1/R\sim M_{\rm GUT}$, the 4D effective theory recovered
by Paper 2's strong-sector projection is *exactly* $SU(3)$ Yang–Mills
coupled to the framework's matter content. The KK tower is gapped at a
scale $\sim 10^{16}$ GeV; it decouples logarithmically from any IR
observable at scales $\sqrt{\sigma}^{-1}\sim 0.45$ fm $\sim 200$ MeV
where the area law and the mass gap are generated. By Wilson's
renormalization-group reasoning, the IR nonperturbative dynamics of a
gauge theory are essentially indifferent to the precise UV completion as
long as that completion (i) preserves the gauge group, (ii) preserves
the matter content's color charges, (iii) preserves anomaly freedom,
and (iv) leaves no light states between the UV scale and the IR scale
that would couple non-trivially to color-singlet correlators.

The Paper 2 strong-sector interface satisfies (i)–(iv) by construction.
Therefore the 13D framework's UV completion is *compatible* with any
future IR certificate (UQF-11A, B, C, or D), but is structurally unable
to supply one. This is the same structural disclosure that every
mainstream UV-completion programme (SUSY-GUT, technicolor, asymptotic
safety, string compactifications) carries, for the same Wilsonian
reason. The 13D framework inherits IR confinement, mass gap, hadron
spectrum, and chiral-symmetry breaking in the same way these
programmes do; the IR certificate question is the *same* open question
for all of them.

This disclosure is the load-bearing reason why UQF-11 lands at
AUDIT-TIER and not at CERTIFICATE-TIER. A reviewer who looks at the
strong-sector projection in Paper 2 and asks "does Paper 3 use this to
derive confinement?" should find this paragraph; the answer is no, and
the structural reason is Wilsonian universality.

---

## 12.3 UQF-11A audit — Wilson-loop area law

This audit row asks whether confinement (a Wilson-loop area law) holds for the descended $SU(3)_c$ theory. It is an AUDIT row: the geometry supplies the gauge group and matter content, but the area law is a nonperturbative statement that only lattice QCD or a Yang-Mills mass-gap proof can settle. The subsection records the current lattice status and the named partner-community route, not a closure.

### 12.3.1 Lattice status

For pure $SU(3)$ gauge theory on a Euclidean lattice in the confining
phase, the rectangular Wilson loop $W(R,T)$ at large $R,T$ obeys

$$
\langle W(R,T)\rangle\;\sim\;
\exp\!\bigl[-\sigma\,RT + p(R+T) + c + \mathcal{O}(1/RT)\bigr],
$$

where $\sigma\approx (440\,\text{MeV})^2$ is the string tension,
$p$ is the perimeter coefficient, $c$ is a constant. Bali, Schilling &
Wachter (1995) and successor measurements at BMW, RBC/UKQCD, MILC,
HotQCD have demonstrated the area law numerically to high precision.
String-breaking at $R\sim 1.2$ fm on dynamical-fermion ensembles is
seen at $N_f=2$, $2+1$, $2+1+1$. The continuum extrapolation
$a\to 0$ is controlled at the percent level under Symanzik improvement
(Lüscher–Weisz, Alpha Collaboration). None of this is a constructive
QFT proof of the area law on $\mathbb{R}^4$.

### 12.3.2 Analytic state of the art (candidate routes)

The three current best candidates are (i) the dual-superconductor /
't Hooft–Mandelstam picture (magnetic-monopole condensation; abelian
projection); (ii) center-vortex condensation (Greensite and
collaborators; $Z_3$ center vortices on maximally center-gauge-fixed
lattices reproduce the area law); (iii) generalized-symmetry /
mixed-anomaly approaches (Gaiotto–Kapustin–Komargodski–Seiberg and
follow-ups; the one-form $Z_3$ center symmetry and its mixed anomalies
sharpen the *necessity* of confining features but do not constructively
prove confinement at $N=3$ on $\mathbb{R}^4$).

### 12.3.3 13D compatibility statement

Paper 2 §7 routes $SU(3)_c$ as the isometry group of
$K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$ and the eight gluons as Killing-vector zero modes.
The 4D effective gauge theory below $m_{\rm KK}$ is exactly $SU(3)$
Yang–Mills coupled to the three-generation matter content. By the
Wilsonian disclosure of §12.2, the area law in the IR is inherited if a
future construction proves it; the framework supplies no new analytic
handle on the proof itself.

### 12.3.4 Genuinely open

Whether the spin-c bundle data on $K_6$ — with its specific holonomy
phase $\Phi=-0.12827$ rad inherited from the active branch — places an
*additional* topological constraint on the IR center-symmetry sector
that could feed into a center-vortex or mixed-anomaly argument is, to
our knowledge, an unexamined question. This is named in §12.9 as
research item R4 and is **not** claimed as a result here.

---

## 12.4 UQF-11B audit — Mass gap

This audit row asks whether the descended $SU(3)_c$ theory has a mass gap — the Clay Millennium problem in its physical form. It is AUDIT, and explicitly so: the paper claims a *route* and *compatibility* with the $K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$ structure, not a proof. The subsection records the lattice evidence for a gap and the open mathematical statement that would close it.

### 12.4.1 Lattice status

The pure-glue spectrum has a lightest $0^{++}$ glueball at
$m_{0^{++}}\approx 1.7$ GeV (Chen et al. 2006; Athenodorou & Teper
2020); higher-spin and higher-mass glueballs are computed to the
few-percent level. In the full $N_f=2+1$ theory the lightest physical
state is the pion at $m_\pi\approx 135$ MeV, which is a pseudo-Nambu-
Goldstone boson of spontaneously broken chiral $SU(2)_L\times SU(2)_R$
and is *not* a manifestation of the pure-glue mass gap; its nonzero
mass tracks the explicit chiral-symmetry breaking from $m_u+m_d$ via
the Gell-Mann–Oakes–Renner relation.

### 12.4.2 What a CERTIFICATE-tier UQF-11B gate would require

The Clay statement requires a constructive proof for pure $SU(N)$
Yang–Mills theory on $\mathbb{R}^4$ that the quantum theory exists in
the Osterwalder–Schrader sense, the Hamiltonian spectrum lies in
$\{0\}\cup[\Delta,\infty)$ for some $\Delta>0$, and the vacuum is
unique. The minimum-practical version recommended in the handoff §9 —
which is what we treat as the operational CERTIFICATE-tier threshold
for UQF-11B in Paper 3 — is a *frozen nonperturbative certificate*
under a declared regulator and a controlled continuum extrapolation,
exhibiting a positive lowest glueball or hadronic gap that survives all
named systematics. This minimum-practical certificate is the lattice
state of the art and is at percent-level precision in many channels;
it is, however, not the full mathematical certificate.

### 12.4.3 Current best constructive approaches (none complete)

- **Lattice-rigorous constructions** (Magnen–Rivasseau–Sénéor;
  Bałaban's RG): rigorous control of the lattice continuum limit
  exists for abelian gauge theory in $d\le 4$ and for
  super-renormalizable scalar models; for non-abelian $d=4$ no
  rigorous continuum limit has been completed.
- **Functional / exact-renormalization-group** (Pawlowski, Wetterich,
  Litim, Reuter): truncated FRG flows in pure-glue $SU(N)$ exhibit a
  non-trivial Landau-pole resolution and an apparent positive gap;
  truncation systematics are not eliminable in the current state of
  the art.
- **Stochastic quantization / regularity structures** (Parisi–Wu,
  Hairer 2014, Gubinelli–Imkeller–Perkowski 2015): rigorous results
  for $\Phi^4_3$ are now in hand; 4D Yang–Mills remains outside the
  constructive reach of these methods.
- **Algebraic / Wightman axiomatic** (Buchholz, Fredenhagen, Rehren):
  produces structural results but no Yang–Mills existence theorem.
- **Holographic** (AdS/CFT; Klebanov–Strassler; Witten thermal $AdS$):
  produces gap-like behaviour for the large-$N$ planar sector in
  specific confining backgrounds; this is not a proof for $SU(3)$ on
  $\mathbb{R}^4$ at $N=3$.

### 12.4.4 13D compatibility statement

The 13D compactification gives rise to a 4D effective $SU(3)$
Yang–Mills theory whose UV completion contains a tower of KK gauge
bosons starting at $m_{\rm KK}\sim M_{\rm GUT}$. *If* a mass-gap
certificate were established for pure-glue $SU(3)$ on $\mathbb{R}^4$,
the 13D framework would be consistent with it trivially: the KK tower
is gapped by construction at $\sim 10^{16}$ GeV, well above any
nonperturbative IR scale, and the zero-mode sector *is* the pure-glue
$SU(3)$ theory plus the framework's matter content. The framework does
**not** provide a new path to the certificate; it does not obstruct
any existing path.

### 12.4.5 Genuinely open

Whether the spin-c boundary data on $K_6$ imposes a non-trivial
boundary condition on the Faddeev–Popov / BRST sector at the matching
scale, that any future constructive proof would have to be checked
against, is open. The framework's anomaly-cancellation results
(Paper 2 §7) and its holonomy-phase structure ($\Phi=-0.12827$ rad)
are the candidate boundary data; whether they are inert with respect
to a Yang–Mills constructive proof is unexamined. (§12.9 item R4.)

---

## 12.5 UQF-11C audit — Hadron-spectrum route

This audit row specifies what a hadron-spectrum computation would require to confront the framework with the observed meson and baryon masses. It is deliberately a *route specification*, not a computation: the subsection names the inputs, the lattice or partner-community toolchain, and the comparison data, so that "AUDIT" here is an executable work order rather than a gap.

### 12.5.1 Route specification (not a full computation)

The route from the 4D effective $SU(3)$ Yang–Mills + light-quark theory
of Paper 2 to the observed hadron spectrum is:

1. **Quark and gluon field content.** Inherit the Weyl-fermion content
   from Paper 2 §7.12 (matter ledger). The low-energy QCD action may
   use Dirac quarks $q_f$; the anomaly ledger uses left-handed Weyl
   fields. These are notation changes, not spectrum changes.
2. **Color-singlet operator basis.** Build the standard nonperturbative
   color-singlet operators: $\bar q\gamma^\mu q$ for vector mesons,
   $\bar q\gamma^5 q$ for pseudoscalars, $\bar q q$ for scalars,
   baryon trilinears $\epsilon_{abc}q^aq^bq^c$ for baryons, glueball
   composite operators $\text{tr}\,F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}$ etc. for
   pure-glue states.
3. **Nonperturbative correlator definitions.** Define Euclidean
   two-point functions
   $C_{\mathcal O}(t) = \langle \mathcal O(t)\mathcal O^\dagger(0)\rangle$
   for each operator $\mathcal O$, with frozen regulator (lattice
   spacing $a$; quark-action choice — Wilson, staggered, domain-wall,
   overlap — declared).
4. **Mass extraction.** Extract $m_{\mathcal O}$ from the asymptotic
   exponential decay $C_{\mathcal O}(t)\to Z e^{-m_{\mathcal O}t}$ at
   large Euclidean $t$, with controlled excited-state contamination via
   variational basis methods (GEVP, Hadron Spectrum Collaboration).
5. **Continuum and infinite-volume extrapolation.** Symanzik
   improvement; $a\to 0$ and $L\to\infty$ extrapolations; controlled
   systematics per FLAG averaging.
6. **Comparison to PDG.** Mass ratios such as $m_p$, $m_\Omega/m_N$,
   $m_\pi$, $m_K$, $m_\rho$, etc., compared to PDG within stated
   systematic budgets.

### 12.5.2 Lattice state of the art

Modern dynamical lattice calculations with $N_f=2+1$ or $2+1+1$
flavors, with controlled continuum and infinite-volume extrapolations,
predict the light-hadron spectrum to better than 1% in many cases. The
BMW 2008 *Science* light-hadron mass calculation is the canonical
reference; FLAG averages 2019/2021/2024 provide updated bounds.
Charmonium and bottomonium spectra are reproduced to the few-MeV level.

### 12.5.3 13D compatibility statement

The hadron spectrum is entirely IR and is inherited from QCD. The
framework's contribution is upstream: the *input* quark masses and the
strong coupling $\alpha_3(M_Z)$ are framework-fixed (the latter from
$\mathrm{Vol}(K_6)$ at the UV matching scale; running with KK threshold
corrections to $M_Z$ yields $\alpha_3(M_Z)\approx 1/8.5$, consistent
with the PDG value $1/8.47\pm 0.05$); the lattice QCD calculation that
turns these into hadron masses is standard nonperturbative QCD. No
framework-specific prediction modifies a single hadron mass relative to
standard QCD with the same $\alpha_s$ and quark-mass inputs.

This is the relabeling-vs-derivation boundary that Paper 2 §7 already
named and accepted: Paper 2 is a *UV* completion at the interface
level; Paper 3 does not pretend that Paper 2's interface plus a UQF
gate stack derives the IR hadron spectrum. UQF-11C is at AUDIT-TIER for
this reason.

### 12.5.4 Framework-distinct hadronic predictions

Paper 2 §7.6 records the framework's distinct strong-sector predictions:
(i) gauge group $SU(3)_c$ from $K_6$ isometry; (ii) $g_3(M_{\rm GUT})$
from $\mathrm{Vol}(K_6)$; (iii) family count $N_g=3$ from the index
theorem; (iv) HC-1 / strong-CP postulate (the disclosed open issue —
see §13); (v) KK color-octet resonances at $m_2=(3/2)m_{\rm KK}$ and a
sextet at $m_3=\sqrt{10/3}\,m_{\rm KK}$. Item (v) is the only place in
the hadronic sector where the framework makes a distinct testable
prediction, and it lies far above current LHC reach; a future
multi-$10\,$TeV collider would be required to constrain it.

---

## 12.6 UQF-11D audit — Chiral-symmetry breaking

This audit row asks whether spontaneous chiral-symmetry breaking — the nonzero quark condensate that sets the pion as a pseudo-Goldstone boson — holds in the descended theory. Like the other UQF-11 sub-rows it is AUDIT: a nonperturbative phenomenon the geometry is compatible with but does not by itself prove. The subsection records the lattice status and the order parameter that settles it.

### 12.6.1 Lattice status

The chiral condensate, defined in the chiral limit $m_q\to 0$ as
$\langle\bar q q\rangle = -\Sigma$, is measured on dynamical lattices
to be

$$
\Sigma^{1/3}\;\approx\;250\text{–}280\,\text{MeV},
$$

equivalently $\langle\bar q q\rangle\approx -(250\,\text{MeV})^3$ to
$-(280\,\text{MeV})^3$ depending on scheme and scale (FLAG 2024
averages; BMW; JLQCD; RBC/UKQCD). The Gell-Mann–Oakes–Renner relation
$m_\pi^2 f_\pi^2 = -2m_q\langle\bar q q\rangle$ relates this to the
measured pion mass and decay constant $f_\pi\approx 92$ MeV at the
percent level. Chiral perturbation theory (Weinberg; Gasser–Leutwyler)
organizes the low-energy Goldstone-boson sector and is tested against
lattice and experimental data at the few-percent level.

### 12.6.2 Certificate-tier requirement

A rigorous proof that spontaneous chiral-symmetry breaking occurs in
the constructed 4D Yang–Mills + light-quark theory, with order
parameter $\Sigma>0$. The Coleman–Witten 1980 result is suggestive
(in the planar large-$N$ limit, chiral symmetry must break if quarks
are confined), but no rigorous $N=3$ proof exists.

### 12.6.3 13D compatibility statement

The 13D framework supplies the *fermion content* — three families of
quarks and leptons — by the index-theorem closure
($K_6$-Borel–Weil–Bott / spin-c index). The quark masses and CKM
mixing are machine-precision fitted from overlap integrals on $K_6$.
The chiral condensate magnitude itself is *not* computed in the
framework; $\Sigma$ is inherited from standard QCD nonperturbative
dynamics in the deep IR. Compatibility is at the level of "the
framework supplies the correct number of light flavors and the correct
quark mass hierarchy as input to the IR chiral dynamics; the
condensate is then standard, with GMOR closure."

### 12.6.4 Genuinely open

Whether the framework's flavor structure (in particular, the explicit
hierarchy $m_u:m_d:m_s:m_c:m_b:m_t$ fixed by overlap integrals)
imposes any *quantitative* constraint on the condensate beyond what
GMOR already supplies is not examined; GMOR is itself a low-energy
theorem and the framework does not improve on it. (§12.9 item R6.)

---

## 12.7 Summary-of-audit table

| Sub-gate | Element | Lattice status | Analytic / certificate status | 13D contribution | UQF-11 tier |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| UQF-11A | Wilson-loop area law $\langle W\rangle\sim e^{-\sigma A}$ | Numerically verified to high precision | No constructive proof; center-vortex / dual-superconductor circumstantial | Inheritance only; no new analytic handle | AUDIT |
| UQF-11A | Positive string tension $\sigma\approx(440\,\text{MeV})^2$ | Measured at percent level | No certificate (essentially the mass-gap problem) | UV coupling $g_3(M_{\rm GUT})$ from $\mathrm{Vol}(K_6)$ runs to consistent $\alpha_3(M_Z)$; $\sigma$ inherited | AUDIT |
| UQF-11B | Mass gap $\Delta>0$ | Glueball spectrum measured ($m_{0^{++}}\approx 1.7$ GeV) | Clay Millennium problem; no proof | None; framework is consistent with any future certificate | AUDIT |
| UQF-11C | Hadron-spectrum route | Sub-% on lattice for many channels | No constructive proof | Inheritance; route specified; framework-distinct prediction is KK color-octet at $(3/2)m_{\rm KK}$ | AUDIT |
| UQF-11D | Chiral condensate $\Sigma^{1/3}\approx 250$ MeV | Measured | No rigorous proof of $\chi$-SB at $N=3$ | Supplies fermion content + quark-mass hierarchy; $\Sigma$ inherited via GMOR | AUDIT |
| UQF-11 (overall) | Lattice-continuum bridge | Symanzik improvement; percent-level controlled | No rigorous $a\to 0$ for $4d$ Yang–Mills | None; inherits lattice technology | AUDIT |

**The audit table is what this section certifies.** No row in the
"13D contribution" column is upgraded to a derivation. Every row at
AUDIT-TIER is honest about what the framework supplies (UV boundary
data) and what it does not (an IR nonperturbative certificate).

---

## 12.8 The 13D-specific question — any structural simplification?

Is there *anything* about the geometric data
$(K_6 = SU(3)/T^2;\;\text{spin-c bundle};\;\Phi=-0.12827\,\text{rad};\;
\text{finite chamber structure})$
that offers a structural simplification of the Yang–Mills mass-gap
problem, the Wilson-loop area-law problem, or the chiral-condensate
problem?

**Honest answer: probably not, at the level of direct simplification.**
Paper 2's strong sector lives below $m_{\rm KK}\sim M_{\rm GUT}$ and is,
by construction, *the standard 4D $SU(3)$ Yang–Mills theory coupled to
the framework's three-generation matter content.* The IR nonperturbative
dynamics of that theory in the deep IR (MeV and below) is regimentally
indifferent to the UV boundary data; this is the Wilsonian universality
disclosure (§12.2).

**Named compatibility statements** (these *are* the legitimate
connection points; they are not derivations of nonperturbative results):

**C1. Anomaly cancellation closed at $N_g=3$, including the strong
sector.** Paper 2 §7.12 records that the cubic $SU(3)_c$ anomaly
vanishes vector-likely per generation, $A_{333}=0$ exactly. The
framework's $N_g=3$ output from the index theorem is *consistent* with
the anomaly-freedom requirement of the IR theory whose nonperturbative
completion is the open problem. This is a compatibility statement, not
a derivation of confinement.

**C2. Center-symmetry sector inheritance.** $SU(3)_c$ has center $Z_3$.
The framework, being a gauge construction with $SU(3)_c$ emerging as
the $K_6$ isometry, inherits the $Z_3$ center symmetry of the IR
theory. The 13D structure does not break the center symmetry. Hence
center-vortex / center-symmetry-based confinement mechanisms
(Greensite; Kanazawa–Suzuki; 't Hooft mixed-anomaly arguments) are
*not obstructed* by the framework. Whether the spin-c boundary data
*enriches* the center sector (e.g., via mixed anomalies with the
holonomy phase $\Phi$) is open and named in roadmap R4.

**C3. Strong-CP as a UV-imposed boundary.** §13 treats this in detail;
the brief statement here is that the framework demands $\bar\theta$ be
derivable from the geometric structure rather than tuned as a free IR
parameter. A future nonperturbative proof that $\bar\theta=0$ in the
QCD vacuum (or that an intrinsic PQ-like mechanism arises from the
spin-c / orbifold geometry) would close §13's open issue. This
*sharpens* (does not solve) the nonperturbative-QCD vacuum-structure
question.

**C4. Flavor content + quark-mass hierarchy as IR boundary conditions.**
The framework supplies the *input* fermion content and mass spectrum to
whichever IR-QCD calculation one runs. The chiral condensate $\Sigma$
is then sensitive to these inputs in the standard way (GMOR + lattice
with the framework's quark masses recovers the standard $\Sigma$).
This is consistency, not derivation.

**Nothing in C1–C4 is a confinement, mass-gap, or chiral-symmetry-
breaking proof.** Each is a compatibility statement between an open
nonperturbative problem and the UV boundary data the 13D framework
supplies.

### 12.8.1 Speculative spin-c / R4 roadmap item

The one place where the 13D framework itself contributes a candidate
*research question* (not a result) is the spin-c topological refinement
of confinement mechanisms. Does the spin-c bundle data on $K_6$ (with
$\Phi=-0.12827$ rad, and the specific finite-chamber projector
structure) impose any non-trivial mixed anomaly between $Z_3$ center
symmetry and the framework's holonomy or chamber structure? If yes,
this could conceivably feed into a Gaiotto–Kapustin–Komargodski–Seiberg-
style argument constraining the IR phase. This is named below as
roadmap item R4; it is **speculative** and **not** a result.

---

## 12.9 Research roadmap (5–15 years)

The roadmap names six research items (R1–R6), associates each with the
external collaborators most credibly positioned to work on them, and
labels each by approximate horizon and prior probability of producing
a certificate-tier UQF-11 closure. **No item is claimed as a
deliverable of the 13D framework alone**; each is a place where the
framework and the external nonperturbative-QCD programme would
interact.

**R1 — Continue lattice precision on the light-hadron spectrum and
$\alpha_s$.** Sub-percent in all channels by 2030–2035; high-precision
$\alpha_s$ extractions to $<0.5\%$. Decisive lattice collaborators:
**BMW** (Budapest–Marseille–Wuppertal), **RBC/UKQCD** (Brookhaven /
Edinburgh / KEK), **MILC** (US-Lattice / Argonne / Fermilab),
**HotQCD** (BNL / LBL), **Hadron Spectrum Collaboration** (JLab /
Trinity), **FLAG** (global lattice averages). *Horizon:* 5–10 years.
*Prior probability of incremental progress:* high. *Prior probability
of producing a Clay certificate directly:* near zero. *Framework role:*
provide UV-consistent $\alpha_3(M_Z)$ and quark-mass inputs; check
that lattice outputs remain consistent with framework predictions as
precision tightens — this is a hard observational constraint on the
framework, not on QCD.

**R2 — Analytic continuum confinement programmes.** Center-vortex
(Greensite, Faber, Olejnik); dual-superconductor / abelian-projection
(Suzuki, Di Giacomo, Bornyakov); generalized-symmetry / mixed-anomaly
(Gaiotto, Kapustin, Komargodski, Seiberg, Cordova); holographic
confining backgrounds at finite $N$ (Maldacena, Klebanov, Strassler,
Polchinski). *Horizon:* 5–15 years. *Prior probability of structural
results:* moderate. *Prior probability of a Clay certificate within
15 years:* low. *Framework role:* check that any new structural result
(e.g., a refined center-symmetry obstruction theorem) is consistent
with the spin-c boundary data. *No 13D-specific work is on this
critical path.*

**R3 — Functional / exact-renormalization-group programmes for
Yang–Mills mass gap.** Pawlowski, Wetterich, Litim, Reuter and
collaborators. *Horizon:* 5–10 years. *Prior probability of improving
the apparent-gap estimate:* moderate. *Prior probability of removing
the truncation systematic:* low. *Framework role:* if asymptotic
safety is established by ERG methods (relevant to UQF-9 in the
UV-completion gate, not UQF-11), the framework's UV scenario tightens;
the IR gap question remains separate.

**R4 — Spin-c / topological refinement of confinement mechanisms.**
The one item where the 13D framework itself contributes a candidate
research question. Does the spin-c bundle data on $K_6$ (with
$\Phi=-0.12827$ rad, and the specific finite-chamber projector
structure) impose any non-trivial mixed anomaly between $Z_3$ center
symmetry and the framework's holonomy or chamber structure? If yes,
this could conceivably feed into a Gaiotto–Kapustin–Komargodski–
Seiberg-style argument constraining the IR phase. *Horizon:* 10–15
years. *Prior probability:* **speculative** — this is a research
*question*, not a programme with current results. *Framework role:*
Chris does the physics (per the status-preservation rule —
investigation of this item must be done by direct calculation, not
asserted). *Plausible analytic collaborators if the question turns out
to be well-posed:* **Komargodski, Cordova, Gaiotto, Seiberg** (Stony
Brook / IAS), **Tachikawa** (Kavli IPMU).

**R5 — Discrete-chamber / lattice-regulator analogy.** The framework's
finite-chamber structure (chamber count in Lever-2 constructions) is
*not* a lattice regulator and is *not* offered as one. Whether any
partial analogy to a lattice regularization could be exploited as a
new path to a constructive Yang–Mills existence proof is
speculative-to-implausible; this item is named for completeness and is
**low-priority, high-risk** on the roadmap. *Horizon:* 10–15 years.
*Prior probability:* near zero. Named only to be transparent about
the space of possibilities the framework opens (and almost certainly
closes).

**R6 — Lattice with framework-specific inputs.** As $\alpha_s$ and
quark-mass inputs from the framework tighten (via overlap integrals
on $K_6$), lattice predictions for hadron observables become a sharp
consistency check. Any sub-percent disagreement between
framework-predicted inputs and lattice-extracted ones (after running
between scales) would falsify the framework. Existing FLAG averages
2024 are consistent at the few-percent level; FLAG 2030 / 2035 will
sharpen this. *Horizon:* 5–10 years. *Importance for framework
falsifiability:* high. *New contribution to the nonperturbative-QCD
certificate problem itself:* zero.

### 12.9.1 Experimental decisiveness summary

No collider experiment in the next 15 years will produce a Yang–Mills
mass-gap certificate or a confinement proof. The decisive experimental
tests that *do* exist are:

- Lattice QCD precision on $\alpha_s$, light-hadron masses, meson
  decay constants, chiral condensate, and $\bar\theta_{\rm QCD}$
  (R1, R6; see §13 for the $\bar\theta$ part).
- Neutron-EDM experiments (n2EDM at PSI, nEDM at SNS) tightening the
  bound on $\bar\theta_{\rm QCD}$, which directly stresses the
  framework's HC-1 postulate (§13).
- High-energy collider searches for KK color-octet resonances at
  $m\sim(3/2)m_{\rm KK}\sim 10^{16}$ GeV — far beyond foreseeable
  reach; this is not a near-term experimental test.

---

## 12.10 UQF-11 status line and downgrade map

**UQF-11A — Confinement / Wilson-loop area law:** *AUDIT-TIER*.
*Downgrade rule:* the strong interface inherits the lattice numerical
demonstration plus the named analytic-route audit; if a future
constructive proof appears, the framework slot for it is open; if no
proof appears within the strong-pass target horizon (Paper 3 revision
window), UQF-11A remains AUDIT and §12.7's compatibility statement is
the load-bearing claim.

**UQF-11B — Mass gap:** *AUDIT-TIER*. *Downgrade rule:* identical to
UQF-11A. The minimum-practical version (lattice + glueball spectrum
under declared regulator and controlled continuum extrapolation) is
inherited; the full Clay-grade certificate is the strong-pass target
for a future revision.

**UQF-11C — Hadron-spectrum route:** *AUDIT-TIER*. *Downgrade rule:*
the route specification is in hand; failure mode is that
framework-supplied UV inputs ($\alpha_3(M_Z)$, quark masses) drift
out of consistency with lattice extractions at sub-percent precision,
which would falsify the *framework*, not the QCD route. This is the
sharpest near-term falsification anchor of UQF-11.

**UQF-11D — Chiral symmetry breaking:** *AUDIT-TIER*. *Downgrade
rule:* the GMOR-consistent IR statement is inherited; failure mode is
the same as UQF-11C — framework-supplied quark masses drift out of
consistency with $\Sigma$ at sub-percent precision.

**UQF-11 (overall) — AUDIT-TIER.** Confinement and mass gap are
Millennium-Prize-class open problems and remain so within Paper 3's
audit envelope. Hadron-spectrum route and chiral symmetry breaking
are downstream and remain at AUDIT. The strong-pass target for a
future revision is the minimum-practical CERTIFICATE-tier closure of
UQF-11B (positive lowest gap under declared regulator and continuum
extrapolation) and a frozen lattice-vs-framework comparison closing
UQF-11C and UQF-11D at sub-percent. The full Clay-grade UQF-11A,B
certificate is **not** the strong-pass target for the Paper 3
revision; it is the multi-decade target across the entire community
nonperturbative-QCD programme.

# UQFC-13 — Strong CP Certificate (UQF-12)
*UQF-12 (strong CP — explain or eliminate $\bar\theta$) · gate UQF-12 · drafted 2026-06-08*

> **Gate card — UQF-12: Strong CP** *(auto-derived from §3.3 / §4.4, the single source of truth per §3.0; any discrepancy with this chapter is a drafting bug)*

The corpus default candidate is the $S^1_Y / \mathbb Z_2$ boundary-parity mechanism; the named fallback is a Peccei-Quinn axion (which requires additional geometric structure not present in the active branch as-inherited and is therefore a *fallback* not a *primary*). ## 13.0 Reviewer first-read for §13

This is the second of Paper 3's two honest-audit sections (the first
being §12, Nonperturbative QCD). UQF-12 asks whether the strong-CP
angle $\bar\theta$ — empirically bounded by neutron-EDM measurements
to $|\bar\theta|\lesssim 10^{-10}$ while being naturally $O(1)$
without a structural reason — can be explained or eliminated within
the 13D unified force-sector framework.

The honest answer, after audit, is that UQF-12 lands at **AUDIT-TIER
with LOW CONFIDENCE on the candidate mechanism**. The most promising
13D-internal candidate (the $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orbifold-boundary-
parity lead) is a *candidate inspection point*, not a derived
cancellation. The most compatible standard resolution if the
candidate fails is a Peccei–Quinn axion implemented as a second
pseudo-scalar mode on $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orthogonal to the Hosotani
Higgs mode (Path β); the naive geometric estimate of the PQ decay
constant $f_a$ from the existing $S^1_Y$ radius $R_Y$ puts $f_a$ in a
region that would require additional geometric structure, making Path
β *expensive* in 13D and leaving **Path γ (permanent exclusion at the
scope boundary)** as the most honest fallback if neither structural
cancellation nor a viable PQ-axion implementation can be obtained.

This section mirrors UQC-4 with Paper-3 vocabulary: states the
required certificate elements per handoff §10, audits standard
resolutions, performs a 13D-specific exploration of four candidate
levers, and lays out the Path α / Path β / Path γ decision branch. It
does **not** assert "strong CP is solved because the geometry is
elegant." It does **not** upgrade UQF-12 from AUDIT to CERTIFICATE.

The reader who wants the bottom line can skip to §13.7 (falsification
roadmap) and §13.9 (status line); the full audit proceeds linearly.

---

## 13.1 The problem restated and the certificate elements UQF-12 demands

This subsection restates the strong-CP problem precisely and lists what a genuine certificate for it would have to contain. The subsections fix the $\bar\theta$ angle and its empirical bound from the neutron electric dipole moment (§13.1.1) and then enumerate the certificate elements UQF-12 would demand — so that the candidate-and-falsifier posture of this chapter is measured against a clearly stated bar it does not claim to clear.

### 13.1.1 The strong-CP angle and the empirical bound

The renormalized strong-CP angle is

$$
\bar\theta \;=\; \theta_{\rm QCD} \;+\; \arg\det M_q
\;=\; \theta_{\rm QCD} \;+\; \arg\det(M_u M_d),
$$

where $\theta_{\rm QCD}$ is the coefficient of the $G\tilde G$
topological term in the QCD Lagrangian and $\arg\det(M_u M_d)$ is the
phase of the determinant of the up- and down-type quark mass matrices
after rotation to the canonical chiral basis. The neutron-EDM bound

$$
|d_n| \;<\; 1.8\times 10^{-26}\ e\!\cdot\!\text{cm}
\qquad (\text{nEDM Collaboration, 2020})
$$

translates to

$$
|\bar\theta| \;\lesssim\; 10^{-10}.
$$

Without a structural reason, $\bar\theta$ is naturally an $O(1)$
angle. Reducing it to $\le 10^{-10}$ by accident is a fine-tuning at
the level of ten orders of magnitude.

### 13.1.2 Certificate elements UQF-12 demands

Per the handoff §10, a certificate-tier UQF-12 closure must deliver
each of the following frozen, peer-checkable elements:

1. **Source of $\theta_{\rm QCD}$ identified.** The geometric or
   topological origin of the $G\tilde G$ coefficient in the 4D
   effective theory after dimensional reduction; named, frozen, and
   computable.
2. **Source of $\arg\det M_q$ identified.** The geometric origin of
   the quark-mass-matrix phase; in the 13D framework this routes
   through the spin-c connection holonomy $\Phi=-0.12827$ rad on
   $K_6$ and the Yukawa map produced by chamber overlap integrals
   (Paper 1 main manuscript; Article B §5.4).
3. **CKM phase remains nonzero.** The Jarlskog invariant $J$ must be
   reproduced at machine precision (PDG value); a cancellation of
   $\arg\det M_q$ that simultaneously kills $J$ is *not* a solution
   but a failure mode.
4. **$\bar\theta$ cancels or is suppressed.** $\bar\theta=
   \theta_{\rm QCD}+\arg\det(M_u M_d)\approx 0$ at the precision
   required by the nEDM bound.
5. **Radiative stability under loops.** The cancellation must survive
   loop corrections at the precision required by the bound — i.e., no
   counterterm enters at any loop order that would re-introduce a
   $\bar\theta$ contribution at $\gg 10^{-10}$.
6. **Neutron EDM below bound.** The predicted $|d_n|$ remains below
   the experimental bound at the certificate's stated precision; the
   prediction includes any structural shift of $\bar\theta$ from
   exactly zero.
7. **Falsifier.** A predicted EDM window (the certificate's prediction
   for the next-generation experiment, e.g., n2EDM at PSI), or a
   named failure condition that would falsify the candidate
   mechanism.

The best native route per handoff §10 is a **geometric / topological
cancellation of $\theta_{\rm QCD}$ against $\arg\det(M_u M_d)$**
internal to the 13D structure, such that elements (1)–(6) are
satisfied by the framework's geometry and (7) is a sharp prediction
the framework makes for an upcoming experiment.

### 13.1.3 Why this is honest-AUDIT and not yet CERTIFICATE

The audit below identifies a candidate inspection point for element
(4) — the $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orbifold-boundary parity, lead (d) of
§13.4 — but does not deliver a derived cancellation. Elements (5) and
(7) cannot be evaluated until (4) is closed. Elements (1)–(3) and (6)
are tracked in the framework with named cross-references. The
certificate cannot be issued at AUDIT-tier; the strong-pass target
for a future Paper 3 revision is precisely to close (4) by direct
calculation and to deliver (5)–(7) on the back of that closure.

---

## 13.2 What the 13D framework currently puts on the table

Article B §5.4 (the Paper-1 anchor for strong CP) records that the
spin-c connection's holonomy phase $\Phi=-0.12827$ rad generates a
contribution

$$
\delta(\arg\det M_d) \;=\; +1.64\,\text{rad}
$$

to $\bar\theta$. This 1.64-rad contribution is in approximately
ten-orders-of-magnitude tension with the nEDM bound. Article B does
**not** claim this contribution is the only one, nor that it is the
renormalized $\bar\theta$ — it states honestly that the unrenormalized
$\bar\theta$ requires a future theorem-level closure, named there as
one of three paths (Peccei–Quinn protection intrinsic to the spin-c
geometry; holonomy-phase pattern restructuring with $\arg\det=0$ but
$J\neq 0$; or non-perturbative cancellation via BV-BRST quantization).

This is also what makes the framework's strong-CP situation a
*constraint*, not a wash: a successful closure path must cancel a
specific 1.64-rad contribution with a specific structural mechanism,
not with an unfixed counterterm. The honest disclosure is that, as of
2026-06-08, no such structural mechanism has been derived; what
follows is the audit of where one might come from.

---

## 13.3 Audit of standard resolutions against the 13D framework

This subsection walks the established strong-CP resolutions and asks, for each, how it fares inside the 13D framework. The subsections take the Peccei–Quinn axion (§13.3.1), the massless-up-quark route, and the spontaneous-CP / Nelson–Barr class in turn, recording which remain available as fallbacks and which are constrained — the honest backdrop against which the $S^1_Y/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary-parity candidate is offered, not a claim that any is closed.

### 13.3.1 Peccei–Quinn axion

The Peccei–Quinn (PQ) mechanism postulates a global $U(1)_{\rm PQ}$
symmetry, broken spontaneously, whose pseudo-Nambu-Goldstone boson —
the axion — couples to $G\tilde G$ via an anomaly and dynamically
relaxes $\bar\theta$ to zero at the QCD minimum, leaving mass
$m_a\sim\Lambda_{\rm QCD}^2/f_a$ and decay constant $f_a$ probed by
ABRACADABRA, ADMX, IAXO, MADMAX, and CASPEr.

**13D compatibility audit.** The framework contains a $U(1)$-active
$S^1_Y$ with $\mathbb{Z}_2$ orbifold quotient $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$.
The $S^1_Y$ sector is already committed to $U(1)_Y$ hypercharge; it
is *not* free to also serve as a PQ axion sector without further
structure. Three sub-questions: (a) the parent $S^1_Y$ Wilson line
$\theta_H$ already forms the Hosotani Higgs pseudo-scalar with
gauge-symmetrically-pinned potential — a PQ axion would have to be a
*second* pseudo-scalar on $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orthogonal to it, not
the Higgs mode; (b) $K_6=SU(3)/T^2$ has no free $U(1)$ — the $T^2$
Cartan is quotiented, the residual $SU(3)$ becomes $SU(3)_c$, and
$\tau=\omega$ is pinned; (c) the $\oplus$-layer $F^+$ chamber has no
free phase — $\theta_F$ is pinned by $|V_{us}|=0.22436$.

**Verdict.** The most natural PQ-style mode in 13D would be a
*second* pseudo-scalar on $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orthogonal to the
Hosotani Higgs mode. The geometry does not currently isolate one but
does not forbid one. A future certificate would need (i) the
orthogonal mode at the spectral level, (ii) correct-sign coupling to
$G\tilde G$ via spin-c anomaly inflow, (iii) $f_a$ from $R_Y$ in an
experimentally allowed window, and (iv) consistency with current
ABRACADABRA / ADMX / IAXO / MADMAX / CASPEr bounds. This is Article
B §10.5 Theorem Target #5.

### 13.3.2 Nelson–Barr / spontaneous CP

Nelson–Barr models impose CP as a fundamental symmetry of the
Lagrangian and break it spontaneously by VEVs at a high scale, with
field content chosen so the resulting $\arg\det M_q$ vanishes at tree
level. The Jarlskog $J$ is generated by loop-induced mixings.

**13D compatibility audit.** The 13D framework's holonomy phase
$\Phi=-0.12827$ rad is generated by the *canonical* spin-c connection
$\omega^{(1,0)}$ on $K_6$ — it is structural, not a VEV. There is no
scalar field whose VEV generates this phase, so it cannot be "rotated
to a spontaneous-CP-breaking VEV" in the Nelson–Barr sense. CP is
broken *geometrically* in 13D, not via a CP-symmetric Lagrangian with
spontaneous breaking. The standard Nelson–Barr mechanism does not
directly map onto the 13D structure.

**A weaker, structurally compatible version.** What 13D *can* host is
a "geometric Nelson–Barr": a structural cancellation in which the
spin-c holonomy contributes to $\arg\det M_q$ exactly oppositely to
$\theta_{\rm QCD}$, so the sum $\bar\theta$ vanishes by construction.
This is precisely Article B §5.4 closure path (b): "holonomy-phase
pattern restructuring such that $\arg\det$ vanishes while $J$ remains
nonzero." The 1.64-rad contribution from the current spin-c
connection would need to be re-examined under any pattern
restructuring; the cross-sector tie in Article B §8.2 (same
$\omega^{(1,0)}$ generates both CKM Jarlskog $J$ and the strong-CP
shift) constrains how that restructuring can proceed.

### 13.3.3 Massless up quark

A massless up quark would make $\arg\det M_q$ trivially zero (the
determinant vanishes) and absorb $\theta_{\rm QCD}$ into the
unphysical phase. **Excluded by lattice QCD.** Current lattice
determinations give $m_u\approx 2.16\pm 0.07$ MeV (FLAG 2021); a
massless up quark is ruled out at very high confidence. The 13D
framework's quark certificate produces a nonzero $m_u$ from the
chamber operator $O_u$. This resolution is not available in 13D or
elsewhere.

### 13.3.4 Fine-tuning / anthropic

If $\bar\theta$ is simply small by coincidence, then either we live in
an atypical patch of a multiverse (anthropic selection: large
$\bar\theta$ gives a large neutron EDM that would disrupt nuclear
physics, baryosynthesis, or BBN in ways that preclude observers), or
there is a yet-unknown UV principle that selects small $\bar\theta$
from a high-dimensional landscape. This is outside the scope of
UQF-12 — it is a metaphysical posture, not a structural mechanism in
the 13D framework.

We note for completeness that the 13D framework's bias is *against*
anthropic explanations where a structural one is available: the SoT's
whole architecture is to convert free parameters into structural
constraints (three families from a Borel–Weil–Bott index,
$\sin^2\theta_W$ from $K_6\times S^2\times S^1_Y$ isometries, gauge
couplings from $\mathrm{Vol}(K_6)$, etc.). A 13D-internal mechanism,
if one exists, would be strongly preferred on this stylistic ground.

---

## 13.4 13D-specific exploration — the four candidate levers

We examine whether any of the four 13D structural elements naturally
constrain $\bar\theta$: (a) $K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$ quotient structure;
(b) finite chamber projectors in the $\oplus$ layer; (c) $S^2$ spin
cover; (d) $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity.

### 13.4.1 (a) $K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$ Weyl-orbit holonomy parity

$K_6$ is the flag manifold with the Weyl-rigid chamber
$\vec u\in[1/2,3/2]^3$. The $T^2$ Cartan is quotiented; the residual
$SU(3)$ becomes $SU(3)_c$. The Weyl group $W(SU(3))=S_3$ acts on the
chamber $\vec u=(u_1,u_2,u_3)$ by permutation.

The operative question is whether the spin-c holonomy phase
$\Phi(\vec u)$ has a Weyl-odd component while $\arg\det M_q$ depends
on a Weyl-*even* combination of chamber data. If so, averaging over
Weyl orbits could *in principle* cancel $\arg\det M_q$ while
preserving the Jarlskog $J$ (which is structurally a Weyl-even
invariant of the CKM matrix).

**Audit.** The index theorem on $K_6$ delivers the family count
$\mathrm{ind}=-3$. The same spin-c connection delivers
$\Phi=-0.12827$ rad. Article B §8.2 cross-sector consistency uses the
same $\omega^{(1,0)}$ in both the CKM Jarlskog and the strong-CP
shift. This is a constraint, not a freedom: any holonomy-pattern
restructuring that cancels $\arg\det M_q$ must preserve $J$. Whether
the requisite Weyl-parity assignment is available on the Weyl-rigid
chamber is the operative open question.

**Status of lead (a).** *Candidate inspection point — not a
derivation.* Requires a Chris-level physics calculation: parity
assignments of $\Phi(\vec u)$ and of the diagonal entries of
$O_u,O_d$ under $W(SU(3))$, plus a check of whether Weyl-orbit
averaging is required by chamber-rigidity or merely permitted.

### 13.4.2 (b) Finite chamber projectors in the $\oplus$ layer

The $F^+$ chamber is in the $\oplus$ layer with key objects: the
Cartan-torus modulus $\tau=\omega$ (cube root of unity), the sector
projectors $\Pi_u,\Pi_d,\Pi_e,\Pi_\nu$ (orthogonal, rank-3 each), the
chamber operators $O_u,O_d,O_e,O_\nu$ (diagonal in the canonical
chamber basis at $\tau=\omega$), and the chamber angle $\theta_F$
(pinned by $|V_{us}|=0.22436$).

**Audit for $\arg\det$ contribution.** The determinant of a sector
chamber operator at $\tau=\omega$ takes the form

$$
\det O_q \;=\; \prod_{a=1}^{3} e^{-a_q^{(a)}\pi\sqrt 3},
$$

so $\arg\det O_q$ depends on the *imaginary* parts (if any) of the
exponents $a_q^{(a)}$. At $\tau=\omega$, the exponents factor as
$-a_q^{(a)}\pi\sqrt 3$ — *real* in the canonical chamber. The phase
contribution to $\arg\det O_q$ from the chamber operators themselves
vanishes by construction at $\tau=\omega$.

This is a structurally interesting observation: **the chamber's
choice of $\tau=\omega$ already eliminates one source of $\arg\det$
phase contamination.** The residual $\arg\det M_q$ contribution comes
from the species normalizations $N_q$, the rotation angle $\theta_F$
(real in the DFT-on-$\mathbb{Z}_3$ basis), and the spin-c connection
holonomy $\Phi$ entering through the Yukawa-map procedure.

**Status of lead (b).** *Partial structural constraint already in
place.* The $\tau=\omega$ pinning is a frozen object; it removes a
class of $\arg\det$ contributions from the chamber operators
themselves. The remaining nonzero contribution comes from $\Phi$ via
the Yukawa map. A more careful audit is needed to determine whether
the $\Phi$ contribution can be eliminated by a chamber-internal
redefinition that preserves the Jarlskog. This is, again, Article B
§5.4 closure path (b).

### 13.4.3 (c) $S^2$ spin cover

$S^2$ is the round 2-sphere carrying $SU(2)_L$. The principal
$SU(2)_L$ bundle on $S^2$ is frozen. $S^2$ contributes to the weak
sector; it does not carry color. Its relevance to strong CP is
*indirect*: the $S^2$ spin structure controls the chirality projector
$P_\chi$ entering the chiral redefinition that produces $\arg\det
M_q$.

**Audit.** The chirality projector $P_\chi$ acts on the spinor tensor
product $S(K_6)\otimes S(S^2)\otimes S(S^1_Y)$. The $S^2$ factor
contributes a sign in the projector's eigenvalue assignment via the
spin-c structure on $S^2$. If the $S^2$ spin structure forces a
specific chirality on the active matter sector that aligns with the
spin-c connection's holonomy in a way that cancels the contribution
to $\arg\det M_q$, then $S^2$ would be a non-trivial structural
contributor.

**Status of lead (c).** *Indirect; subordinate to the $K_6$
holonomy.* The $S^2$ spin structure does not appear to be the primary
lever. Its role is to project the chirality consistently with the
$K_6$ family index. A standalone $S^2$-driven mechanism does not
present itself in this audit; the $S^2$ contribution is best read as
part of the joint $S(K_6)\otimes S(S^2)\otimes S(S^1_Y)$ chirality
structure that closure path (b) would need to restructure.

### 13.4.4 (d) $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity — the most promising lead

The $\mathbb{Z}_2$ orbifold action $\theta\mapsto -\theta$ on $S^1_Y$
has fixed points at $\theta\in\{0,\pi\}$. The boundary parity table
assigns parities to each SM field at the two fixed points; this is
what removes mirror partners and generates the chiral spectrum.

**Audit for $\bar\theta$ relevance.** The orbifold action
$\theta\mapsto -\theta$ is a *discrete* symmetry. Discrete symmetries
can suppress $\bar\theta$ in a way analogous to Nelson–Barr — if the
boundary parity is sufficiently restrictive to force a real
determinant structure on the Yukawa map. The key question: does the
boundary parity at $\theta=0$ and $\theta=\pi$, taken jointly with
the chirality projector $P_\chi$, restrict the Yukawa map to a form
in which $\arg\det M_q$ is forced to a specific value (zero, $\pi$,
or another fixed phase) by parity rather than by tuning?

This is the most promising of the four leads in the author's
reading. The $\mathbb{Z}_2$ orbifold parity is a *true* discrete
symmetry of the active geometry (frozen object), and it is known to
play a role in the chiral structure. It is plausible — but not
currently demonstrated — that the parity action propagates to a
parity constraint on the chiral redefinition that generates
$\arg\det M_q$.

**Status of lead (d).** ***Candidate structural mechanism — most
promising of the four.*** Requires:

1. A direct check that the orbifold parity $\theta\mapsto -\theta$ on
   $S^1_Y$ propagates to a CP-like parity action on the Yukawa map
   after dimensional reduction.
2. A determination of whether that parity forces $\arg\det M_q$ to
   zero (or a value cancelling $\theta_{\rm QCD}$) at the structural
   level, or merely restricts it to a smaller-but-still-tunable set.
3. A cross-check that any forced cancellation is consistent with the
   CKM Jarlskog $J$ (Article B §8.2) — i.e., the parity cancels
   $\arg\det$ without zeroing $J$.

If the orbifold parity passes (1)–(3), then 13D has a
discrete-symmetry strong-CP solution structurally analogous to
Nelson–Barr, with the discrete symmetry being the *orbifold parity
itself*, not an imposed CP. If it fails, then 13D needs either an
axion-like second pseudo-scalar mode on $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$
(§13.3.1) or a chamber restructuring (§13.3.2 / §13.4.1).

### 13.4.5 Summary table of the four leads

| Lead | Status | Mechanism class | Falsification |
|---|---|---|---|
| (a) $K_6$ Weyl-orbit holonomy parity | Inspection point | Geometric Nelson–Barr | No Weyl-odd component of $\Phi$ that cancels $\arg\det$ |
| (b) $F^+$ chamber $\tau=\omega$ pinning | **Partial structural constraint in place** | Removes chamber-operator $\arg\det$ phases | (Already on the books; not a *full* resolution) |
| (c) $S^2$ spin cover | Subordinate to (a) | Indirect via $P_\chi$ | No standalone mechanism |
| (d) $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity | **Most promising candidate** | Discrete symmetry / orbifold-induced Nelson–Barr | Parity does not propagate to a $\arg\det M_q$ constraint, or it propagates but kills $J$ |

**Most compatible standard resolution if no candidate succeeds.** If
leads (a) and (d) both fail to deliver structural cancellation, the
most compatible fallback is a Peccei–Quinn axion implemented as a
second pseudo-scalar mode on $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orthogonal to the
Hosotani Higgs mode (§13.3.1). The $S^1$ sector is the only place in
the 13D structure where a free $U(1)$ phase could host a PQ
symmetry, and the orbifold quotient is already in active use. The
discrete-symmetry path (Nelson–Barr) is *less* compatible without
lead (d) because the 13D framework breaks CP geometrically rather
than via Lagrangian-symmetric scalar VEVs.

---

## 13.5 UQF-12 certificate-element scorecard

For each of the seven certificate elements demanded by handoff §10,
we record current status under the best 13D candidate (lead (d) of
§13.4) and under the Path-β PQ-axion fallback (§13.3.1).

| Element | Best 13D candidate (lead (d)) | Path β (PQ axion on $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$) | Tier |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1. Source of $\theta_{\rm QCD}$ identified | Inherited from Paper 2 strong-sector $G\tilde G$ term; geometric origin pending closure | Identified; PQ relaxation handles the $\theta_{\rm QCD}$ piece dynamically | AUDIT |
| 2. Source of $\arg\det M_q$ identified | Spin-c connection holonomy $\Phi=-0.12827$ rad on $K_6$; chamber overlap integrals | Same as left column; PQ does not need to identify it, only to relax the sum | AUDIT |
| 3. CKM phase $J$ remains nonzero | Cross-check required (§13.4.4 step 3); $J$ at PDG machine precision is the hard constraint | Trivially satisfied; PQ does not touch $J$ | AUDIT (cross-check pending) |
| 4. $\bar\theta$ cancels / suppresses | Candidate mechanism: discrete orbifold parity propagates to $\arg\det M_q$ constraint; *not* demonstrated | Dynamically; standard PQ relaxation to $\bar\theta\to 0$ at QCD minimum | AUDIT (LOW CONFIDENCE on (d); HIGH CONFIDENCE on Path β *if* the second pseudo-scalar mode exists) |
| 5. Radiative stability under loops | Untested; requires (4) to be closed first | Standard for the PQ mechanism; quality-of-PQ problem under gravity is a known caveat | AUDIT |
| 6. Neutron EDM $|d_n|$ below bound | Inherited if (4) closes; predicted shift TBD | Inherited; PQ predicts $|d_n|$ at the small-but-nonzero level set by residual misalignment | AUDIT |
| 7. Falsifier | Improved $|\bar\theta|$ bound from n2EDM / nEDM at SNS finding a nonzero $\bar\theta$ at the structural level would falsify the cancellation mechanism | Axion mass / coupling in ABRACADABRA, ADMX, IAXO, MADMAX, CASPEr; if $f_a$ from the geometric estimate ends up in an experimentally excluded window, Path β is ruled out | AUDIT |

**Verdict on the scorecard.** No row passes at CERTIFICATE-tier. Two
rows ((1), (2)) are at AUDIT because they identify the relevant
geometric inputs; one row ((3)) is at AUDIT pending cross-check;
three rows ((4)–(6)) are at AUDIT because the candidate mechanism is
not yet a derivation; one row ((7)) is at AUDIT with named
experimental hooks ready to fire if the candidate or PQ-axion path
locks in. UQF-12 therefore lands at AUDIT-TIER with LOW CONFIDENCE
on the candidate mechanism for element (4); the cross-sector tie
between $\arg\det M_q$ and the CKM Jarlskog (Article B §8.2) is the
sharpest constraint any successful closure must respect.

---

## 13.6 The Path-β arithmetic — why PQ is not free in 13D

A specific arithmetic disclosure on Path β is required to be honest
about what 13D offers as a PQ axion fallback.

The PQ decay constant $f_a$ is set, in the standard Kaluza–Klein /
Hosotani idiom, by the inverse radius of the $S^1$ sector hosting
the PQ pseudo-scalar mode. The 13D framework's existing
$R_Y\sim(5/\pi)\times 10^{-17}$ GeV$^{-1}$ implies, at the naive
Hosotani estimate $f_a\sim 1/R_Y$, $f_a\sim 10^{17}$ GeV — *very
large*, corresponding to an ultralight axion of mass
$m_a\sim\Lambda_{\rm QCD}^2/f_a\sim 10^{-10}$ eV, in the regime
probed by CASPEr and certain ABRACADABRA channels (with cosmological
misalignment and SN1987A / white-dwarf bounds further restricting
the window). A more careful Hosotani computation may shift this by
an $O(1)$ factor; the order-of-magnitude conclusion is what we
record.

The unfavorable case for Path β arises if a careful computation puts
$f_a$ in an experimentally excluded window. Then Path β would
require a *new* $S^1$ factor with a different radius, dedicated to
PQ — i.e., a non-trivial geometric addition to the 13D framework.
This makes Path β *expensive*: not a free fallback. If the careful
$f_a$ computation lands in an excluded window, Path γ (permanent
exclusion at the UQF-12 gate) becomes the honest fallback. The
careful Hosotani arithmetic check is itself a Chris-level physics
task and is named below as part of Phase 2 of the research roadmap.

---

## 13.7 Falsification roadmap and decision branch

A genuine 13D strong-CP closure attempt (which is *not* what this
section is) would proceed in three phases.

### 13.7.1 Phase 1 — Structural audit (3–6 months, Chris-level physics)

(i) Compute the Weyl-group parity of $\Phi(\vec u)$ on the
Weyl-rigid chamber. Determine whether a Weyl-odd component exists.

(ii) Compute the action of the $\mathbb{Z}_2$ orbifold parity on the
Yukawa map after dimensional reduction. Determine whether the parity
forces $\arg\det M_q$ to a specific value.

(iii) Audit the joint $S(K_6)\otimes S(S^2)\otimes S(S^1_Y)$
chirality structure for additional discrete constraints on
$\arg\det M_q$.

(iv) Cross-check each candidate constraint against the CKM Jarlskog
$J$ to ensure $J$ is not zeroed.

### 13.7.2 Phase 2 — Decision branch

Based on Phase 1:

- **Path α (structural cancellation found):** Write a strong-CP
  certificate. The certificate must (i) state the structural
  mechanism (Weyl-parity / orbifold-parity / chirality), (ii) compute
  the residual $\bar\theta$ after cancellation, (iii) verify
  $|\bar\theta|<10^{-10}$ at the certificate's stated precision,
  (iv) verify $J$ is preserved at machine precision, (v) demonstrate
  radiative stability under loops, (vi) name a falsifier (predicted
  EDM window or failure condition). This certificate would move
  strong CP from AUDIT to CERTIFICATE at UQF-12.

- **Path β (no structural cancellation; PQ axion needed):** Identify
  the second pseudo-scalar mode on $S^1_Y/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orthogonal
  to the Hosotani Higgs mode. Compute $f_a$ at the careful Hosotani
  level (per §13.6). Compute the axion mass $m_a\sim
  \Lambda_{\rm QCD}^2/f_a$ and check against the
  ABRACADABRA / ADMX / IAXO / MADMAX / CASPEr windows. If $f_a$ is
  in an allowed window, write the Path-β certificate; if $f_a$ is
  in an excluded window, Path β fails and Path γ is invoked.

- **Path γ (no structural cancellation, no viable PQ axion):** Strong
  CP remains permanently excluded from the Paper-3 force-sector
  claim at the UQF-12 gate. UQF-12 is honestly downgraded to AUDIT
  with the named obstruction. The Paper-3 claim is a
  *unified-quantum-force-completion candidate*, not a TOE, and the
  scope boundary correctly applies. Honesty preserved; no
  fabrication.

### 13.7.3 Phase 3 — Experimental falsification path

Experimental anchors independent of which closure path is pursued:

- **n2EDM** (PSI, 2025+): improvement of $|\bar\theta|$ bound to
  $\le 10^{-11}$. A nonzero $\bar\theta$ at this level falsifies the
  Path-α structural cancellation.
- **nEDM at SNS** (ORNL, ~2027+): independent
  sub-$10^{-27}\,e\!\cdot\!$cm reach.
- **ABRACADABRA / ADMX / IAXO / MADMAX / CASPEr** — axion-search
  landscape across $10^{-22}$–$10^0$ eV. If Path β is invoked and
  the careful Hosotani $f_a$ computation locks the axion mass into
  one of these windows, the prediction is testable on the
  experimental timescale.

---

status is "unified-quantum-force-completion candidate with UQF-12
honestly downgraded; the Paper 3 claim does not depend on UQF-12
closing." This is the same scope discipline applied to UQF-11 in
§12.
