## 14.0 Scope statement and tier discipline

This section is the **UQF-9 UV-completion certificate** for Paper 3. It is the second-hardest gate in the UQF stack (after the nonperturbative-QCD certificate of §12-§13), and it inherits — without weakening — every scope discipline placed on the UV question by Paper 2 §6.5, §6.7, and by UQC-1.

UQF-9 has three operational duties only:

1. Pick one UV route and stop being ambiguous about which programme this paper is committing to.
2. Write the certificate template that route would have to satisfy at Minimum, Strong, and Full pass tiers, and mark each row of that template with its present status.
3. State an honest research roadmap and a downgrade rule for what happens to the paper's overall tier if UQF-9 fails to clear even the Minimum bar.

UQF-9 does *not* do, and cannot honestly do at this writing, any of the following:

- It does not claim that a non-Gaussian UV fixed point exists in the restricted theory space of Paper 2 §6.5.
- It does not claim that asymptotic safety, as a programme, has been closed in any dimension.
- It does not claim that the BV-BRST package of Paper 2 §6.3 has been shown positive-definite at the interacting level.
- It does not claim that the global RG trajectory from the (hypothesised) UV fixed point through the relevant compactification thresholds to the four-force interface scale has been controlled.
- It does not invent any new physics result that the global asymptotic-safety / loop QG / string communities have not already produced.

The honest landing for UQF-9 — argued in detail below — is **audit-tier with a structured certificate sketch and a named research roadmap**. The Minimum pass tier is plausibly achievable as an audit-tier result conditional on one external FRG truncation being performed. The Strong and Full pass tiers are open problems at the level of the global quantum-gravity literature, not at the level of this programme alone. The downgrade rule of §14.6 explains how Paper 3's overall claim tier reacts to that landing.

UQC-1 covered the UV question as a single audit. Paper 3 splits the UQC-1 content across two UQF gates: UQF-9 (UV completion, this section) and UQF-10 (quantum compactification stability, §15). This split is for gate hygiene; the underlying physics inherits unchanged from UQC-1. Wherever UQC-1 said "outside scope" or "open at the level of the global literature," this section says the same thing in the same words. Wherever UQC-1 supplied a 13D-specific narrowing — there are exactly three of them — this section reproduces it explicitly and routes it into a certificate row.

**Corpus guard — the Λ / vacuum-energy line (§11, 2026-06-12).** A reader must not infer from §14's UV-completion narrative that controlled high-energy behavior would supply a cancellation of the cosmological constant or the vacuum energy. The corpus has settled that line as a **computed honest fail**: TOE_FINAL **v12** ran the exact-weight graded supertrace over the Paper-3 §4 nine-row ledger and found **no structural cancellation at any coefficient order** (ratio 0.58 at $k{=}0$, 1.000 at $k{=}1\text{–}8$ — the chamber grading is coefficient-blind); TOE_FINAL **v14** then **THEOREM_REFUTED** the chamber-cancellation route (the Λ operator is the unit operator — grading-even, label-blind). The conclusion banked by the corpus is **Λ stays Weinberg-open as a computed one-loop certificate** (EXTERNAL; no observed-Λ comparison was performed). This guard does **not** change UQF-9's status — the asymptotic-safety fixed point remains a global open problem and UQF-9 remains correctly AUDIT (§11.3) — but it removes any reading of §14 (or its §15 cross-certificate) as housing a live Λ-cancellation mechanism. The UV question and the Λ question are distinct; the corpus has closed the latter as a fail while the former stays open.

The hard-gate vector $\mathsf{D},\mathsf{D}\text{-local},\mathsf{D},\mathsf{D},\mathsf{D}$ is preserved. BG-10 is preserved as *Open / Diagnostic* and is Paper 4 material; UQF-9 does not interact with it in either direction. C-FF0..C-FF14 are not modified. No filed-patent material, NRC packet, main-manuscript SoT, or `baryogenesis_build` content is edited or invoked as authority. "Chris does the physics"; this section organizes, audits, and drafts; it does not invent fixed-point existence proofs.

---

## 14.1 UV route selection

Paper 2 §6.5 commits the four-force interface paper to one nonperturbative model-definition target:

> The flow is governed by the exact FRG equation
> $\partial_t \Gamma_k = \tfrac12 \mathrm{STr}\big[(\Gamma_k^{(2)} + R_k)^{-1} \partial_t R_k\big]$,
> on the restricted theory space compatible with $M_{13} = M_{3,1} \times K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$, $K_6 = F_2 = SU(3)/U(1)^2$, $\mathrm{spin}^c(1,0)$ on $K_6$, the selected $S^2$ spin-c weak sectors, the $S^1$ hypercharge lattice, and the active $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ chirality domain.

That target rule is, structurally, the asymptotic-safety (Weinberg–Reuter) target. UQC-1 reviewed three candidate UV programmes — asymptotic safety, loop quantum gravity / spin-foam, and string / M-theoretic completion — against the 13D constraint method and found asymptotic safety the most structurally compatible of the three. That review is reproduced in compressed form below; the full review remains in UQC-1.

**Decision.** UQF-9 commits Paper 3 to the **asymptotic-safety route** as the primary UV-completion target. The two alternatives are not ruled out, and are noted as research-backup paths in §14.5, but every claim Paper 3 makes about UV-completion status is framed in the asymptotic-safety vocabulary.

Reasons for this commitment, in three sentences:

1. The Paper 2 §6.5 nonperturbative target rule *already is* the FRG equation that the asymptotic-safety community uses; there is no translation step.
2. The restricted theory space implied by the constraint-selected compactification is the natural object the asymptotic-safety community already constructs (background-metric, BV-BRST gauge-fixing, finite-dimensional truncation, matter-coupled), so progress in either direction feeds the other.
3. Adopting loop QG or string completions would require rewriting Paper 2 §6.3 and §6.5 wholesale, which the constraint method on its own does not motivate.

This is a *compatibility commitment*, not an existence claim. The 13D programme does not derive asymptotic safety, asymptotic safety has not been proved as a programme, and the 13D programme adds no new evidence on its own that the non-Gaussian fixed point exists. What the commitment buys is a stable certificate vocabulary: every row in §14.2 below can be stated in a form the asymptotic-safety community already recognises.

The alternative UV routes are kept in §14.5 as named backups under one rule: if a positive result in either alternative programme arises that aligns with the Paper 2 §6.3 package, this section's commitment is re-opened. No such result is known at the time of writing.

---

## 14.2 The asymptotic-safety / FRG certificate template

This is the load-bearing table of §14. It lists every element a Minimum-tier FRG fixed-point certificate must supply, names what would close it, and marks its present status. The rows are aligned with the handoff template (handoff §11) and with the UQC-1.2 audit table; the union is the certificate sketch.

| # | Row | What the Minimum-tier certificate must supply | Present status | What closes it |
|---|-----|-----------------------------------------------|---------------|----------------|
| FRG-1 | **Theory space** | Declared finite-dimensional truncation of the effective average action $\Gamma_k$ compatible with $\mathfrak B_{\rm active}$: operator basis restricted to symmetric tensors / scalars / connections / fermion bilinears under the residual $SU(3)\times SU(2)\times U(1)$ that the compactification carries, with explicit choice of curvature monomial cutoff order $n_R$, matter-coupling order $n_m$, and boundary-parity sector. | **Declarable at audit-tier.** The 13D constraint method supplies the symmetry content; the truncation order is a free choice subject to the convergence test of FRG-5. | A frozen written specification of $\Gamma_k^{\rm trunc}$ with $(n_R, n_m)$ and boundary sector explicit, in a form a partner FRG calculation can ingest without further interpretation. |
| FRG-2 | **Beta functions** | Explicit one-loop or higher beta functions $\partial_t g_i = \beta_i(g_j)$ for every running coupling $g_i$ of the FRG-1 truncation, computed with the FRG-1 truncation and with the regulator chosen in FRG-3. | **Open.** The 13D-specific truncation has not been computed; the asymptotic-safety community has computed analogous truncations in $d=4$ and in $d>4$ pure-gravity / matter-coupled cases, but not for this restricted theory space. | One concrete FRG calculation on FRG-1, published or filed, with the beta functions written explicitly in the paper's notation. This is the principal external deliverable required for Minimum-tier pass. |
| FRG-3 | **Regulator** | Fixed choice of cutoff function $R_k(p)$ (Litim / sharp-cutoff / exponential / smoothed-step) used uniformly across FRG-1 through FRG-7, with regulator-dependence checked as a scheme-dependence cross-check in FRG-6. | **Declarable.** The asymptotic-safety community has standard regulator choices; the 13D programme has no reason to deviate. The Litim regulator is the working default for this section. | A regulator declaration in the FRG-2 calculation that lists $R_k$ explicitly, plus the documentation that the same $R_k$ is used in FRG-4 through FRG-7. |
| FRG-4 | **Fixed point** | Non-Gaussian fixed point $g_i^{\ast}\neq 0$ of $\beta_i$ at the FRG-2 order, established within the FRG-1 truncation. | **Open. *Honest "search candidate" only* at this writing.** No FRG-1 truncation has been computed for the 13D restricted theory space, so no fixed-point search has been performed on the actual operator basis. Analogue calculations in $d>4$ pure gravity show fixed points in many truncations, but the 13D-specific case has not been done. | A computed FRG-2 calculation that returns a fixed-point candidate within FRG-1 and demonstrates basin-of-attraction control to the precision the FRG-3 regulator permits. |
| FRG-5 | **Critical exponents** | Finite number of relevant directions (negative critical exponents $\theta_i = -\lambda_i$ of the stability matrix at the fixed point), so the UV-critical surface is finite-dimensional. | **Open.** Conditional on FRG-4. The asymptotic-safety community's working answer in $d=4$ pure gravity is "a small number ($\leq 3$) of relevant directions"; the 13D case has not been computed. | Computation of the stability matrix eigenvalues at the FRG-4 fixed-point candidate; a finite, small number of relevant directions is the pass criterion. |
| FRG-6 | **Trajectory** | Controlled global RG trajectory from the FRG-4 fixed point ($k\to\infty$) through the relevant compactification thresholds (KK scale, $S^1$ inverse radius, $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary scale) to the four-force interface scale ($k\to 0$ matches the recovered Paper 2 IR physics). | **Open.** Conditional on FRG-4 and FRG-5. Threshold matching across $K_6\times S^2\times S^1$ is structurally well-defined (discrete spectrum; §14.3(i)) but has not been computed. | An IR-flow calculation, in the same truncation, showing the trajectory reaches the Paper 2 IR values within the truncation's intrinsic accuracy. |
| FRG-7 | **Stability** | Compactification remains stable along the FRG-6 trajectory: no runaway volume modulus, no tachyonic KK / orbifold mode, no destabilising boundary contribution from $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$. | **Open.** Forward-referenced to §15 (UQF-10). The two gates are coupled: if the volume modulus destabilises along the trajectory, the §6.9.3a Einstein-frame caveat in Paper 2 fails and the gravity interface itself downgrades. | Cross-certificate with §15: the moduli mass-matrix positivity check at the FRG-4 fixed point and along the FRG-6 trajectory. |
| FRG-8 | **Reproducibility** | Code / hash / environment for the FRG-2 calculation, with frozen inputs (geometry, matter content, truncation order, regulator) sufficient for an independent reproduction. | **Declarable** *if* an FRG-2 calculation is performed. The 13D programme can supply a frozen-inputs specification that a partner calculation can hash against. | A reproduction artifact (script + container or environment manifest + hash) attached to the FRG-2 calculation, mirroring the reproducibility discipline of the main GUT manuscript's freeze records. |

**Reading of the table.** Of the eight rows, **two (FRG-1, FRG-3) are declarable at audit-tier** by the 13D programme acting alone. **One (FRG-8) becomes declarable** as soon as an external FRG calculation is performed. **The remaining five (FRG-2, FRG-4, FRG-5, FRG-6, FRG-7) require external physics work** — specifically, an FRG truncation calculation on the FRG-1 theory space, performed by the asymptotic-safety community or by a partner using their machinery — that has not been performed at this writing.

The honest summary: **the 13D programme can supply, today, a structured FRG-1 / FRG-3 / FRG-8 declaration that a partner can compute against. It cannot, today, supply the actual fixed-point existence (FRG-4) or any of the rows that depend on it (FRG-5, FRG-6, FRG-7).**

---

## 14.3 The three 13D-specific narrowings (inherited from UQC-1.3)

The constraint method does not, on its own, prove a UV completion. But the choice of compactification is not arbitrary, and UQC-1.3 identified three structural features of $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ with the active $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity that *narrow* the FRG-2 / FRG-4 search problem without solving it. They are reproduced here because each one feeds a specific row of the §14.2 certificate template.

### 14.3(i) Discrete $K_6$ Laplacian spectrum → narrows FRG-1 (theory space)

The internal manifold is compact, homogeneous, and finite-spectrum. $K_6 = SU(3)/U(1)^2$ is a flag manifold with a fully discrete and computable Laplacian spectrum on every harmonic class. $S^2$ and $S^1$ likewise. The Kaluza–Klein quantization route of Paper 2 §6.4 therefore produces a *discrete* internal mode problem.

For an FRG truncation, this matters in two ways. First, the internal mode sums are convergent harmonic sums rather than continuum integrals, so the truncated $\Gamma_k$ has explicit threshold structure rather than a smeared continuum — the threshold matching of FRG-6 has a finite, computable set of crossings rather than an open integral. Second, the operator basis for the restricted theory space inherits the symmetry content of $SU(3) \times SU(2) \times U(1)$ that the compactification carries, which *prunes* the truncation rather than expanding it. A generic higher-dimensional asymptotic-safety calculation has a much larger operator basis at any given curvature order because no internal symmetry projects out terms; the 13D case projects out every operator that is not invariant under the residual gauge group.

**Concretely, narrowing 14.3(i) feeds FRG-1:** the operator basis declared in FRG-1 is the smallest gauge-invariant basis at curvature order $n_R$ and matter-coupling order $n_m$ that survives projection onto $SU(3)\times SU(2)\times U(1)$ invariants. This is a *constraint on* candidate truncations, not a *proof that* a particular truncation exists. The truncation specification of FRG-1 must record this projection step explicitly.

This is a partial simplification of audit-row (E) in UQC-1.2 — the truncation space is smaller and more structured than in a generic higher-dimensional asymptotic-safety setup. It is **not** a proof that the fixed point exists, and it is **not** a guarantee that the truncation is non-trivial.

### 14.3(ii) Finite Dai–Freed anomaly class from $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ → narrows FRG-4 / FRG-5 (anomaly closure as a consistency filter on the fixed point)

The $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity produces a chirality domain, not a mirror. The main GUT manuscript records that hypercharge is geometric with the $\mathbb{Z}_2$ quotient supplying the boundary / parity data that prevents a mirror partner for each chiral mode. For element (D) of the UQC-1.2 audit table — measure and anomaly closure — this has a sharp consequence: the boundary anomaly content that has to be checked is exactly the Dai–Freed / Freed–Hopkins data for the active interval sector with the specific matter representations dictated by the constraint method, **not a generic interval orbifold**.

The audit row therefore has a *finite* and *specifiable* set of mod-2 / global classes to verify, rather than an open-ended search. This is a partial simplification of (D), conditional on the inherited Standard Model anomaly ledger of the main manuscript continuing to hold.

**Concretely, narrowing 14.3(ii) feeds FRG-4 and FRG-5 as a consistency filter on the fixed-point candidate.** Any FRG-4 fixed-point candidate that drives the boundary anomaly content off the Dai–Freed-consistent set is excluded, irrespective of whether it is a fixed point of the bulk beta functions. Anomaly closure is therefore an external constraint on which fixed-point candidates are physically admissible, and the 13D programme has a finite, named set of classes to check, rather than the open-ended boundary-anomaly search that a generic interval orbifold would require.

This narrowing does **not** prove anomaly closure. It supplies a finite checklist whose entries are the inputs to a calculation that has not been performed.

### 14.3(iii) Single-modulus Einstein-frame reduction → narrows FRG-7 (stability) to a one-modulus question

The Einstein-frame reduction of Paper 2 §6.9.3 fixes one scaling relation,

$$
M_{\mathrm{Pl}}^2 = M_{13}^{11}\,\mathrm{Vol}(K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1),
$$

conditional on volume-modulus stabilization. This couples element (H) of UQC-1.2 — quantum compactification stability — directly to the four-force trunk: any quantum-completion candidate that destabilizes the volume modulus simultaneously breaks the §6.9.3a Einstein-frame caveat and downgrades the gravity interface itself, not merely the UQF-9 certificate.

The 13D programme therefore has a clean *single-modulus* stability question, not the generic multi-modulus problem of the string landscape.

**Concretely, narrowing 14.3(iii) feeds FRG-7** by reducing the moduli-stability check that FRG-7 (and §15 / UQF-10) must perform to a one-dimensional positivity question on the volume modulus at the FRG-4 fixed point and along the FRG-6 trajectory. The Einstein-frame caveat of Paper 2 §6.9.3a is the operational falsifier: if the FRG-6 trajectory drives the volume modulus out of any stable basin, §6.9.3a fails and the cross-certificate with §15 collapses.

This narrowing is a partial simplification of (H), but only relative to the multi-modulus baseline. The single-modulus question is still an open question; the narrowing does not solve it.

**None of (i), (ii), (iii) is a proof of anything.** They are structural features that *narrow* the FRG / Dai–Freed / moduli-stability questions; the questions themselves remain open. The honest summary, reproduced verbatim from UQC-1.3, is:

> The constraint-selected compactification supplies a smaller, more structured restricted theory space and a finite boundary-anomaly class set than a generic higher-dimensional setup would. This shrinks the search problem facing the asymptotic-safety programme without solving it.

---

## 14.4 Pass tiers, tier landing, and the honest "search candidate" framing

The handoff (§11) defines three pass tiers for UQF-9:

- **Minimum** — finite-dim truncation certificate: an FRG-1 / FRG-3 / FRG-8 declaration plus one FRG-2 calculation on it that reports either (a) a fixed-point candidate (FRG-4 pass), or (b) a negative result that informs the next truncation (FRG-4 fail, but FRG-2 closed). Either outcome counts as a Minimum-tier *certificate*; only outcome (a) counts as an upgrade of confidence.
- **Strong** — truncation-stable fixed point with relevant-direction count + IR trajectory: FRG-4 closed in at least one truncation, FRG-5 returns a finite small relevant-direction count, FRG-6 reaches the Paper 2 IR within truncation accuracy, FRG-7 closes against §15.
- **Full** — constructive / nonperturbative UV definition: an existence theorem at the level of the asymptotic-safety programme's own closure standard, with truncation independence (FRG-4 closed in at least two independent operator bases) and Lorentzian / operator-algebraic completion.

**Tier landing for UQFC-14 at this writing.** UQF-9 lands at **audit-tier** with a structured certificate sketch and a named research roadmap. None of the three pass tiers has been *achieved*; the certificate template of §14.2 is *declarable* but not yet *closed*.

- **Minimum is plausibly achievable as an audit-tier result** if and only if one partner FRG calculation on FRG-1 is performed. The 13D programme can today supply FRG-1, FRG-3, FRG-8 in a form a partner can ingest; the partner must supply FRG-2 (and incidentally FRG-4, since the FRG-2 calculation is the fixed-point search).
- **Strong is an open problem** at the level of the global asymptotic-safety literature, not merely at the level of this programme. The asymptotic-safety community has produced single-truncation Strong-equivalent results in 4D pure gravity; truncation-independence in any dimension is a frontier question.
- **Full is an open problem** at the level of the global quantum-gravity literature. A constructive, nonperturbative UV definition for an interacting gauge-coupled matter theory in $d>4$ has not been produced; that includes the 13D case.

**The honest "search candidate" framing.** In the absence of an FRG-2 calculation on FRG-1, the fixed-point row FRG-4 is *not* claimed as a candidate, much less as a result. The honest label is: *no fixed-point search has been performed on the actual operator basis*; the 13D programme inherits, by structural analogy with $d>4$ asymptotic-safety results, the *prior* that such a fixed point is plausible, but inherits no *evidence* specific to the FRG-1 truncation. This is the same prior the asymptotic-safety community would assign to any restricted theory space that has not been computed.

This section commits to the following phrasing rule, which mirrors UQC-1.0's discipline:

> Wherever §14 of this paper uses the words "fixed point," "trajectory," or "UV completion" in the present tense, the qualifier "for the FRG-1 truncation, conditional on an external FRG calculation that has not yet been performed" is to be read as if appended. No present-tense existence claim in §14 is intended without that qualifier.

A reviewer who finds a sentence in §14 that asserts a fixed point exists without the qualifier should report it as a bug; the bug-report routing rule is identical to UQC-1.0's: the sentence downgrades to audit-tier per the §14.6 downgrade ladder.

---

## 14.5 Research roadmap (inherited and compressed from UQC-1.4)

The roadmap is identical in substance to UQC-1.4 and is reproduced in compressed form here, with the row identifiers of §14.2 attached so the deliverables are traceable to the certificate template.

**Year 0–2 (in-house, partnership)**

- *In-house (FRG-1).* Write the restricted theory space of Paper 2 §6.5 in the asymptotic-safety community's notation, with the operator basis pruned by the symmetry content of $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ as described in §14.3(i). Deliverable: a frozen FRG-1 specification with $(n_R, n_m)$ and boundary sector explicit, in a form a partner FRG calculation can ingest without further interpretation.
- *In-house (FRG-3, FRG-8).* Declare the regulator choice (Litim default) and write the reproducibility envelope (frozen-inputs manifest, hashable specification).
- *In-house (anomaly-closure feed for FRG-4 admissibility).* Write the Dai–Freed / Freed–Hopkins finite-class checklist that any FRG-4 fixed-point candidate must respect (per §14.3(ii)). Mark each class as *closed* / *open* / *cancels by inheritance from main-manuscript anomaly ledger*.
- *Partnership (FRG-2, FRG-4).* Approach the asymptotic-safety community (Reuter group at Mainz; Saueressig at Nijmegen; Eichhorn at Heidelberg / Southern Denmark; Pawlowski at Heidelberg; Percacci at SISSA; Bonanno at Catania; Codello) with the FRG-1 deliverable plus the anomaly-class checklist, with one concrete ask: compute the lowest non-trivial FRG truncation on this restricted theory space.
- *Backup partnership.* Parallel approach to the higher-dimensional LQG / spin-foam community (Loll; Thiemann / Bodendorfer; Rovelli) with the narrower question of whether background independence allows the constraint-selected compactification to emerge as a semiclassical sector. This is a research-backup track, not a primary commitment.
- *Falsifier check, in-house.* The Paper 2 §6.3a equivalence-principle check, §6.9.3b universal-coupling test, and §6.9.6 weak-field Newtonian limit are already operational. Any UV-completion candidate that breaks them is excluded; this is the bottom rung of the falsifier ladder.

**Year 2–5 (partnership-led)**

- *Partnership (FRG-2 closes; FRG-4 returns either a candidate or a negative).* First FRG truncation on the FRG-1 theory space. The deliverable is a numerical result: either a candidate non-Gaussian fixed point with a small finite UV-critical surface (FRG-4 pass + FRG-5 declarable), or a negative result that constrains the next truncation (FRG-4 fail, but Minimum-tier certificate closed). **Either outcome is informative and counts as Minimum-tier closure.**
- *In-house (FRG-6, conditional on FRG-4 pass).* If a fixed-point candidate appears, write the corresponding global trajectory: identify the relevant matching scales between the UV fixed point and the four-force interface scale, and check whether the recovered IR physics matches the four-force trunk. If it does, this is an upgrade of confidence, not a Strong-tier closure.
- *Partnership (FRG-4 truncation-independence).* Cross-check by a second FRG truncation in a different operator basis, independently performed. Asymptotic safety as a programme treats single-truncation results as suggestive, not as proof; the same standard applies here. Two independent truncations both finding the fixed point is the threshold for Strong-tier eligibility on FRG-4.
- *Field-wide.* Any progress on constructive positivity for interacting BV-BRST gauge theory in any dimension feeds the §14.6 cross-references to UQF-3 (physical Hilbert space) and UQF-14 (unitarity).

**Year 5–10 (field-wide, with 13D-specific deliverables)**

- *In-house, conditional.* If the FRG-4, FRG-5, FRG-6, FRG-7 rows close at the asymptotic-safety community's standard of evidence and the §15 (UQF-10) cross-certificate closes, write the Strong-tier upgrade of UQF-9. This is the only condition under which §14 could be re-classified above audit-tier with a Minimum-tier certificate.
- *Field-wide.* Progress on the black-hole information problem, on dS in quantum gravity, and on operator-algebraic Lorentzian quantum field theory is inherited rather than produced by the 13D programme. None of these are required for the Minimum-tier or Strong-tier UQF-9 certificate; all are required for a Full-tier UQF-9 certificate.
- *Falsification, in-house.* The hard falsifiers are the ones already in Paper 2: equivalence-principle violation at the leading reduced action; failure to recover Newtonian gravity in the weak-field limit; sector-dependent leading gravitational coupling; collapse of the Einstein-frame reduction (§6.9.3a) because the volume modulus refuses to stabilize. None of these is hypothetical; each is operational on the existing Paper 2 machinery.

**What no roadmap can promise.** Asymptotic safety has been an active research programme since 1979 and is still without a closed existence theorem in 4D. The honest expectation is that the 13D-specific narrowings of §14.3 make the truncation problem more tractable for the asymptotic-safety community without inventing a new path to closure. UQF-9 cannot promise a UV-completion proof in any timeframe; it can promise the certificate template that a future closure would inhabit.

## 14.6 Downgrade ladder, cross-gate impact, and verdict

UQF-9 inherits the per-gate downgrade ladder of §3 (the UQF status vocabulary). The ladder for UQF-9 specifically, in falling order of strength:

| If UQF-9 lands at... | The certificate reads... | Cross-gate impact |
|---|---|---|
| **Full pass** | "A constructive, nonperturbative UV definition of the 13D restricted theory has been written; FRG-4 closes in at least two independent operator bases; FRG-6 / FRG-7 / §15 cross-certificate closes." | UQF-9 Full pass → UQFC paper as a whole eligible for *complete unified quantum theory of all known forces* claim (Full tier of the handoff's tier ladder), subject to every other UQF row also at Full. |
| **Strong pass** | "A non-Gaussian fixed point is demonstrated in the FRG-1 restricted theory space by at least one FRG truncation; relevant-direction count is finite and small; IR trajectory matches the Paper 2 trunk within truncation accuracy; §15 cross-certificate closes." | UQF-9 Strong pass → UQFC paper eligible for *certificate-complete unified quantum force theory under declared assumptions* (Strong tier). |
| **Minimum pass (current target)** | "FRG-1 / FRG-3 / FRG-8 declared; one external FRG truncation has been computed on the FRG-1 theory space, returning either a fixed-point candidate or a negative result; the Dai–Freed checklist of §14.3(ii) has been written and no admissibility violation is reported." | UQF-9 Minimum pass → UQFC paper eligible for *candidate unified quantum-force completion under declared assumptions* (Minimum tier). |
| **Audit-tier landing (current state)** | "FRG-1 / FRG-3 / FRG-8 declarable; FRG-2 / FRG-4 / FRG-5 / FRG-6 / FRG-7 open. The fixed-point question is treated as a *search candidate*, not a result. The Dai–Freed checklist is in preparation." | UQF-9 audit-tier → UQFC paper bounded above by the audit-tier interpretation of every downstream Phase 6 / Phase 7 row; specifically §15 (UQF-10) is forward-referenced and likewise lands at audit-tier with declared truncation, and Phase 7 precision claims (§16 / UQF-13) are weak-bounded by the fact that the UV trajectory is not under control. |
| **UQF-9 failure** | "FRG-1 cannot be written down (operator basis ill-defined) or FRG-2 on every reasonable truncation excludes a fixed point under the 13D-specific narrowings." | UQF-9 failure → §14.6 routes the failure into the §19 falsification map. The asymptotic-safety route is then abandoned and §14.5's research-backup tracks (LQG/spin-foam, string) are promoted. The Paper 2 §6.5 target rule is preserved as a *target only*; the UQFC paper's overall tier downgrades to *interface-only* on the gravity sector. |

**Verdict for §14 in the current draft.** UQF-9 lands at **audit-tier with structured certificate sketch and named research roadmap**, as the honest landing the handoff (§11) requests. The verdict sentence, in the discipline of UQC-1.0's closing paragraph:

> Status: Audit-tier. UV route committed: asymptotic safety. Certificate template (FRG-1 through FRG-8) declared. FRG-1 / FRG-3 / FRG-8 declarable today; FRG-2 / FRG-4 / FRG-5 / FRG-6 / FRG-7 open at the level of the global asymptotic-safety literature. No fixed-point existence proof claimed. The 13D-specific narrowings of §14.3 shrink the search problem facing the partner FRG calculation without solving it. Minimum pass tier is plausibly achievable conditional on one partner FRG calculation; Strong / Full pass tiers are open problems in the wider field. Hard-gate vector preserved. BG-10 preserved. C-FF12 / C-FF13 respected. No gate upgrade is performed or implied by this section.

## 15.0 Scope statement and tier discipline

This section is the **UQF-10 quantum compactification stability certificate** for Paper 3. It is the cross-certificate forward-referenced by §14 (UQF-9, FRG-7) and the operational dependency of the Paper 2 §6.9.3a Einstein-frame caveat.

UQF-10 asks one question only:

> Does the constraint-selected compact branch $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ with the active $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity remain stable under quantum corrections, specifically along the FRG-6 trajectory of §14 from the (hypothesised) UV fixed point to the four-force interface scale?

The question is unpacked into seven required certificate rows, listed in §15.2. For each row this section states whether the row is a **CERTIFICATE** within the declared truncation, an **AUDIT** with named research path, or **OPEN** at the level of the global literature.

UQF-10 does *not* do, and cannot honestly do at this writing, any of the following:

- It does not claim that the moduli mass matrix has been computed at the interacting level on the FRG-6 trajectory of §14; that calculation has not been performed.
- It does not claim that quantum compactification stability has been established as a theorem; it claims, where it claims anything, certificate-completeness *within the declared truncation*.
- It does not claim that the Dai–Freed / Freed–Hopkins finite anomaly class set on the $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity sector has been closed; that calculation is forward-referenced to §14.3(ii).
- It does not invent any new physics result that the global moduli-stabilization / extra-dimensions literature has not already produced.

The honest landing for UQF-10, summarised in §15.6, is:

> **Quantum compactification stability is certificate-complete only within the declared truncation.** Three rows are CERTIFICATE within truncation (single-modulus reduction, classical orbifold stability, classical KK structure); four rows are AUDIT with named research paths (moduli mass-matrix positivity at interacting level, vacuum-energy control, threshold corrections, no runaway volume modulus); zero rows are at full closure.

This phrasing matches the handoff (§12) instruction that, if not fully proven, the section state explicitly: *"quantum compactification stability is certificate-complete only within the declared truncation."*

UQC-1 covered UV completion and compactification stability as a single audit (audit row (H) of UQC-1.2 and narrowing (iii) of UQC-1.3). Paper 3 splits that content across UQF-9 (§14) and UQF-10 (this section). UQF-10 inherits the substance of UQC-1.2(H) and UQC-1.3(iii) unchanged; the structural reformulation into seven explicit certificate rows is for gate hygiene only.

**Corpus reconciliation note (2026-06-12; see §11 Corpus Reconciliation).** Since this section was drafted (2026-06-08) the TOE_FINAL capsule (EXTERNAL; v6–v15, 2026-06-11/12) **independently discharged the compactification-stability *existence* question at decision grade**, by a route this section does not use. The corpus did not run the §14 FRG-6 trajectory; it evaluated its own native three-layer stabilization object
$$V(\sigma) = c_{KK}\,e^{-4\sigma} + c_{bdry}\,e^{-2\sigma} + c_{W}\cos\theta_W\,e^{-4\sigma} + c_{loop}\,e^{-6\sigma},$$
and recorded: TOE_FINAL **v8** the countersigned ruling `H04_DISCHARGED_AT_DECISION_GRADE` (the operative curved-share bound cleared by 35× in the weakest accepted variant, 2.4×10³ central); **v9** Gap 04 **CLOSED at decision grade** (D15-native runner PASS; package `gap04_frozen_package_native.json`); **v10** the boundary-sign event $c_{bdry}=-1.08\times10^{-2}$ (negative across the full band) ⟹ the stabilization well **exists unconditionally** in $c_{loop}$ (the earlier $c_{loop}$ window vacated; self-caught #5). The honest consequence for UQF-10 is *narrow and does not change this row's tier*: the corpus supplies a **decision-grade** statement that the active background is a stable minimum (an existence result), which this paper **inherits as input** and which makes the row's literal "blocked by UQF-9" framing too pessimistic — a stability discharge already exists, independent of the asymptotic-safety fixed point. It does **not** supply this paper's *certificate-grade* result on the §14 FRG-6 trajectory (S-2 / S-5 / S-7 below), which remains UQF-10's own open obligation. The row therefore stays **AUDIT**; the decision-grade discharge is cited, not promoted. Promotion of this row to certificate tier on the strength of the corpus discharge is a countersign decision (the Return-YAML / Chris instrument), not an edit made here.

The hard-gate vector $\mathsf{D},\mathsf{D}\text{-local},\mathsf{D},\mathsf{D},\mathsf{D}$ is preserved. BG-10 is preserved as *Open / Diagnostic* and is Paper 4 material. C-FF0..C-FF14 are not modified. No filed-patent material, NRC packet, main-manuscript SoT, or `baryogenesis_build` content is edited or invoked as authority. "Chris does the physics"; this section organizes, audits, and drafts.

## 15.1 The declared truncation (what "within truncation" means)

UQF-10 is certificate-complete *within the declared truncation only*. The truncation is declared once, here, and used as the scope guard throughout §15.2.

**Declared truncation for UQF-10:**

1. **Geometry.** $M_{13} = M_{3,1} \times K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$, with $K_6 = F_2 = SU(3)/U(1)^2$, the selected $S^2$ spin-c weak sectors, the $S^1$ hypercharge lattice, and the active $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ chirality domain. This is the Paper 2 §6.5 / Paper 2 §6.9.2 active compactification.

2. **Modulus content.** The volume modulus $\sigma$ associated with $\mathrm{Vol}(K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1)$ — the *single* modulus that enters the Paper 2 §6.9.3 Einstein-frame relation $M_{\mathrm{Pl}}^2 = M_{13}^{11}\mathrm{Vol}(K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1)$ — is the only modulus treated dynamically. Shape moduli of the homogeneous $K_6$ factor and of $S^2$, $S^1$ are *frozen at their constraint-selected values* by the residual $SU(3)\times U(1)^2 / SU(2) / U(1)$ isometry structure that the compactification carries. This single-modulus framing is the UQC-1.3(iii) narrowing.

3. **Quantum framework.** The same BV-BRST package of Paper 2 §6.3, with the FRG flow on the restricted theory space of Paper 2 §6.5 / UQFC-14 FRG-1, evaluated within the same truncation order $(n_R, n_m)$ that UQFC-14 declares.

4. **Boundary sector.** The $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ orbifold boundary parity is treated with the Dai–Freed / Freed–Hopkins finite-class checklist of UQFC-14.3(ii); UQF-10 forward-references the admissibility filter to that checklist.

5. **Truncation scope.** Quantum corrections to the moduli effective potential are evaluated to the same loop order at which §14 evaluates the beta functions $\beta_i$; explicit cross-loop or non-perturbative corrections beyond that order are outside the declared truncation.

**What "within truncation" rules out as a closure claim.** A CERTIFICATE row of §15.2 is certified *within* this truncation. It is *not* certified against:

- corrections at loop orders strictly beyond $(n_R, n_m)$;
- moduli that arise from shape / complex-structure deformations of the compact factors (these are frozen by 15.1(2));
- non-perturbative effects (instantons, condensates, branes) that are not visible in the FRG flow at the §14 truncation order;
- boundary anomaly classes outside the §14.3(ii) checklist.

A reviewer who finds a §15.2 CERTIFICATE claim being applied beyond the declared truncation should report it as a bug; the bug-report routing rule is identical to §14.4's: the claim downgrades to AUDIT for the out-of-truncation region.

---

## 15.2 The seven required certificate rows

The handoff (§12) enumerates seven certificates UQF-10 must address. Each is given a row identifier (S-1 through S-7), a row content statement, a status (CERTIFICATE within truncation / AUDIT / OPEN), and a named research path for the non-closed rows.

| # | Row | Content | Status | Closure / research path |
|---|-----|---------|--------|-------------------------|
| **S-1** | Single-modulus reduction (forward-condition for S-2 / S-4 / S-6) | The compact branch admits a one-dimensional dynamical modulus reduction (the volume modulus $\sigma$), with shape moduli frozen by the residual isometry / spin-c structure of the constraint-selected geometry. | **CERTIFICATE within truncation.** Per §15.1(2); inherited from UQC-1.3(iii) and Paper 2 §6.9.3. | Within the declared truncation, the single-modulus reduction is a theorem of the constraint method. *Outside* the truncation (shape-moduli activation), the question becomes a multi-modulus question and is treated as the string-landscape baseline, which is OPEN field-wide. |
| **S-2** | Moduli mass-matrix positivity $\lambda_{\min}(M^2_{\mathrm{moduli}}) > 0$ | Smallest eigenvalue of the moduli quadratic-form matrix at the chosen background $\bar G_{MN}$ is strictly positive. Per S-1 this reduces to $V''(\sigma)|_{\sigma = \sigma_\ast} > 0$ for the single-modulus effective potential $V(\sigma)$ at its critical point $\sigma_\ast$. | **AUDIT.** Classical positivity at the constraint-selected $\sigma_\ast$ is established at the level of the §6.9 reduction; the *quantum-corrected* positivity along the §14 FRG-6 trajectory has not been computed. | Compute $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$ at the §14 FRG-2 truncation order, evaluate $V_{\rm eff}''(\sigma_\ast)$, check sign. Cross-certificate with §14 FRG-7. **Research path:** partnered with the §14 FRG-2 calculation; not independent of it. |
| **S-3** | No tachyonic compact modes (perturbative spectrum, $\bar G_{MN}$ vacuum) | At the linearised level around the constraint-selected $\bar G_{MN}$ background, the KK mass spectrum on $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ — including the boundary sector — has no negative-mass-squared mode. | **CERTIFICATE within truncation.** $K_6 = SU(3)/U(1)^2$ is a homogeneous Einstein space; $S^2$ and $S^1$ have constant curvature; the Laplacian on every compact factor has a fully discrete, non-negative spectrum starting from the zero mode. The boundary parity quotient projects out half the modes but does not introduce negative-mass states. | **At linearised level, closed within truncation.** Non-perturbative ghost-tachyon exclusion (vacuum tunneling, dynamical condensate effects) is row (C) of UQC-1.2 and is **OPEN**; that out-of-truncation question is treated under S-7 below. |
| **S-4** | Vacuum energy controlled or explicitly scoped | The vacuum energy contribution from the compactification — the 4D cosmological constant induced by KK / boundary / loop effects on the active compact branch — is either computed and small, or is explicitly scoped as a Paper 4 question. | **AUDIT, explicitly scoped to Paper 4.** Paper 2 §6.10 already routes the cosmological constant to "outside this paper's scope — R2 / Section 8 of main manuscript." Paper 3 inherits the same routing: UQF-10 does not compute the induced 4D vacuum energy; Paper 4 (TOE) is the venue. | **Research path:** Paper 4. This row is at AUDIT in Paper 3 *only because* the question is explicitly handed to Paper 4 and is not litigated here. The handoff (§12) requires this row be either controlled or explicitly scoped; "explicitly scoped to Paper 4" is the closure of the gate at this paper's tier. **Corpus guard (§11.2, 2026-06-12):** the Paper-4 venue has since computed the Λ line as an **honest fail** — TOE_FINAL **v12** the exact-weight graded supertrace shows **no structural cancellation at any coefficient order** (chamber grading coefficient-blind), **v14** the chamber route is **THEOREM_REFUTED** (the Λ operator is the unit operator); **Λ stays Weinberg-open as a computed one-loop certificate** (EXTERNAL; no observed-Λ comparison performed). Nothing in S-4 may be read as implying a live vacuum-energy-cancellation mechanism; the corpus has closed that route as a computed fail, which is fully consistent with S-4's "scoped to Paper 4" status. |
| **S-5** | KK spectrum stable (no spectrum collapse along FRG trajectory) | The Kaluza–Klein mass spectrum on $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ retains its discrete, $O(M_{\rm KK})$-spaced structure along the §14 FRG-6 trajectory; no KK level crosses zero, and no infinite degeneracy collapse occurs as $k$ varies between the UV fixed point and the four-force interface scale. | **AUDIT.** Spectrum stability at the *classical* compactification scale is a theorem of the constraint method (S-3 covers the perturbative spectrum). Stability along the FRG-6 trajectory has not been verified; it is implicitly assumed by Paper 2 §6.4's threshold structure. | **Research path:** evaluate the KK threshold function along FRG-6 (see narrowing §14.3(i)'s explicit threshold structure); confirm no level crossing. Partnered with §14 FRG-6 calculation; cross-certificate with §14 FRG-7. |
| **S-6** | Orbifold / boundary conditions stable | The $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity assignments — which fix the active chirality domain and prevent mirror partners — remain stable under quantum corrections; no boundary-anomaly violation re-introduces a forbidden boundary condition. | **AUDIT.** Classical stability of the orbifold structure is a theorem of the constraint method. Quantum stability reduces to the Dai–Freed / Freed–Hopkins finite-class checklist of §14.3(ii). The checklist is *declarable* (the finite class set is named) but has not been computed. | **Research path:** write and compute the §14.3(ii) Dai–Freed checklist; cross-certificate with §14 FRG-4 admissibility. This row is shared with §14, not independent of it. |
| **S-7** | No runaway volume modulus | The volume modulus $\sigma$ does not run away to $\sigma \to \pm \infty$ along the FRG-6 trajectory; equivalently, the effective potential $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$ has a stable basin of attraction at $\sigma_\ast$ that is preserved along the trajectory. | **AUDIT.** *Most consequential of the four AUDIT rows.* Conditional on S-2 closing at AUDIT-resolution: positivity of $V_{\rm eff}''$ is necessary but not sufficient; the absence of a runaway requires the *global* shape of $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$ to be bounded below in the operating range. | **Research path:** compute $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$ globally at §14 FRG-2 truncation order, not merely $V_{\rm eff}''$ at $\sigma_\ast$; check for a runaway direction. Cross-certificate with §14 FRG-7 and with the Paper 2 §6.9.3a Einstein-frame caveat: **a runaway here breaks §6.9.3a and downgrades the gravity interface itself, not merely UQF-10.** |

**Threshold corrections frozen** (8th row mentioned in handoff §12): this is treated as a sub-row of S-5 (KK spectrum stable) in this section's organisation. The KK spectrum's discrete, $O(M_{\rm KK})$-spaced structure is exactly what makes threshold corrections frozen along the FRG-6 trajectory; if S-5 closes, the threshold-correction freeze closes with it. If S-5 fails, the threshold-correction freeze fails. The row is therefore not double-counted; it is the FRG-6 reading of S-5.

**Reading of the table.** Three rows (S-1, S-3, S-4) are at certificate or explicitly-scoped status within the declared truncation. Four rows (S-2, S-5, S-6, S-7) are at AUDIT with named research paths, all of which are coupled to the §14 FRG calculation that has not yet been performed. **Zero rows are at full quantum closure.** S-7 is the most consequential AUDIT row because its failure mode is also a failure mode of the Paper 2 §6.9.3a Einstein-frame caveat.

---

## 15.3 The 13D-specific framing: $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ with $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity

The geometry-specific reading of each row, with the UQC-1.3 narrowings made explicit. The subsections take the stability question down to the actual factors of $M_{13} = M_{3,1}\times K_6\times S^2\times S^1$: how the $K_6 = SU(3)/U(1)^2$ homogeneous-Einstein structure feeds the S-3 and S-5 rows (§15.3(i)), how the $S^2$ and $S^1_Y/\mathbb Z_2$ boundary-parity factors enter, and where the single-modulus truncation of §15.1 is doing the load-bearing work — making explicit what is certificate-within-truncation and what remains the §14 FRG obligation.

### 15.3(i) $K_6 = SU(3)/U(1)^2$ homogeneous-Einstein structure feeds S-3 and S-5

$K_6$ is a flag manifold (the full $SU(3)$ flag $F_2$) with a fully discrete, computable Laplacian spectrum on every harmonic class, and admits a homogeneous Einstein metric at the constraint-selected scale. The implications for §15.2:

- **S-3 (no tachyonic compact modes).** The Laplacian spectrum on a homogeneous Einstein manifold is non-negative and discrete; no negative-mass-squared mode arises at linearised level. The same statement holds on $S^2$ (constant positive curvature) and on $S^1$ (flat). The combined spectrum on $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ is the discrete tensor product, with the $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ quotient projecting out half the modes; nothing in this construction introduces a tachyonic mode. **S-3 closure within truncation rides directly on the homogeneous-Einstein structure of $K_6$.**
- **S-5 (KK spectrum stable).** The discrete spectrum has explicit threshold structure (UQC-1.3(i) / §14.3(i)). For S-5 the question is whether that threshold structure is preserved along the FRG-6 trajectory; the constraint method does not guarantee preservation under quantum flow, but it does guarantee that any candidate violation would be a *named*, *computable* level crossing rather than a smeared spectral collapse. This is what makes S-5 an AUDIT row with a named research path rather than an OPEN row.

### 15.3(ii) $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity feeds S-6 and S-7

The active $S^1/\mathbb{Z}_2$ boundary parity is the chirality-domain mechanism (no mirror partners) inherited from the main GUT manuscript. The implications for §15.2:

- **S-6 (orbifold / boundary conditions stable).** Classical stability is a theorem of the constraint method (the boundary parity assignment is a discrete topological choice, not a tunable parameter). Quantum stability requires the Dai–Freed / Freed–Hopkins finite-class checklist of §14.3(ii) to clear. **S-6 is coupled to §14.3(ii); it is not an independent calculation.**
- **S-7 (no runaway volume modulus, boundary contribution).** The boundary parity sector contributes to the effective potential $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$ on the volume modulus. Whether that contribution is bounded below depends on the boundary-anomaly content (i.e., on §14.3(ii)). The runaway question therefore couples S-7 to both S-6 and §14.3(ii).

### 15.3(iii) Single-modulus framing (UQC-1.3(iii) reproduced) feeds S-1, S-2, S-7

This is the most consequential narrowing for UQF-10 because it converts a generic multi-modulus problem (the string-landscape baseline, where moduli-stabilization is a major open problem with thousands of moduli to control) into a single-modulus problem.

The Einstein-frame reduction of Paper 2 §6.9.3 fixes one scaling relation,
$$
M_{\mathrm{Pl}}^2 = M_{13}^{11}\,\mathrm{Vol}(K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1),
$$
conditional on volume-modulus stabilization. Per §15.1(2) the shape moduli are frozen by the residual isometry / spin-c structure; the volume modulus $\sigma$ is the only dynamical modulus in the declared truncation.

**Implications for §15.2:**

- **S-1 (single-modulus reduction).** Direct theorem of the constraint method within the declared truncation; CERTIFICATE.
- **S-2 (moduli mass-matrix positivity).** Reduces from a matrix positivity question (computationally heavy in the multi-modulus case) to a single sign check $V_{\rm eff}''(\sigma_\ast) > 0$. The reduction is structural; the calculation of $V_{\rm eff}''$ still has to be performed and has not been; AUDIT.
- **S-7 (no runaway volume modulus).** Reduces from a multi-modulus runaway analysis to a global-shape check on $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$. The reduction is structural; the global-shape calculation has not been performed; AUDIT.

This single-modulus framing is **the** reason UQF-10 can land at "certificate-complete within the declared truncation" with three CERTIFICATE rows and four named-path AUDIT rows, rather than at the generic-multi-modulus-baseline open-problem status. It does not solve the question; it makes the question small enough to be a single forward-referenced computation.

---

## 15.4 Coupling to UQF-9 (§14) — the cross-certificate

UQF-10 is not independent of UQF-9. The seven rows of §15.2 couple to §14's FRG template as follows.

| §15.2 row | §14 FRG dependency | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| **S-1** | None (constraint-method theorem within truncation) | CERTIFICATE row; declarable independent of §14. |
| **S-2** | §14 FRG-2 (beta functions) → $V_{\rm eff}''(\sigma_\ast)$ | AUDIT row; closes when §14 FRG-2 closes. |
| **S-3** | None (linearised-level theorem from homogeneous-Einstein structure) | CERTIFICATE row; declarable independent of §14. |
| **S-4** | None (explicitly scoped to Paper 4) | AUDIT (explicit-scope) row; not a §14 dependency. |
| **S-5** | §14 FRG-6 (trajectory) → KK threshold function along trajectory | AUDIT row; closes when §14 FRG-6 closes. |
| **S-6** | §14.3(ii) (Dai–Freed checklist) → boundary-anomaly admissibility | AUDIT row; closes when §14.3(ii) checklist closes. Shared with §14. |
| **S-7** | §14 FRG-2 + FRG-6 → global $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$ along trajectory | AUDIT row; **most consequential**; closes when §14 FRG-2 and FRG-6 both close *and* $V_{\rm eff}(\sigma)$ is bounded below. |

**The §14 ↔ §15 cross-certificate.** UQFC-14 FRG-7 forward-references §15 for the moduli-stability piece of its certificate; UQFC-15 forward-references §14 for the FRG calculation on which four of its seven rows depend. The two gates are coupled: the Minimum-tier pass on §14 (FRG-2 + FRG-4 + Dai–Freed checklist) is the *same calculation* that closes S-2 / S-5 / S-6 / S-7 to AUDIT-resolution within their truncation, and the Strong-tier pass on §14 (FRG-4 + FRG-5 + FRG-6 closed) is the calculation that promotes S-2 / S-5 / S-7 from AUDIT to CERTIFICATE within their truncation.

**At the current draft state**, with §14 at audit-tier and the FRG calculation not performed:
- The three CERTIFICATE-within-truncation rows of §15.2 (S-1, S-3, S-4) are *declarable now*.
- The four AUDIT rows (S-2, S-5, S-6, S-7) are *declarable now as AUDIT*; their promotion to CERTIFICATE within truncation requires the §14 FRG calculation that has not yet been performed.
- Zero rows are at CERTIFICATE-beyond-truncation status; that promotion requires §14's Strong / Full pass.

| **CERTIFICATE-within-truncation (Strong, current target)** | "S-1, S-3, S-4 CERTIFICATE within truncation; S-2, S-5, S-6, S-7 promoted to CERTIFICATE within truncation by §14 Strong pass closing the cross-references." | UQF-10 Strong → UQFC paper eligible for Strong tier on the gravity sector, conditional on §14 Strong. |

| **UQF-10 failure (tachyonic mode at non-perturbative level)** | "S-3 fails out-of-truncation: a non-perturbative tachyon / vacuum tunneling channel exists that is not visible at linearised level." | UQF-10 out-of-truncation failure on S-3 → out-of-truncation correction; CERTIFICATE-within-truncation rows of §15.2 remain valid statements, but the declared truncation is no longer sufficient and §15.1 must be re-declared at a wider truncation. |

**Verdict for §15 in the current draft.** UQF-10 lands at **AUDIT with declared truncation, three rows at CERTIFICATE-within-truncation and four rows at AUDIT with named research paths**, with the explicit honest landing phrase:

> **Quantum compactification stability is certificate-complete only within the declared truncation.**

This phrasing is the handoff (§12) required honest landing.

The single-modulus framing of UQC-1.3(iii) is what reduces the multi-modulus baseline to a single forward-referenced computation. **Corpus reconciliation (§11.2):** the compactification-stability *existence* question is, independently of the §14 FRG route, **CLOSED at decision grade** in the corpus (TOE_FINAL v8–v10, EXTERNAL; native stabilization object with the boundary-sign event making the well unconditional in $c_{loop}$); UQF-10 inherits this as a decision-grade input but its own certificate-grade FRG verification (S-2 / S-5 / S-7) remains open, so this row's tier is **preserved at AUDIT**. The associated Λ / vacuum-energy line (S-4) is Weinberg-open as a computed certificate per TOE_FINAL v12/v14 (no live cancellation mechanism). Hard-gate vector preserved. BG-10 preserved. C-FF12 / C-FF13 respected. No gate upgrade is performed or implied by this section.

# UQFC-16 — Force-Sector Precision Likelihood
*Phase 7 — Precision comparison · gate UQF-13 · drafted 2026-06-08*

> **Gate card — UQF-13: Precision-force phenomenology** *(auto-derived from §3.3 / §4.4, the single source of truth per §3.0; any discrepancy with this chapter is a drafting bug)*
>
> | Field | Value |
> |---|---|
> | Tier | **CANDIDATE (Tier-1)** with **AUDIT (Tier-2)** per UQC-8 inheritance. |
> | Required certificate | Two-tier per UQC-8 inheritance. **Tier-1** (specification): per observable, name the required calculation, the constraint experiment, and the partner toolchain (HEPfit, CKMfitter, NuFIT, flavio, RBC-UKQCD, etc.). **Tier-2** (values): explicitly deferred to partner-community execution; this paper produces **no numerical predictions**. |
> | Frozen inputs | Paper 2 §11 sanity targets; UQF-7 (fermion quantization for flavor structure); regulator compatibility (C-FF9). |
> | Pass / fail | Pass (Tier-1): every observable in the force-sector precision set has a named calculation, named experiment, named partner. Pass (Tier-2): not in this paper. Fail (Tier-1): any observable missing one of the three named pieces. |
> | Downgrade | Tier-1 incompleteness → UQF-13 drops to AUDIT; the precision-likelihood claim becomes "Tier-1 partial specification." |
