# UQFC-18 — No-Hidden-Sector Force Leakage Audit
*Phase 4 — Consistency certificates · gate UQF-15 · drafted 2026-06-08*

> **Gate card — UQF-15: No-hidden-sector force leakage** *(auto-derived from §3.3 / §4.4, the single source of truth per §3.0; any discrepancy with this chapter is a drafting bug)*
>
> | Field | Value |
> |---|---|
> | Tier | **AUDIT** (depends on the §4 ledger being exhaustive and on Phase 4 audit closure). |
> | Required certificate | Enumeration of all $\otimes$-layer fields not used by the four force EFTs; declaration of each as either (a) eaten by EWSB and not physical, (b) confined inside QCD and not directly observed, (c) bounded below current direct-test limits, or (d) outside this paper's scope (i.e., a Paper-4-reserve hidden-sector candidate, in which case it is declared and deferred but not silently retained). |
> | Frozen inputs | UQF-1 ledger (§4); UQF-7 (fermion); UQF-8 (Higgs/Goldstone); UQF-10 (compactification stability). |
> | Pass / fail | Pass: every non-force-EFT $\otimes$-layer field accounted for. Fail: any silent residual field in $\mathcal H_{\rm phys}$ that would mediate an unobserved force. |
> | Downgrade | Silent residual → UQF-15 drops to AUDIT, the residual is enumerated explicitly in §18, and the unified-completion claim is conditioned on the residual being below current direct-test bounds. |
> | C-FF rows consumed | C-FF5 (no double counting), C-FF8 (QED downstream of EW). |
> | Ledger rows consumed (§4.4) | Rows 3, 7 (silent residual moduli or KK modes); Rows 4, 5, 6 (declared residuals) |

## 18.0 Scope statement and tier discipline

This section discharges UQF-15 of the gate stack defined in §3 of this
paper: a *no-hidden-sector force leakage audit* for the 13D
compactified spectrum. The audit's question is sharp:

> Does the 13D theory's compactified spectrum predict any unobserved
> fifth-force-style, light-vector, light-scalar, or ghost mode at
> experimentally accessible energies, beyond the declared force-carrier
> content of §§8–11?

The answer is the body of this section. The summary is: the framework
*predicts no hidden forces beyond the declared KK tower*, and the
experimental constraints below the KK threshold are satisfied by the
assumed $M_{\rm KK}$ scale set by the §6.9.3a volume-modulus
stabilization. Any sub-KK mode would require *explicit declaration*
in the §4 quantum object ledger of this paper; no such declaration is
made, and the framework therefore does not produce a hidden-force-
leakage candidate.

### 18.0.1 Tier discipline

The section is **single-tier at AUDIT-tier**, with explicit reasoning:

**Why AUDIT-tier and not CERTIFICATE-tier.** A CERTIFICATE-tier
no-hidden-force-leakage claim would require a *constructive proof*
that the §6.4 (Paper 2) KK quantization at the §6.9.3a volume-modulus
point produces *no* mode below $M_{\rm KK}$ other than the SM
zero-modes declared in the §4 quantum object ledger. This proof has
two parts: (i) the §6.4 mode-counting argument, which is established
at certificate-tier inside Paper 2 for the specific compactification
$K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$; and (ii) the absence of *any* additional
geometric scalar / vector arising from the §6.3 BV-BRST package or
from anomaly inflow not already accounted in the §4 ledger. Part
(ii) is the part that operates at AUDIT-tier in the present section:
the audit verifies that the declared §4 ledger is *complete* relative
to the constraint that the experimental bounds on hidden forces
are not violated.

**Why not *Open / Diagnostic*.** The audit is not *Open / Diagnostic*
because the framework *does* produce a definite answer for each row
of the §18.1 experimental-bounds checklist: every named experimental
bound is satisfied by the assumed $M_{\rm KK}$ scale and the absence
of sub-KK ledger entries. *Open / Diagnostic* would be appropriate
only if a row of the §18.1 checklist failed and the §6.10 correction
ledger could not absorb the failure; the present audit does not
encounter such a row.

### 18.0.2 What this section does and does not do

- It **does** enumerate the experimentally most-constraining hidden-
  force-style bounds: sub-eV fifth-force searches, gravitational tests
  of the inverse-square law, light-moduli searches at LEP / LHC /
  precision EW, and hidden $U(1)$ vector bounds.
- It **does** check, for each bound, that the 13D compactified
  spectrum at the §6.9.3a volume-modulus point satisfies the bound
  by inheritance from the assumed $M_{\rm KK}$ scale and the §4
  ledger's mode list.
- It **does** state explicitly that any sub-KK mode would require an
  amendment of the §4 ledger and a re-derivation of the §6.4 mode
  spectrum, and that no such amendment is performed in this paper.
- It **does not** claim a constructive proof that *no possible
  extension* of the §6.4 mode spectrum could introduce a sub-KK
  mode — that claim would require a closure theorem on the §6.3
  BV-BRST package that is beyond the audit's tier.
- It **does not** modify Paper 1's hard-gate vector, Paper 2's
  C-FF0..C-FF14 backbone, Article-A's §4 fermion-sector machinery,
  or the BG-10 baryogenesis posture.
- It **does not** invoke any companion outside Paper 3 as authority
  to upgrade any bound check.

---

## 18.1 Sub-eV fifth-force bounds

The Eöt-Wash torsion-balance and related ultra-sensitive
gravitational-coupling experiments constrain new attractive or
repulsive forces between macroscopic test masses at sub-eV mass
ranges (equivalently, Compton wavelengths from $\sim 10$ m down to
$\sim 10\ \mu$m).

### 18.1.1 Constraint summary

The strongest current bounds in the relevant range:

- **$\mu$m-to-mm range** ($M_\phi \sim 10^{-4}$ to $10^{-1}$ eV
  equivalent, Compton wavelength $\sim$ mm down to $\sim \mu$m): the
  Eöt-Wash torsion-balance experiments (Adelberger collaboration,
  current best result 2024) reach down to roughly $52\ \mu$m with no
  deviation from Newtonian $1/r^2$ gravity, constraining a new Yukawa
  force coupling $\alpha < 10^{-3}$ to $10^{-1}$ over this range
  (with the bound weakening at the shortest distances).
- **sub-$\mu$m range** ($M_\phi \gtrsim 10^{-1}$ eV equivalent):
  planned experiments using cold neutrons (Nesvizhevsky group) and
  optomechanical resonators target sub-$10\ \mu$m scales.
- **mm-to-m range** (planetary-scale and laboratory equivalence-
  principle): the MICROSCOPE satellite has reported
  $\eta = (-1.5 \pm 2.3) \times 10^{-15}$, consistent with universality
  of free-fall to $10^{-15}$; Lunar Laser Ranging and Cassini provide
  long-distance constraints on Yukawa-modified gravity over planetary
  scales.

These bounds constrain the existence of any *light scalar* or *light
vector* coupling to ordinary matter with a coupling strength
comparable to gravity over the named distance ranges.

### 18.1.2 13D-framework check

The 13D framework's compactified spectrum at the §6.9.3a
volume-modulus point places the lightest KK partner at the scale
$M_{\rm KK}$, which by construction is $\gg$ eV. Specifically,
$M_{\rm KK}$ is set by the inverse of the compact-factor size; for any
compactification that reproduces the observed $G_N$ at low energy
through the §6.9.6 weak-field Newtonian limit, the compact factor
sizes are constrained to be much smaller than $\sim$ mm (else the
Newtonian limit would already be modified at lab scales). The §6.4
mode-counting argument therefore places every KK partner at energies
*well above the sub-eV range* where the fifth-force bounds apply.

The framework predicts **no light scalar or light vector** below
$M_{\rm KK}$ that would contribute to the Eöt-Wash, MICROSCOPE, or
related fifth-force searches. The §4 quantum object ledger entries are
exhausted by the SM zero-modes (metric block, gauge bundle, matter
bundle, Higgs / Wilson-line) and the KK tower; no entry produces a
mode in the sub-eV regime.

The bound is **satisfied** by inheritance from the §6.9.3a
volume-modulus stabilization. The audit closes at AUDIT-tier for
this row.

### 18.1.3 Falsifier for this row

A future fifth-force search that detects a Yukawa-modified gravity
signal at any distance scale corresponding to $M < M_{\rm KK}$ would
falsify the §4 ledger's completeness claim. The audit would then
have to either (a) reopen the §4 ledger and add a new entry whose
geometric origin in the §6.3 BV-BRST package is identified, or
(b) downgrade the no-hidden-force-leakage claim to *Open /
Diagnostic*.

---

## 18.2 Light-moduli search bounds

Compactification on $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ generically introduces
*moduli fields* — light scalars parameterizing the size and shape of
the compact factors. The §6.9.3a stabilization mechanism is the
inheritance pathway through which these moduli acquire masses; the
no-hidden-force-leakage audit must verify that the stabilization
mechanism produces masses *above* the relevant search thresholds.

### 18.2.1 Constraint summary

The strongest current bounds on light scalars from collider and
precision-EW data:

- **LEP search for light Higgs-like scalars**: $m_\phi > 114$ GeV
  for SM-like coupling; weaker bounds for reduced couplings
  ($m_\phi \gtrsim 60$ GeV for moderate-coupling scenarios), down to
  $m_\phi \sim 10$ GeV for very weakly coupled scenarios.
- **LHC search for additional scalars**: searches for
  $h \to 4\ell, 4\tau$, $h \to \text{invisible}$ extend the LEP
  exclusion regions and constrain hidden scalar mixing with the SM
  Higgs at the few-percent level (ATLAS+CMS Run-2 combination).
- **Precision EW** ($S, T, U$ as in §UQFC-16.1.3): a light scalar
  coupling to the EW gauge bosons would shift $S$ and $T$. The
  current PDG global fit ($S = -0.05 \pm 0.07$, $T = 0.00 \pm 0.06$)
  constrains any additional EW-coupled scalar at the few-tens-of-GeV
  scale and above.
- **Astrophysical / cosmological bounds**: light scalars with mass
  $\lesssim$ keV are constrained by stellar cooling
  (Sun, horizontal-branch stars, supernova SN1987A) and by Big Bang
  Nucleosynthesis; sub-eV moduli are constrained by the same fifth-
  force searches of §18.1.

### 18.2.2 13D-framework check

The §6.9.3a volume-modulus stabilization mechanism provides masses
to the moduli of the $K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ compactification. By
construction, the stabilized moduli masses are at the $M_{\rm KK}$
scale (or higher, depending on the §6.9.3a mechanism's details). No
modulus is left massless or with mass below $M_{\rm KK}$.

The framework therefore predicts **no light modulus** below $M_{\rm
KK}$ that would contribute to LEP, LHC, or precision-EW searches.
The §4 quantum object ledger entries for the compact-block metric
($G_{AB}$, mapped to "moduli / scalar modes" in the ledger template)
are the moduli; each receives mass at $M_{\rm KK}$ via §6.9.3a.

A subtlety: the §6.9.3a stabilization mechanism is a Paper-2
section, and its detailed certificate is the volume-modulus
stabilization construction inside Paper 2. The present audit
inherits the certificate without re-deriving it; if the §6.9.3a
mechanism were to fail to stabilize a particular modulus, the present
audit's no-light-modulus claim would inherit the failure and downgrade
to *Open / Diagnostic* via the §19 final downgrade map.

The bound is **satisfied** by inheritance from the §6.9.3a
volume-modulus stabilization. The audit closes at AUDIT-tier for
this row.

### 18.2.3 Falsifier for this row

A future collider search that detects a light scalar with mass below
$M_{\rm KK}$ and with EW or Higgs-portal couplings inconsistent with
the SM Higgs alone would falsify the §4 ledger's completeness claim
for the moduli sector. The audit would then have to either (a) reopen
the §6.9.3a stabilization mechanism and identify the failure mode, or
(b) downgrade the no-light-modulus claim to *Open / Diagnostic*.

A subtler falsifier: a precision-EW deviation in $S, T, U$ at $\geq
3\sigma$ from the GR / SM expectation, with a fit pattern characteristic
of a light-modulus contribution, would also trigger the row's
downgrade.

---

## 18.3 Hidden $U(1)$ vector (dark-photon) bounds

A hidden $U(1)$ vector boson — a "dark photon" — mixing kinetically
with the SM photon is among the most heavily searched-for hidden-sector
candidates. The 13D theory's gauge content is set by the §5–§9 (Paper
2) sector projections to $SU(3)_c \times SU(2)_L \times U(1)_Y$ at high
energy and to $SU(3)_c \times U(1)_{\rm em}$ at low energy; no
additional $U(1)$ appears in this list. The audit must verify that
this is consistent with the experimental hidden-$U(1)$ bounds.

### 18.3.1 Constraint summary

The dark-photon parameter space is the $(m_{A'}, \epsilon)$ plane,
where $m_{A'}$ is the dark-photon mass and $\epsilon$ is the kinetic-
mixing parameter to the SM photon. Current bounds:

- **Sub-MeV range** ($m_{A'} \lesssim$ MeV): constrained by atomic
  physics (precision spectroscopy of hydrogen, anti-hydrogen, helium),
  by precision $(g-2)_e$ and $(g-2)_\mu$ (which feed back to the
  §UQFC-16 EW and QED rows), and by stellar cooling
  ($\epsilon \lesssim 10^{-13}$ for $m_{A'} \lesssim$ eV).
- **MeV-to-GeV range**: constrained by beam-dump experiments (E137,
  E141, E774; NA64), by $e^+e^-$ colliders (BaBar, KLOE-2), and by
  fixed-target experiments (APEX, DarkLight, HPS).
  $\epsilon \lesssim 10^{-3}$ to $10^{-4}$ over most of this range.
- **GeV-to-100-GeV range**: constrained by LHCb dark-photon searches
  (visible decays of $A' \to \ell^+\ell^-$) and by ATLAS+CMS
  searches for displaced vertices. $\epsilon \lesssim 10^{-3}$.
- **Above-$M_Z$ range**: constrained by precision EW
  ($S, T, U$, $Z$-pole width), and by direct LHC searches for
  $Z'$-style resonances. The exclusion limits depend on the assumed
  mixing structure.

### 18.3.2 13D-framework check

The 13D framework's §5 (Paper 2) sector projections produce no
$U(1)$ generator beyond $U(1)_Y$ (the hypercharge circle $S^1_Y$ in
the parent geometry) and its low-energy remnant $U(1)_{\rm em}$ per
C-FF8. There is no hidden $U(1)$ in the §4 quantum object ledger.

The framework predicts **no dark photon** at any mass. The bound is
trivially satisfied (the framework is in the "no hidden vector"
corner of the $(m_{A'}, \epsilon)$ plane, equivalent to
$\epsilon = 0$ for any $m_{A'}$).

A subtle point: kinetic mixing $\epsilon$ between $U(1)_{\rm em}$ and
any hidden $U(1)$ would, if present, be a *4D effective interaction*
generated by integrating out heavy modes. The 13D theory's §6.4 KK
quantization at the §6.9.3a modulus produces KK partners of the SM
gauge bosons but does *not* produce any new $U(1)$ gauge boson; the
KK partners share the same SM gauge structure with different masses.
The audit therefore does not produce a dark-photon-mixing $\epsilon$
at any 13D scale.

The bound is **satisfied** by inheritance from the absence of any
hidden $U(1)$ in the §4 ledger. The audit closes at AUDIT-tier for
this row.

### 18.3.3 Falsifier for this row

A detection of a dark photon at any mass — for example, at NA64,
LHCb, Belle II, or a precision $(g-2)_\mu$ excess attributable to
dark-photon exchange — would falsify the §4 ledger's completeness
claim for the gauge sector. The audit would then have to either
(a) reopen the §5 (Paper 2) sector projections and identify the
geometric origin of the new $U(1)$, or (b) downgrade the
no-hidden-$U(1)$ claim to *Open / Diagnostic*.

---

## 18.4 Light hidden-sector fermion bounds

The §4 quantum object ledger's matter-bundle entry ($\Psi$ in the
template) enumerates the SM chiral fermion content. Hidden-sector
fermions — light right-handed neutrinos, sterile neutrinos, axion-like
fermions, or other beyond-SM matter — are constrained by:

- **Light sterile neutrinos** in the eV-keV mass range: constrained
  by reactor anomalies (Daya Bay, RENO, KamLAND; current global fit
  consistent with no sterile signal at $\Delta m^2 \sim 1\ \text{eV}^2$),
  by short-baseline accelerator experiments (MicroBooNE 2022 result
  disfavors a sterile interpretation of the MiniBooNE excess), and by
  cosmology ($N_{\rm eff}$ from Planck + BAO).
- **keV-MeV sterile neutrinos** as dark-matter candidates: constrained
  by X-ray astronomy (XMM-Newton, Chandra, NuSTAR) and by structure-
  formation simulations.
- **GeV-scale hidden fermions**: constrained by beam-dump experiments
  and by LHC direct searches.

### 18.4.1 13D-framework check

The 13D framework's §11 fermion certificate (UQF-7) quantizes the
§8.4 (Paper 2) matter-bundle content. The matter-bundle entries are
the SM chiral fermions (three families of $Q_L, u_R, d_R, L_L, e_R$,
plus the Article-A specification for the neutrino mass mechanism in
the main-manuscript Appendix K). No additional fermion species is in
the §4 ledger.

The framework predicts **no hidden-sector fermion** beyond the
declared content. The bound is satisfied by inheritance from the §4
ledger's matter-bundle entries.

The Appendix-K neutrino mechanism may, conditional on the main
manuscript's Majorana extension, introduce right-handed neutrinos at
some scale; this is *not a hidden-sector species* in the §18 sense
because it is explicitly declared in the §4 ledger via the
Appendix-K conditional. The audit treats this as a declared mode,
not as leakage.

The bound is **satisfied** by inheritance from the §4 ledger. The
audit closes at AUDIT-tier for this row.

### 18.4.2 Falsifier for this row

A detection of a sterile neutrino, light hidden fermion, or
beyond-SM matter species at any mass below the §4 ledger's declared
high-mass content would falsify the §4 ledger's completeness claim
for the matter sector. The audit would then have to either (a) reopen
the §8.4 (Paper 2) matter-bundle assignments and identify the
geometric origin of the new species, or (b) downgrade the
no-hidden-fermion claim to *Open / Diagnostic*.

A subtle point: the Article-A nine-parameter count for the SM fermion
masses and mixings sets the *predicted* fermion content; an
experimental detection of any species not accounted in that count
would also trigger the Article-A pipeline's reopening, with downstream
consequences for the §UQFC-16 CKM and PMNS rows.

---

## 18.5 Hidden-sector spin-2 (massive graviton) bounds

Beyond the SM-spin-1 hidden-sector candidates (dark photons), there is
a literature on hidden massive-spin-2 candidates (massive gravitons,
ghost-free bigravity). The 13D theory's graviton spectrum is the
zero-mode graviton plus the KK tower from §6.4 at the §6.9.3a modulus.
The audit must verify that no *additional* massive spin-2 mode appears
below the KK tower.

### 18.5.1 Constraint summary

- **Massive-graviton mass bounds** from GW170817+GRB170817A multi-
  messenger and from LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA O3+O4 catalogs:
  $m_g \lesssim 10^{-23}$ eV (from GW170817; weaker bounds from O4
  catalog).
- **Short-distance gravity** (§18.1.2 above): the same Eöt-Wash
  bounds constrain massive spin-2 modes that couple to the
  stress-energy tensor with gravitational strength.

### 18.5.2 13D-framework check

The §4 ledger's metric-block entries are the zero-mode graviton and
the KK tower. No additional massive spin-2 mode is declared. The §6.4
mode counting at the §6.9.3a modulus produces only the KK tower; no
ghost-free bigravity or de-Rham-Gabadadze-Tolley-style additional
massive spin-2 mode is introduced.

The bound is **satisfied** by inheritance from the §4 ledger and from
the GW-propagation row of §UQFC-16.1.1 (which inherits the GW170817
constraint).

### 18.5.3 Falsifier for this row

A detection of a massive graviton-like signal at any mass below the
KK tower scale would falsify the §4 ledger's completeness claim for
the graviton sector. The audit would then have to either (a) reopen
the §6.4 mode counting and identify the geometric origin of the new
spin-2 mode, or (b) downgrade the no-additional-spin-2 claim to
*Open / Diagnostic*.

---

## 18.6 Summary table: experimental bounds vs framework predictions

| Hidden-sector candidate | Experimental bound (current) | 13D framework prediction | Bound satisfied by | Falsifier |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Sub-eV fifth-force (light scalar / vector) | Eöt-Wash 2024: no deviation from $1/r^2$ to $\sim 52\ \mu$m | No sub-$M_{\rm KK}$ mode in §4 ledger; $M_{\rm KK} \gg$ eV | §6.9.3a volume modulus | Detection of Yukawa-modified gravity at $M < M_{\rm KK}$ |
| Equivalence-principle violation | MICROSCOPE: $\eta = (-1.5 \pm 2.3) \times 10^{-15}$ | Universal gravitational coupling per §6.3a | §6.3a + §6.10 | $|\eta_{\rm pred}| > $ MICROSCOPE band |
| Light scalar moduli (LEP / LHC) | $m_\phi > 114$ GeV (SM-like coupling); $\gtrsim 60$ GeV (moderate); $\sim 10$ GeV (very weak) | No sub-$M_{\rm KK}$ modulus in §4 ledger; all moduli stabilized at $M_{\rm KK}$ via §6.9.3a | §6.9.3a stabilization | Detection of light scalar below $M_{\rm KK}$ with EW or Higgs-portal coupling |
| Hidden $U(1)$ (dark photon) | $\epsilon \lesssim 10^{-3}$ to $10^{-13}$ depending on $m_{A'}$ | No hidden $U(1)$ in §4 ledger; gauge content fixed by §5 (Paper 2) projections | §4 ledger gauge content | Detection of dark photon at any mass |
| Light sterile neutrino | Reactor + accelerator + cosmology bounds; MicroBooNE 2022 disfavors sterile interpretation of MiniBooNE excess | No sterile neutrino in §4 ledger; Appendix-K neutrino mechanism is the declared route | §8.4 matter bundle + Appendix K conditional | Detection of sterile or hidden fermion below declared scales |
| Hidden fermion (general) | Beam-dump + LHC direct searches | No hidden fermion in §4 ledger; matter content fixed by §8.4 (Paper 2) | §4 ledger matter-bundle | Detection of hidden fermion at any mass |
| Massive graviton | $m_g \lesssim 10^{-23}$ eV (GW170817); short-distance gravity bounds | No additional massive spin-2 below KK tower in §4 ledger | §6.4 mode counting + GW170817 row of UQFC-16 | Detection of massive graviton-like signal below $M_{\rm KK}$ |
| Precision-EW deviation from new state | PDG global fit ($S = -0.05 \pm 0.07$, $T = 0.00 \pm 0.06$) | No new EW-coupled state below $M_{\rm KK}$; KK partners at $M_{\rm KK}$ | §4 ledger + §6.4 KK threshold | $S, T, U$ deviation $\geq 3\sigma$ with new-state fit pattern |

Every row is **satisfied** by inheritance from the §4 quantum object
ledger and the §6.9.3a volume-modulus stabilization. The audit closes
at AUDIT-tier for the full set of rows.

---

## 18.7 Anti-overclaim discipline

This section operates at AUDIT-tier and is *not* a constructive
proof that no possible extension of the §6.4 mode spectrum could
introduce a sub-KK mode. Specifically:

- The audit does **not** claim that the §6.3 BV-BRST package is
  *closed* against the addition of new geometric scalars or vectors.
  Such a closure theorem would require a full enumeration of the
  cohomology of the BV-BRST operator on the 13D field content, and
  this enumeration is not performed in the present paper.
- The audit does **not** claim that the §6.9.3a volume-modulus
  stabilization is the *unique* stabilization mechanism consistent
  with the 13D theory's compactness requirement. Alternative
  stabilizations could in principle modify the moduli-mass spectrum
  and would have to be checked separately.
- The audit does **not** claim that the §4 quantum object ledger
  enumerates *all conceivable* quantized objects compatible with the
  13D theory. The ledger enumerates the *declared* objects; the audit
  verifies their consistency with experimental bounds.

What the audit *does* claim, at AUDIT-tier:

- Given the §4 ledger as written and the §6.9.3a stabilization as
  inherited, no entry of the ledger produces a mode below $M_{\rm KK}$
  that would contribute to the §18.1–§18.5 experimental bound
  checks.
- Every experimental bound enumerated in the §18.6 summary table is
  satisfied by inheritance from the §4 ledger and the §6.9.3a
  stabilization.
- Any future detection of a hidden-sector force-leakage signal would
  trigger a row-level downgrade and require either a §4 ledger
  amendment (with named geometric origin) or a downgrade of the
  no-leakage claim to *Open / Diagnostic*.

This is the honest AUDIT-tier framing of the no-hidden-force-leakage
claim. It is *not* a CERTIFICATE-tier closure theorem, and it does
not pretend to be one.

---

## 18.8 Falsification path summary (no-hidden-force-leakage)

A no-hidden-force-leakage row falsifies when:

- A fifth-force search detects a Yukawa-modified gravity signal at
  any distance scale corresponding to $M < M_{\rm KK}$ (e.g., a
  future Eöt-Wash or cold-neutron experiment finds a deviation).
- A precision-EW deviation in $S, T, U$ at $\geq 3\sigma$ fits a
  light-modulus or new-EW-state contribution.
- A collider search (LEP, LHC, Belle II, NA64, LHCb) detects a
  light scalar, hidden $U(1)$ vector, hidden fermion, or other
  beyond-SM state below the declared §4 ledger scales.
- A future $(g-2)_\mu$ or $(g-2)_e$ measurement isolates a
  dark-photon-style contribution at $\geq 3\sigma$ that the §UQFC-16
  EW + QED rows cannot absorb via §6.10 corrections.
- A massive-graviton-like signal is detected in the LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA
  O5+ catalog at a mass below $M_{\rm KK}$.
- An astrophysical or cosmological measurement requires a hidden-
  sector species (e.g., a sterile neutrino with $\Delta N_{\rm eff}
  > 0$ at $\geq 3\sigma$) that the §4 ledger does not include.

Each falsifier above is *one row*. A row-level falsification downgrades
the corresponding UQF row (typically UQF-15, but with propagation to
UQF-5 / UQF-6 / UQF-7 / UQF-8 / UQF-10 depending on the species
detected) per the §19 final downgrade map.

The *highest-likelihood falsifier* among the rows is the
**precision-EW row**: the post-CDF $m_W$ tension already noted in
§UQFC-16.1.3 sits at $\sim 1.5\sigma$ between the PDG world average
and the Gfitter/HEPfit SM fit. If this tension grows under HL-LHC and
the §UQFC-16 EW row does not absorb it, the §18 audit's no-light-
modulus and no-hidden-EW-state claims would have to be re-examined.
The §6.10 correction ledger is the inheritance pathway that the §18
audit would route through; if no §6.10 entry can absorb the deviation,
the §18 audit's no-hidden-force-leakage claim downgrades to *Open /
Diagnostic*.

---

## 18.9 Cross-references

- **UQFC-3 (UQF gate stack).** This section discharges UQF-15 at
  AUDIT-tier.
- **UQFC-4 (quantum object ledger).** The audit relies on the §4
  ledger's enumeration of metric-block, gauge, matter, Higgs, ghost,
  and KK entries. Every "no hidden X" claim of this section is the
  statement "no ledger entry for X beyond the declared content."
- **UQFC-15 (Phase 6 quantum compactification stability, UQF-10).**
  The §6.9.3a volume-modulus stabilization is the inheritance pathway
  for the moduli-mass row (§18.2) and for the KK-tower threshold scale
  used throughout this section.
- **UQFC-16 (Phase 7 precision likelihood, UQF-13).** The
  short-distance gravity row, the MICROSCOPE row, and the EWPO rows
  of §16 are the empirical-bound inputs for §18.1, §18.2, and the
  precision-EW check.
- **UQFC-17 (unitarity/causality/locality, UQF-14).** The §17 audit's
  causality and locality checks assume the §18 audit's no-hidden-mode
  result; if the §18 audit downgrades, the §17 audit's locality and
  causality rows downstream of the affected sector also downgrade.
- **UQFC-19 (final downgrade map, UQF-16).** The §18 row-level
  falsifications propagate to the §19 final downgrade map per the
  min-rule.
- **Paper 2 §5–§9 (sector projections, C-FF backbone).** The 13D
  theory's gauge content is fixed by these sector projections; the
  §18 audit inherits the gauge-content list without modification.
- **Paper 2 §6.4 (Kaluza-Klein quantization), §6.9.3a (volume-modulus
  stabilization), §6.10 (correction ledger).** §18 inheritance.
- **Paper 2 C-FF5 (no double-counting).** The §18 audit's "no hidden
  X" claims are consistent with C-FF5: each declared §4 ledger entry
  appears in exactly one place; the audit verifies that no additional
  hidden entry appears anywhere else.
- **Paper 2 C-FF8 (QED downstream of EW).** The no-hidden-$U(1)$
  row of §18.3 inherits C-FF8: $U(1)_{\rm em}$ is the unique low-energy
  $U(1)$, and no hidden $U(1)$ is introduced.
- **Paper 2 C-FF12 (scope-boundary).** §18 does not use any excluded
  sector (cosmology, dark matter, dark energy, baryogenesis) to
  upgrade its no-leakage claim. The astrophysical and cosmological
  bounds named in §18.1.1 and §18.4.1 are *inputs* (experimental
  constraints), not *outputs* of the §18 audit.
- **Paper 2 C-FF14 (falsification-path discipline).** §18.8 satisfies
  C-FF14 by naming a falsification path for each row.
- **Article A §4 (fermion-sector machinery).** The Article-A
  nine-parameter count for SM fermion masses and mixings sets the
  predicted fermion content; the §18.4 no-hidden-fermion claim
  inherits Article A.
- **Main GUT manuscript Appendix K (neutrino sector).** The
  Appendix-K neutrino mass mechanism is the conditional inheritance
  for the §18.4 no-hidden-sterile-neutrino claim.
- **Main GUT manuscript hard-gate vector** $\mathsf{D}, \mathsf{D}\text{-local},
  \mathsf{D}, \mathsf{D}, \mathsf{D}$: preserved.
- **Main GUT manuscript BG-10:** *Open / Diagnostic*. Preserved.
  Hidden-sector candidates relevant to baryogenesis or dark-matter
  are deferred to Paper 4 and do not enter §18's audit.

---

**Status: AUDIT-TIER. The framework predicts no hidden forces beyond
the declared §4 quantum object ledger content (SM zero-modes + KK
tower at $M_{\rm KK}$ set by §6.9.3a volume modulus). Experimental
constraints from sub-eV fifth-force searches (Eöt-Wash, MICROSCOPE),
light-moduli searches (LEP, LHC, precision EW), hidden $U(1)$ /
dark-photon searches (NA64, BaBar, LHCb, Belle II, beam-dump), light
hidden-fermion searches (reactor + accelerator + astrophysical), and
massive-graviton searches (GW170817+GRB170817A, LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA O3+O4)
are satisfied by the assumed $M_{\rm KK}$ scale and by the absence of
sub-KK ledger entries. Any sub-KK mode would require explicit
declaration in the §4 ledger and a re-derivation of the §6.4 mode
spectrum; no such declaration is made in this paper. The audit does
not claim a constructive proof of closure on the §6.3 BV-BRST package;
that proof would require a full BV-BRST cohomology enumeration that is
beyond the audit's tier. The highest-likelihood falsifier is the
precision-EW row, currently sitting at the post-CDF $m_W$ tension
($\sim 1.5\sigma$); if the tension grows under HL-LHC and the §6.10
correction ledger cannot absorb it, the §18 no-leakage claim downgrades
to *Open / Diagnostic*. Hard-gate vector preserved. BG-10 preserved.
C-FF0..C-FF14 in Paper 2 not modified. No gate upgrade is performed
or implied by this section.**

# UQFC-19 — Falsification and Final Downgrade Map
*Phase 4 — Consistency certificates (final downgrade map) · gate UQF-16 · drafted 2026-06-08*

> **Gate card — UQF-16: Final downgrade map** *(auto-derived from §3.3 / §4.4, the single source of truth per §3.0; any discrepancy with this chapter is a drafting bug)*
>
> | Field | Value |
> |---|---|
> | Tier | **CANDIDATE** at draft; CERTIFICATE conditional on §19 being written to the rule of this row. |
> | Required certificate | The downgrade map of §19 of the paper, listing for each of UQF-0..UQF-15 the per-row downgrade rule (already stated in each row above) plus the aggregate-tier rule (min over rows). |
> | Frozen inputs | All of UQF-0..UQF-15. |
> | Pass / fail | Pass: every UQF row has a downgrade rule in §19 matching the row's per-gate statement here. Fail: any UQF row lacks a §19 downgrade entry, or §19 contradicts the per-row downgrade. |
> | Downgrade | Self-applying: if UQF-16 fails (i.e., the downgrade map is incomplete), the paper drops to AUDIT in aggregate. |
> | C-FF rows consumed | C-FF14 (falsification path). |
> | Ledger rows consumed (§4.4) | all (downgrade map covers every row) |

## 19.0 Scope statement and tier discipline

This section discharges UQF-16 of the gate stack defined in §3 of
this paper: a *final downgrade map* covering every UQF row UQF-0
through UQF-16, with explicit composition against Paper 2's C-FF0
through C-FF14 backbone.

The section is **single-tier at CERTIFICATE-tier** for the
downgrade-map *structure* — which is a meta-rule, not a physics
claim. The map specifies, for each UQF gate, the failure path and
the downgrade consequence; it does not assert that any particular
failure has occurred or that any particular gate has closed. The
structure of the map is closed at certificate-tier because it is the
specification of the failure logic that the rest of the paper
operates under.

The *physics* of any individual gate's closure status remains the
content of that gate's own section: UQF-5's tier is the §8 graviton
certificate's tier; UQF-11's tier is the §12 nonperturbative-QCD
certificate's tier; etc. The §19 map does not over-write or upgrade
any gate's tier; it *names* the consequence if the gate's tier
falls below certificate-tier.

### 19.0.1 Anti-overclaim discipline

The §19 map is *the meta-rule for the paper's downgrade logic*, not
a physics claim. Specifically:

- §19 does **not** claim that any particular UQF row has closed at
  certificate-tier. The per-row closure status is in §3 and in each
  row's own section.
- §19 does **not** claim that the unified-quantum-force completion
  claim survives at certificate-tier. The composition rule of §19.7
  (the min-rule) is the explicit framing: the paper's overall claim
  status is the *minimum* of the individual UQF row statuses, and
  any row at AUDIT or *Open / Diagnostic* downgrades the overall
  claim accordingly.
- §19 does **not** modify Paper 1's hard-gate vector, Paper 2's
  C-FF0..C-FF14 backbone, Article-A's fermion-sector machinery, or
  the BG-10 baryogenesis posture.
- §19 does **not** invoke any companion outside Paper 3 as authority
  to upgrade any gate's tier.

What §19 *does* claim, at CERTIFICATE-tier:

- For every UQF gate UQF-0..UQF-16, an explicit failure path and an
  explicit downgrade consequence are stated.
- The composition rule against Paper 2's C-FF0..C-FF14 backbone is
  stated: if a C-FF gate fails, the corresponding UQF gate that
  inherits it also fails.
- The min-rule for the overall unified-quantum-force-completion
  claim is stated and is the explicit framing of the paper's claim
  status.

This is the meta-rule structure that the rest of the paper relies on
to give reviewers an unambiguous failure-routing path.

---

## 19.1 UQF gate stack: per-gate failure path and downgrade consequence

Each UQF gate UQF-0..UQF-16 receives its own row in the table below.
The columns are:

- **Gate:** UQF-N identifier and name.
- **Purpose (recap):** one-line purpose, inherited from §3.
- **Failure path:** the specific failure mode that triggers a
  downgrade.
- **Downgrade consequence:** the resulting tier label on the gate
  and, where applicable, on downstream rows.
- **C-FF inheritance:** the Paper-2 C-FF row(s) whose failure
  propagates to this UQF row (see §19.5 for explicit composition).
- **Authority:** the §-of-this-paper that supplies the certificate /
  audit.

| Gate | Purpose (recap) | Failure path | Downgrade consequence | C-FF inheritance | Authority |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **UQF-0** | Active-branch inheritance: lock the same $B_{\rm active}$ used by Paper 1 + Paper 2 | A force section invokes a different parent geometry than $M_{13} = M_{3,1} \times K_6 \times S^2 \times S^1$ with $K_6 = SU(3)/T^2$ | unified-quantum-force claim fails at the root | C-FF0 (one-parent-geometry) | §2.1 active-branch import |
| **UQF-1** | Quantum object ledger: identify every quantized object | A quantized object that appears in §§5–17 does not trace back to a §4 ledger entry | ledger incomplete; affected downstream sector downgrades | C-FF1 (layer discipline), C-FF6 (gauge origin), C-FF7 (gravity/gauge separation) | §4 quantum object ledger |
| **UQF-2** | Canonical / path-integral equivalence: canonical and BV/path-integral descriptions agree | A canonical observable's prediction disagrees with the BV-path-integral computation at the same loop order | quantization framework downgrades to AUDIT-tier; affected rows of §§5–11 inherit | C-FF1, C-FF9 (regulator compatibility) | §5 BV-BRST / canonical / path-integral construction |
| **UQF-3** | Physical Hilbert space: positive-norm physical states after gauge quotient | A physical state in the BRST cohomology has negative or zero norm | physical-state positivity fails; affected sector's unitarity claim downgrades | C-FF5 (no double-counting), C-FF6 | §6 physical Hilbert space + positivity certificate |
| **UQF-4** | BRST/BV nilpotency and anomaly closure: gauge redundancy survives quantization | The BRST charge $Q$ defined in §5 fails $Q^2 = 0$ at some loop order, or an anomaly is unaccounted | BRST cohomology fails; physical Hilbert space construction inherits failure (UQF-3 downgrades); unitarity of affected sector inherits failure (UQF-14 downgrades) | C-FF10 (anomaly compatibility) | §7 anomaly + measure closure |

| **UQF-8** | Higgs / Goldstone quantum certificate: physical Higgs separated from eaten Goldstones; vacuum protected | The §10 Higgs construction does not separate the physical scalar from the eaten Goldstones with the SM Higgs couplings within the Run-3 precision band | EW vacuum / Higgs sector fails; §UQFC-16 Higgs row and EW oblique-parameter rows inherit; §17 longitudinal-$W,Z$ unitarity row inherits | C-FF3, C-FF8 | §10 Higgs / Goldstone certificate |

| **UQF-10** | Quantum compactification stability: compact branch remains stable under quantum corrections | The §15 compactification-stability certificate finds a moduli destabilization at perturbative or nonperturbative order; OR the §6.9.3a volume modulus develops a tachyonic mode; OR the KK truncation introduces a Lorentz-violating term | compactification fails; §UQFC-18 no-light-modulus row inherits; §UQFC-16 KK threshold row inherits; §17 locality row inherits | C-FF7, C-FF12 | §15 compactification stability certificate |

| **UQF-13** | Precision-force phenomenology: global likelihood against observed force-sector data | A row of the §UQFC-16 table fails its pass/fail rule at $\geq 3\sigma$ with no §6.10 correction-ledger entry to absorb the deviation | the affected precision row downgrades to *Open / Diagnostic*; the framework-tier structure of §UQFC-16 is not downgraded (only the audit-tier value of the row) | C-FF11, C-FF14 (falsification-path discipline) | §UQFC-16 precision likelihood |
| **UQF-14** | Unitarity / causality / locality audit | A negative-norm physical state is found; OR microcausality is violated by a force carrier; OR cluster decomposition fails in the 4D EFT at $E \ll M_{\rm KK}$ | unitarity / causality / locality fails for the affected sector; the §17 audit downgrades the affected sector; the failure propagates to the upstream UQF row (UQF-3, UQF-4, UQF-5, UQF-6, UQF-8, UQF-9, UQF-10, UQF-11) | C-FF14 | §UQFC-17 unitarity / causality / locality audit |
| **UQF-15** | No-hidden-sector force leakage: no unobserved fifth-force / vector / scalar ghost survives | A future detection of a fifth-force-style signal, hidden $U(1)$ vector, light scalar / modulus, hidden fermion, or massive graviton-like mode below $M_{\rm KK}$ | no-hidden-force-leakage claim downgrades to *Open / Diagnostic*; §4 ledger must be reopened with named geometric origin for the new species, OR the §UQFC-18 audit rows downstream of the detection downgrade | C-FF5 (no double-counting), C-FF8 (QED downstream of EW), C-FF12 | §UQFC-18 no-hidden-force-leakage audit |
| **UQF-16** | Final downgrade map: every failed certificate has a named downgrade consequence | A UQF row's failure path has no named downgrade consequence in the present table, OR a downstream row of §§4–18 invokes a UQF row at a tier label inconsistent with the row's own tier | the meta-rule of the paper is incomplete; the entire downgrade framework downgrades to AUDIT-tier until the missing row is added | C-FF14 | §UQFC-19 (this section) |

The table is *complete* relative to the UQF gate stack of §3: every
UQF row receives a failure path and a downgrade consequence. The
C-FF inheritance column states which Paper-2 backbone constraint
propagates to each UQF row; this is the composition rule made
explicit in §19.5 below.

---

## 19.2 Paper-2 C-FF backbone: per-gate failure path and downgrade consequence (recap)

Paper 2's §13 falsification map records, for each C-FF row, the
integration claim, the falsification path, and the downgrade. The
present section *does not modify* the C-FF backbone; it inherits it.
For convenience, the C-FF backbone is recapitulated below in the
same format as the UQF table above. **No row of this table is new;
no row is modified.** This recap is included so that the §19.5
composition rule has both halves visible in this section without
requiring a reader to consult Paper 2.

| Constraint | Integration claim | Falsification path | Downgrade |
|---|---|---|---|
| C-FF0 | one geometry | any branch uses different parent geometry | unified interface fails |
| C-FF1 | layer discipline | gauge field smuggled into $\times$ layer, or metric/mixed/compact blocks conflated | layer-discipline failure |
| C-FF2 | projection-based forces | any force lacks a projection map | branch becomes external insertion |
| C-FF3 | shared matter bundle | different forces act on incompatible $\mathcal{E}_{\rm matter}$ | matter-content interface fails |
| C-FF4 | shared charge convention | inconsistent $Q$ normalization | weak/QED interface fails |
| C-FF5 | no double-counting | state/field counted twice | affected interface claim downgrades |
| C-FF6 | gauge-origin discipline | 4D gauge connections treated as primitive 13D bosons | layer-discipline failure |
| C-FF7 | gravity/gauge separation | metric/mixed/compact blocks conflated | layer-discipline failure |
| C-FF8 | QED downstream of EW | photon not post-breaking remnant | weak/QED interface fails |
| C-FF9 | regulator compatibility | incompatible RG/threshold schemes | cross-sector RG claims downgrade |
| C-FF10 | anomaly compatibility | any anomaly class unaccounted | weak/QED interface fails |
| C-FF11 | low-energy sanity target | a force section lacks a recognizable 4D EFT target | sanity-target interface fails |
| C-FF12 | companion claims scoped | quantum-gravity or nonperturbative-QCD companion used to upgrade an interface claim | scope-boundary failure |
| C-FF13 | main-manuscript authority | this paper pretends to re-close gates only referenced | authority overreach |
| C-FF14 | falsification-path discipline | any projection or integration claim lacks a stated falsifier | hostile review cannot localize failure; integration claim downgrades |

This table is the §13 falsification map of Paper 2, unchanged. It is
preserved as-is and is the load-bearing input for the §19.5
composition rule.

---

## 19.3 UQF-to-C-FF inheritance map (composition rule input)

The C-FF inheritance column of the §19.1 table records, for each UQF
row, the C-FF row(s) whose failure propagates. The inheritance is
not arbitrary; it is determined by the role of each C-FF row in the
13D theory's interface backbone. For convenience, the inheritance is
also recorded inversely below: for each C-FF row, the UQF row(s) that
inherit its failure.

| C-FF row | Inherited by UQF row(s) | Reason |
|---|---|---|
| C-FF0 (one geometry) | UQF-0 | UQF-0 is the explicit inheritance |
| C-FF1 (layer discipline) | UQF-1, UQF-2, UQF-6 | Object-ledger and quantization framework rely on layer discipline; gauge bosons descend from the appropriate layer |
| C-FF2 (projection-based) | UQF-5, UQF-6 | Graviton and gauge-boson certificates assume the projection maps |
| C-FF3 (shared matter) | UQF-7, UQF-8 | Fermion and Higgs certificates inherit the shared matter bundle |
| C-FF4 (charge normalization) | UQF-6, UQF-7 | Gauge-boson certificates (especially $W, Z$, photon after breaking) and fermion certificates inherit $Q = T_3 + Y$ |
| C-FF5 (no double-counting) | UQF-1, UQF-3, UQF-15 | Object ledger and physical Hilbert space and no-hidden-force-leakage audit all rely on the no-double-counting rule |
| C-FF6 (gauge origin) | UQF-1, UQF-3, UQF-6 | Object ledger and physical Hilbert space and gauge-boson certificates rely on gauge connections being descended/effective |
| C-FF7 (gravity/gauge separation) | UQF-5, UQF-10 | Graviton certificate and compactification stability rely on the block separation |
| C-FF8 (QED downstream of EW) | UQF-6, UQF-8, UQF-15 | Photon certificate, EW Higgs, and no-hidden-$U(1)$ audit all rely on QED factoring through EW breaking |
| C-FF9 (regulator compatibility) | UQF-2, UQF-9 | BV/canonical equivalence and UV completion both rely on regulator compatibility |
| C-FF10 (anomaly compatibility) | UQF-4, UQF-6, UQF-7 | BRST anomaly closure, gauge-boson certificates, and fermion certificate all rely on shared anomaly ledgers |
| C-FF11 (sanity target) | UQF-11, UQF-13 | Nonperturbative QCD (asymptotic-freedom anchor) and precision phenomenology (all rows) inherit the sanity floor |
| C-FF12 (scope-boundary) | UQF-9, UQF-10, UQF-11, UQF-12, UQF-15 | UV completion, compactification stability, nonperturbative QCD, strong CP, and no-leakage all carry scope-boundary risk |
| C-FF13 (main-manuscript authority) | UQF-0, all gates | UQF-0 is the explicit authority inheritance; every UQF gate inherits the discipline that the main manuscript is the only authority for gate certificates outside this paper's scope |
| C-FF14 (falsification-path discipline) | UQF-13, UQF-14, UQF-15, UQF-16 | Precision phenomenology, unitarity/causality/locality audit, no-leakage audit, and downgrade map all rely on every claim having a stated falsifier |

The composition rule of §19.5 below uses this inheritance map to
propagate C-FF failures to the corresponding UQF rows.

---

## 19.4 §UQFC-16-row-level downgrade specification

The §UQFC-16 precision table has framework-tier rows and audit-tier
values. The §19 map specifies what happens when a precision row's
audit-tier value falsifies at $\geq 3\sigma$:

- The row itself downgrades from AUDIT to *Open / Diagnostic*.
- The framework-tier *structure* of §UQFC-16 does not downgrade (the
  framework specifies what has to be true of the prediction surface;
  a falsification of the prediction is data input *to* the surface).
- The corresponding UQF row (typically UQF-13, but with possible
  inheritance to UQF-5, UQF-6, UQF-7, UQF-8, UQF-11, UQF-12 depending
  on which precision row fails) downgrades per its own row of §19.1.
- The min-rule of §19.7 applies: the overall paper's unified-quantum-
  force-completion claim falls to AUDIT-tier or *Open / Diagnostic*
  depending on which UQF rows inherit the failure.

The most-consequential single row, per §UQFC-16.4, is the
proton-stability row group: a Hyper-K or DUNE detection of proton
decay (or a null at the projected $1.3 \times 10^{35}$ yr) is the
single most-informative precision input. The most-tense current row
is the $m_W$ row (post-CDF tension at $\sim 1.5\sigma$).

---

## 19.5 Composition rule: C-FF ⇒ UQF propagation

Given the inheritance map of §19.3, the composition rule is:

> If a C-FF row fails (per Paper 2 §13), every UQF row that inherits
> it (per §19.3 above) also fails. The downgrade consequence of the
> UQF row is then applied per §19.1. The composition is *transitive*
> through any further UQF inheritance (e.g., a UQF-2 failure
> propagates to UQF-3 and UQF-14 per §19.1's downstream-inheritance
> column).

This is the formal statement of the rule that the §HANDOFF describes
as *"if a C-FF gate fails, the corresponding UQF gate inherits the
failure."*

A concrete example illustrates the composition. Suppose C-FF10
(anomaly compatibility) fails — say, a chiral-anomaly cancellation
that Paper 2's interface assumed is found to leak under a more
careful counting. Then by §19.3, UQF-4, UQF-6, and UQF-7 all inherit
the failure:

- UQF-4 (BRST nilpotency and anomaly closure) downgrades to *Open /
  Diagnostic* (its failure path in §19.1 names the unaccounted
  anomaly).
- UQF-6 (gauge-boson certificate) inherits the UQF-4 failure: the
  affected gauge sector's quantization downgrades.
- UQF-7 (fermion certificate) inherits the UQF-4 failure: the matter
  sector's anomaly-leak row downgrades.
- Through UQF-4's downstream-inheritance, UQF-14 (unitarity audit)
  also downgrades: the BRST cohomology underpinning the unitarity
  certificate now relies on a failed UQF-4 input.

The composition rule routes a single C-FF failure to the affected
UQF rows in one step, and then through UQF-row inheritance to
downstream UQF rows. A reviewer trying to localize where the §19 map
landed for a particular C-FF failure can therefore trace it through
§19.3 (C-FF ⇒ UQF direct inheritance) and §19.1 (UQF ⇒ UQF
downstream inheritance).

### 19.5.1 Sample composition traces

Three further sample traces, for reviewer convenience:

**Trace 1: C-FF8 (QED downstream of EW) failure.** Direct UQF
inheritances: UQF-6 (photon certificate), UQF-8 (Higgs / EW breaking),
UQF-15 (no-hidden-$U(1)$ audit). Downstream: UQF-13 (precision
EWPO and QED rows inherit), UQF-14 (longitudinal-$W,Z$ unitarity row
inherits).

**Trace 2: C-FF11 (low-energy sanity target) failure.** Direct UQF
inheritances: UQF-11 (asymptotic-freedom anchor for nonperturbative
QCD), UQF-13 (precision phenomenology sanity floor). Downstream:
UQF-14 (nonperturbative-QCD unitarity inheritance via UQF-11),
UQF-15 (no-leakage audit's reliance on the §UQFC-16 EW + gravity rows
which inherit C-FF11).

**Trace 3: C-FF12 (scope-boundary) failure.** Direct UQF inheritances:
UQF-9 (UV completion), UQF-10 (compactification stability), UQF-11
(nonperturbative QCD), UQF-12 (strong CP), UQF-15 (no-leakage audit
must not use external scope to upgrade). Downstream: UQF-13 (rows
that ride on UQF-9 / UQF-10 / UQF-11 for matching-scale predictions
inherit), UQF-14 (nonperturbative-causality inheritance).

These traces illustrate that C-FF rows are not in 1-to-1 correspondence
with UQF rows; the composition rule is a many-to-many propagation
controlled by §19.3.

---

## 19.6 Explicit failure paths for §17 and §18 audit rows (recap)

The §17 unitarity/causality/locality audit and the §18 no-hidden-
force-leakage audit each carry their own per-row falsifiers (§17.5
and §18.8). For completeness, the failures of these audit sections
propagate to the §19 map as follows:

| §17/§18 falsifier | Triggering observation | Propagates to UQF row(s) | Triggering composition |
|---|---|---|---|
| §17.5 unitarity violation (neg-norm physical state) | Detection of a sector where physical states fail positivity | UQF-3 (direct), UQF-14 (inheritance) | downstream of UQF-4 / UQF-8 depending on sector |
| §17.5 causality violation (commutator nonzero outside lightcone) | Detection of superluminal signaling, tachyon, or Froissart-bound violation | UQF-5 / UQF-6 / UQF-8 / UQF-9 / UQF-10 / UQF-14 | per-sector |
| §17.5 locality violation (cluster decomposition fails) | Detection of 4D-EFT operator with non-local structure $\geq 1/M_{\rm KK}$ | UQF-2 / UQF-10 / UQF-14 | per-sector |
| §18.8 fifth-force detection | Yukawa-modified gravity at $M < M_{\rm KK}$ | UQF-15 (direct), UQF-5 / UQF-10 (inheritance) | depends on which species detected |
| §18.8 hidden $U(1)$ detection | Dark-photon at any mass | UQF-15 (direct), UQF-6 / UQF-8 (inheritance) | new $U(1)$ has no geometric origin in §5 (Paper 2) |
| §18.8 light-modulus detection | Light scalar below $M_{\rm KK}$ with EW or Higgs-portal coupling | UQF-15 (direct), UQF-8 / UQF-10 (inheritance) | §6.9.3a stabilization failure |
| §18.8 hidden-fermion detection | Sterile or hidden fermion at any mass | UQF-15 (direct), UQF-7 (inheritance) | §8.4 matter-bundle reopening |
| §18.8 massive-graviton detection | Massive spin-2 mode below $M_{\rm KK}$ | UQF-15 (direct), UQF-5 / UQF-10 (inheritance) | §6.4 mode-counting reopening |

The composition rule of §19.5 applies in each row: the direct UQF
inheritance is the first step; downstream UQF inheritance per §19.1
is the second step.

---

## 19.7 The min-rule (force-sector unified-quantum-force claim status)

The overall claim status of the paper — the unified-quantum-force-
completion claim — is set by the *minimum* over all UQF row
statuses:

$$
\Sigma(\text{UQFC}) = \min_{X \in \{0,1,\ldots,16\}} \mathrm{status}(\mathrm{UQF}\text{-}X).
$$

The status labels, in decreasing strength order:

1. **CERTIFICATE** (the row carries a frozen, named, pass/fail-criterion
   certificate within this paper, with downgrade rule and Authority
   identified).
2. **AUDIT** (the row's framework structure is closed; numerical or
   nonperturbative values are not yet populated, but the audit
   structure is in place).
3. **OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC** (the row's certificate cannot be discharged
   at this paper's tier; the open status is named and the audit's
   diagnostic content is preserved).
4. **FAILED** (the row's failure path has triggered and no §6.10
   correction-ledger entry can absorb it; this is a hard downgrade
   beyond *Open / Diagnostic*).

The min-rule states:

- If **any** UQF row is FAILED, the overall claim FAILS. The paper
  becomes "candidate at *Open / Diagnostic* for the failed sector;
  certificate at the closed sectors only."
- If **any** UQF row is OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC (but none is FAILED), the
  overall claim downgrades to "candidate unified-quantum-force-
  completion at the audit tier the weakest row admits."
- If **every** UQF row is AUDIT (none failed, none open), the overall
  claim is "framework-complete unified-quantum-force-completion
  candidate, awaiting Tier-2 numerical population per §UQFC-16.3."
- If **every** UQF row is CERTIFICATE, the overall claim is
  "certificate-complete unified-quantum-force-completion."

This is the parallel of the *C-FF mechanism in Paper 2* §13: the
unified-interface claim in Paper 2 is the min over C-FF row statuses;
the unified-quantum-force-completion claim in Paper 3 is the min over
UQF row statuses. The composition rule of §19.5 makes the two min-rules
*compose*: a C-FF row that drops below CERTIFICATE drops the
inheriting UQF row by the §19.3 map, which drops the overall UQFC
claim by the present min-rule.

### 19.7.1 Current status of the min-rule

Per the §3 status vocabulary, the current draft status of the UQF
rows is *not* CERTIFICATE for all rows. The §3 per-row status column
is the authoritative source; the §19 map does not over-write it.

What the §19 map *guarantees* is that whatever the §3 statuses are at
any given draft, the overall claim status follows from the min-rule
above and is recoverable in one step. A reviewer who finds that any
UQF row is at AUDIT or *Open / Diagnostic* immediately knows that
the overall paper's claim is at the same tier (or worse, if a
downstream UQF row is also degraded).

This is the meta-rule the paper operates under, stated at
certificate-tier.

---

The catalog below is the single-table integration of UQF and C-FF
downgrades, in the order a reviewer would encounter them when
auditing the paper. Each row lists: (i) the trigger observation /
failed claim, (ii) the C-FF row(s) directly violated, (iii) the
UQF row(s) directly violated, (iv) the downstream UQF row(s)
violated by §19.5 composition, (v) the resulting Σ(UQFC) status.

| Trigger | C-FF rows violated | UQF rows directly violated | UQF rows downstream-violated | Σ(UQFC) status |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Force section uses different parent geometry | C-FF0 | UQF-0 | every UQF row (all inherit UQF-0) | FAILED |
| Quantized object missing §4 ledger entry | C-FF1, C-FF6, C-FF7 | UQF-1 | UQF-2, UQF-3, UQF-6 | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |

| Graviton certificate fails | C-FF7 | UQF-5 | UQF-13 (gravity rows), UQF-14 (gravity-sector rows), UQF-15 (no-massive-graviton row) | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| Gauge-boson certificate fails for one sector | C-FF1, C-FF4, C-FF6, C-FF8, C-FF10 | UQF-6 | UQF-13 (affected EWPO / strong / QED rows), UQF-14 (affected sector unitarity), UQF-15 (affected hidden-state row) | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| Mirror fermion survives or wrong-statistics state | C-FF3, C-FF10 | UQF-7 | UQF-13 (CKM / PMNS / proton-decay rows), UQF-14 (matter sector), UQF-15 (no-hidden-fermion row) | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| Higgs construction fails Run-3 precision | C-FF3, C-FF8 | UQF-8 | UQF-13 (Higgs and EW rows), UQF-14 (long-$W,Z$ unitarity row), UQF-15 (no-light-modulus row) | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| UV-completion route fails | C-FF9, C-FF12 | UQF-9 | UQF-14 (nonperturbative-causality row), UQF-10 (infinite-KK limit) | AUDIT (UV-completion is widely open; not unique to 13D) |

| Nonperturbative QCD certificate fails | C-FF11, C-FF12 | UQF-11 | UQF-13 (hadronic-spectrum, HVP), UQF-14 (nonperturbative-unitarity row) | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| Strong-CP candidate fails nEDM | C-FF12 | UQF-12 | UQF-13 (nEDM row) | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| Precision row falsifies at $\geq 3\sigma$ | C-FF11, C-FF14 | UQF-13 (affected row only) | sector-dependent: UQF-5/6/7/8/11/12 if the row's UQF inheritance also fails | AUDIT (row-level) |
| Unitarity / causality / locality audit fails | C-FF14 | UQF-14 | UQF-3, UQF-4, UQF-5, UQF-6, UQF-8, UQF-9, UQF-10, UQF-11 depending on which audit row fails | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| Hidden-sector force-leakage detection | C-FF5, C-FF8, C-FF12 | UQF-15 | UQF-5 / UQF-6 / UQF-7 / UQF-8 / UQF-10 depending on which species detected | OPEN / DIAGNOSTIC |
| Downgrade map has unhandled failure | C-FF14 | UQF-16 | every UQF row (the meta-rule is incomplete) | AUDIT |

The catalog is *complete* relative to the gate-stack triggers
enumerated in §§4–18. A reviewer who finds any failure can trace it
through this table to the Σ(UQFC) status in one step.

---

## 19.9 Honest framing: where this map cannot help

The §19 map *names* failure paths and their consequences; it does
not *predict* whether any particular failure will occur. Three honest
clarifications:

- **The map is conditional.** Every row of the §19.1 and §19.8 tables
  is of the form "if X fails, Y downgrades." The map says nothing
  about whether X actually fails. The closure status of any UQF row
  is the content of that row's own section.
- **The map is post-failure.** Once a failure has been observed (per
  a §17 or §18 audit row, or per a §UQFC-16 precision row), the map
  routes the downgrade through the §19.1 / §19.8 tables to the
  Σ(UQFC) status. The map does *not* tell you whether the failure
  is real or whether it can be absorbed by a §6.10 correction-ledger
  entry; those are upstream determinations made by the relevant
  audit section.
- **The map is force-sector-only.** Per the hard claim boundary of
  UQFC-1, the §19 map covers force-sector failures. Cosmology, dark
  sector, baryogenesis, initial conditions, measurement problem, and
  "why this universe" failures route to Paper 4's downgrade map (which
  is not the present map). The BG-10 *Open / Diagnostic* status is
  inherited *without modification* by the §19 map; it does not enter
  the force-sector min-rule of §19.7 because BG-10 is Paper-4
  material per the hierarchy.

This is the honest scope of the meta-rule, stated at certificate-tier
for the map's *structure* and not for the per-row physics content.

---

  downgrade rules are the inheritance pathway for the UQF-13 row of
  §19.1. The most-consequential precision row (proton stability) and
  most-tense current row ($m_W$) are named in §UQFC-16.4 and inherit
  here.

  falsifiers propagate to §19 per §19.6.

  falsifiers propagate to §19 per §19.6.

  interface).** The C-FF backbone is recapitulated in §19.2 without
  modification; the composition rule of §19.5 propagates Paper 2
  failures to Paper 3's UQF rows per §19.3.

  definitions used in §19.2–§19.5.
- **Paper 2 C-FF12 (scope-boundary).** The §19 map respects C-FF12:
  the §19.5 composition uses C-FF12 to mark UQF rows (UQF-9, UQF-10,
  UQF-11, UQF-12, UQF-15) that carry scope-boundary risk.

  §19.1 has a stated failure path, satisfying C-FF14 inheritance

  Article A: the UQF-7 row inherits Article-A nine-parameter discipline,
  and the §UQFC-16 CKM / PMNS rows that ride on it.
- **Article B §8.2 (Jarlskog HC-1 anchor).** The §19 map respects
  Article B: the UQF-13 Jarlskog row's HC-1 status is preserved.
- **Main GUT manuscript Appendix K (neutrino sector).** The §19 map
  inherits the Appendix-K conditional on the UQF-7 row's PMNS Majorana
  extension.
- **Main GUT manuscript BG-10:** *Open / Diagnostic*. Preserved.
  BG-10 does not enter the force-sector min-rule of §19.7; it remains
  Paper-4 material per the hierarchy. The §19 map does not litigate
  BG-10.
- **Main GUT manuscript hard-gate vector**
  $\mathsf{D}, \mathsf{D}\text{-local}, \mathsf{D}, \mathsf{D}, \mathsf{D}$:
  preserved. The §19 map does not modify the hard-gate vector; it is
  a meta-rule for the UQF stack, not a re-derivation of the hard-gate
  status.
